1401 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Tovar v. State


No. 05-83-00881-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


685 S.W.2d 707; 1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 6978



November 16, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM A DISTRICT COURT OF DALLAS COUNTY, TEXAS


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his conviction for attempted murder imposed by the District Court of Dallas County (Texas). He contended that the trial court erred by admitting into evidence a penitentiary packet as proof of a prior theft conviction because the theft statute, Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 31.03 (1974), was unconstitutionally vague and ambiguous rendering the conviction void.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of attempted murder, and punishment was enhanced. Defendant asserted that the trial court erred by admitting into evidence a penitentiary packet as proof of a prior theft conviction, because the theft statute, Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 31.03 (1974), had become unconstitutionally vague and ambiguous rendering the conviction void. The court affirmed the judgment of conviction, finding that § 31.03 was neither vague nor ambiguous, and that the penitentiary packet was properly admitted into evidence. The statute was presumed to be valid, and defendant was required to prove beyond a reasonable doubt that it was unconstitutionally vague. The negation of effective consent was illustrated four alternative ways in § 31.01(4). Considering that the allegedly vague and ambiguous language had four expressed statutory definitions, the court held that the presumption of validity had not been overcome beyond a reasonable doubt even though the statutory definitions were not exhaustive.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment of conviction, finding that the trial court properly admitted into evidence a penitentiary packet as proof of a prior theft conviction and rejecting defendant's contention that the theft statute was unconstitutionally vague and ambiguous rendering the theft conviction void.

 

1402 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Benavides v. State


No. 01-82-0162-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


680 S.W.2d 899; 1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 6998



November 8, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 183rd District Court of Harris County, Texas Trial Court Cause No. 342,550.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his conviction by the 183rd District Court of Harris County (Texas), pursuant to a plea of guilty to possession of marijuana in a quantity of more than 5 pounds but less than 50 pounds in violation of Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15, § 4.051(b)(4).


OVERVIEW: Defendant pleaded guilty to possession of more than 5 but less than 50 pounds of marijuana. Defendant sought review, and the court affirmed. Defendant filed a petition for discretionary review, which was granted, and the case was remanded to the court for reconsideration. The court affirmed, holding that the declaration that an amendment to the Controlled Substances Act was invalid did not remove the conduct of possessing marijuana from criminal penalties. Although the amendment to the act was declared unconstitutional, the act was still valid under Tex. Const. art. III, § 35. Therefore, possession of marijuana was still a criminal offense. Finally, the court held that defendant failed to show that he was harmed by any erroneous admonition by the court prior to the entry of his guilty plea.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction for possession of marijuana, holding that defendant knowingly possessed a usable quantity of marijuana, which was a criminal offense, and that defendant did not show that he was harmed by any erroneous admonition by the court prior to his guilty plea.

 

1403 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Plano Independent School Dist. v. Oake


No. 05-83-01388-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


682 S.W.2d 359; 1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 6806



November 2, 1984 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied December 6, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: From a District Court of Collin County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, Plano Independent School District, its acting tax collector, the tax collector of Collin County Central Appraisal District, and Collin County, challenged a judgment of a District Court, Collin County, Texas, granting summary judgment to appellee property owner, permanently enjoining them from assessing or collecting taxes on appellee's property until the boundary between Dallas and Collin Counties was established by law.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, Plano Independent School District, its acting tax collector, and the tax collector of Collin County Central Appraisal District, failed to file appeal bonds as required by Tex. R. Civ. P. 354 (1983). On appeal, the court dismissed their appeals because the court did not have jurisdiction as a result of their failure to file appeal bonds. The court held that an appeal bond was not required of appellant Collin County under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann., art. 279a (1973) and Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 2276 (1971). The court reversed the judgment in favor of appellee property owner granting an injunction against appellant Collin County because appellee failed to present summary judgment evidence to discharge his burden establishing that the property sought to be assessed and taxed did not lie within the boundaries of appellant Collin County.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the appeals filed by appellants, Plano Independent School District, its acting tax collector, and the chief of the Collin County Central Appraisal District, due to lack of jurisdiction. The court reversed the judgment against appellant Collin County and vacated and set aside the permanent injunction enjoining it from assessing or collecting taxes on appellee property owner's property and remanded the cause for trial.

 

1404 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


ABURTO v. STATE


No. 01-84-0291-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 6624



November 1, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] On Appeal from the County Criminal Court of Law No. 7 of Harris County, Texas Trial Court Cause No. 752,077


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the County Criminal Court of Law No. 7, Harris County, Texas, which convicted him of promoting an obscene device within the meaning of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 43.21(a)(7), in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. §43.21(c)(1).


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that Tex. Penal Code Ann. §§ 43.21(a)(7) and 43.23(c)(1) were unconstitutional on their face and as applied to his case. He also challenged the inconsistency of the information under which he was charged, which referred to the obscene device in the singular and the plural. On appeal, the court affirmed defendant's conviction and held that §§ 43.21(a)(7) and 43.23(c)(1), which were part of the Texas Obscenity Statute, were constitutional. The court rejected the argument that the statutes invaded defendant's right to privacy, noting that defendant was not charged with possessing an obscene device within the confines of his home, but was charged with the offense of promotion of an obscene device. The court found that while it would have been better to phrase the information consistently singular or consistently plural, the court did not find that this harmed defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment convicting defendant of promoting an obscene device because the sections of the Texas Obscenity Statute under which defendant was convicted were constitutional.

 

1405 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Ex parte Stacey


No. 05-84-00369-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


682 S.W.2d 348; 1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 7025



October 31, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From a District Court of Dallas County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment of a District Court, Dallas County (Texas), which denied his application for writ of habeas corpus and remanded him for extradition to another state, in an action involving a habeas corpus hearing before a magistrate and sufficiency of evidence in sustaining the judgment of extradition.


OVERVIEW: Appellant contended that because the trial judge did not enter a referral order, his habeas corpus hearing was improperly held before a magistrate, and that the evidence was insufficient to sustain a judgment of extradition. The court affirmed the judgment, holding that although the record contained a transcription of a "writ of habeas corpus" hearing held before a magistrate, the trial court judgment unequivocally stated that the trial judge heard the evidence and that he was of the opinion that appellant was legally held in custody; absent evidence in rebuttal, the court could not infer otherwise. The court could not address appellant's arguments that the magistrate lacked jurisdiction to hear the writ and that there was no referral order. The court further held that the record contained a governor's warrant that was regular on its face, thus under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 51.13 § 3 (1979), the warrant alone became prima facie evidence authorizing extradition; no defensive theory was placed in issue.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment which denied appellant's writ of habeas corpus and which remanded him for extradition, because there was a presumption that the trial judge heard evidence pertaining to the extradition and the presumption was not rebutted, even though the magistrate also conducted a hearing. The evidence was sufficient, because the governor's warrant, regular on its face, was prima facie evidence authorizing extradition.

 

1406 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Collins v. El Campo


No. 13-83-528-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Thirteenth District, Corpus Christi


684 S.W.2d 756; 1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 6566



October 25, 1984 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied November 20, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the 23rd District Court of Wharton County, Texas.



DISPOSITION:  We REVERSE the judgment of the trial court and order that the permanent injunction be dissolved.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant subdivision homeowners sought review of the judgment entered the 23rd District Court of Wharton County, Texas in favor of appellee city, which permanently enjoined as a violation of a zoning ordinance and a restrictive covenant, the use of appellant's property as a residence for four unrelated, mentally retarded men and their supervising houseparents, and which awarded special damages and attorney's fees to appellee.


OVERVIEW: Four unrelated, mentally retarded men, along with their two supervising houseparents, moved into a subdivision house that the evidence indicated was a permanent living arrangement. Appellee city filed suit against appellant subdivision homeowner seeking to permanently enjoin appellants from using the property as a group home, as such use allegedly violated residential covenants and city zoning ordinances. The court concluded that the property was a "single-family dwelling" similar to other structures in the same neighborhood; that the property was used as a single-family residence in accordance with the manifest purpose and the clear intention of the zoning ordinance; and that the occupants met the definition of a "family" since there was no requirement that the parties occupying a dwelling and living as a "single housekeeping unit" be related by blood or marriage. While the home may be properly called a "group home," the court held that it was clear that the home did not qualify as a boarding house, lodging house, or hotel as defined and prohibited in the zoning ordinance.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and order that the permanent injunction be dissolved, concluding that the trial court's findings that the use of appellants' property violated both the zoning ordinance and the restrictive covenant were improper bases for the permanent injunction, since the dwelling was used as a "single-family" residence and the occupants met the definition of a "family."

 

1407 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Trahan v. Trahan


No. 14,145


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


682 S.W.2d 332; 1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 6831



October 24, 1984 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied December 19, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the District Court of Travis County, 200TH Judicial District No. 344,539, Honorable Charles D. Mathews, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant former husband sought review of the judgment from the 200th Judicial District Court of Travis County (Texas) in which appellee former wife, in her suit against appellant for partition of his military retirement benefits, was awarded a percentage of appellant's retirement benefits.


OVERVIEW: Appellant former husband and appellant former wife had been married and divorced twice. The parties were married 187 months of the 240 months appellant was in the military. Neither divorce decree awarded appellee any interest in appellant's retirement benefits. Appellee had filed a previous partition suit, and the trial court had awarded her an interest in the benefits. However, the decision was reversed by the Texas Supreme Court, and it was ordered that appellee take nothing. Appellee filed suit again seeking to partition appellant's retirement benefits in light of the Uniformed Services Former Spouses' Protection Act (Act), 10 U.S.C.S. § 1408. The lower court ordered a partition of appellant's benefits, and he challenged, arguing that appellee's action was barred by res judicata. The court disagreed and affirmed the lower court's judgment. Initially, the court found that the Act was properly applied to the case. Further, the doctrine of res judicata did not apply in the case because applying the doctrine of res judicata would subvert the intent and the plain meaning of the Act. The judgment was not an unconstitutional garnishment of appellant's wages.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's judgment awarding appellee former wife a percentage of appellant former husband's military retirement benefits because the doctrine of res judicata did not apply to the facts of the case.

 

1408 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


FRIEDEN v. WRIGHT


No. 01-84-0307-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 6483



October 18, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] On Appeal from the Probate Court No. 3 of Harris County, Texas Trial Court Cause No. 188,455-002


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant contestant challenged a judgment from the Probate Court No. 3 of Harris County (Texas), which had appointed a temporary guardian of a ward. Appellee temporary guardian moved to dismiss the appeal because of mootness.


OVERVIEW: Appellee guardian was appointed as temporary guardian of the estate of a ward. Appellant contestant sought to set aside appellee's appointment and challenged the constitutionality of Tex. Prob. Code Ann. §§ 131 and 133 (1980). Appellee moved to dismiss the appeal for mootness, and the court granted the motion. The court noted that the trial court had approved the closing of the temporary guardianship and had appointed another as limited guardian over the ward's estate. The ward had given appellee a full release with respect to claims concerning her estate or assets. Thus, the court held that the controversy between the parties had ceased to exist, and there was no longer a justiciable controversy that would have authorized a declaratory judgment. Additionally, it was unnecessary to decide whether the challenged sections were unconstitutional as a basis for relief sought by appellant, and any opinion would merely have been an advisory opinion, which the court was not authorized to issue.


OUTCOME: The court granted appellee guardian's motion to dismiss appellant contestant's appeal. The court held that the parties' controversy no longer existed and that the court was not authorized to issue an advisory opinion.

 

1409 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Werner v. State


No. 01-83-0069-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


680 S.W.2d 858; 1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 6381



October 4, 1984 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied November 21, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 228th District Court of Harris County, Texas Trial Court Cause Number 371,591.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, whose parents were Holocaust victims, sought review of a judgment of the 228th District Court of Harris County (Texas), which convicted appellant of murdering an individual he "arrested" for damaging a friend's car.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, convicted of murdering an individual who damaged a friend's car, argued trial court error in charging the jury on the use of deadly force to make an arrest. The court disagreed, noting first that appellant shot the victim after he made a threatening movement when appellant told him to "get up against the car." Explaining, the court ruled that the instruction properly reflected appellant's theories of defense, that force was justified in effecting an arrest and that he acted in self defense. No error occurred when evidence related to appellant's then state of mind was excluded. Although Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 19.06 (1974) allowed for testimony on state of mind, testimony as to effect of being related to a Holocaust survivor had upon his belief of being in danger was irrelevant to the issue of self defense. A new trial was not required despite evidence of jury misconduct in discussing parole law; no showing was made that the jurors relied on a misstatement of the law to increase the punishment; nor did a mistrial need to be declared when the trial court's instruction to disregard followed improper jury argument by the prosecutor on early termination of probation.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed convicting appellant of murder, because testimony as to his state of mind -- a belief stemming from being a Holocaust descendant of then being in danger -- was irrelevant to the issue of self defense when attempting to effect an arrest, as jury instructions properly reflected appellant's theories of defense, and as a new trial was not required for jury misconduct when jury did not rely on a juror's misstatement of parole law.

 

1410 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Danner v. Watauga


No. 02-84-048-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Second District, Fort Worth


676 S.W.2d 721; 1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 6392



October 4, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From the 348th District Court of Tarrant County Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relators, state and property owners, sought review of a grant of summary judgment in favor of appellee city from the District Court of Tarrant County (Texas) in their action to enjoin appellee from collecting taxes on annexed property. Relators asserted that the validation statute, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 974d-28, was unconstitutionally retroactive and a denial of the due process of law.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed a grant of summary judgment in favor of appellee city in a quo warranto proceeding brought by relators, state and property owners, that sought to enjoin appellee from the collection of taxes upon property annexed by appellee. The court held that the validation statute, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 974d-28, which validated original boundary lines of an incorporated municipality, or any extensions of those boundaries adopted prior to January 1, 1975, even if those actions were not in accordance with the law, was constitutional. The court stated that the legislature was free to validate any act that it had the power to authorize initially. The court rejected relators' argument that the statute was unconstitutionally retroactive because a property owner was afforded no constitutional right regarding the location or existence of municipalities. The court rejected relators' argument that the statute was a denial of due process because the constitutional inhibition against taking private property for public use without compensation had reference solely to the exercise of the right of eminent domain and not to taxation for public use.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment in favor of appellee. The court held that the validation statute was constitutional when the legislature had the power to ratify any act that it could have authorized. The court found there was no constitutional right regarding the location of municipalities or constitutional prohibition against the taxation of property for public use.

 

1411 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


DAILY v. WHEAT


No. A14-82-112CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


681 S.W.2d 747; 1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 6402



October 4, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Probate Court No. One of Harris County, Texas Trial Court No. 165, 423.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant contestant, the testatrix's daughter, sought review of a judgment from Probate Court No. One, Harris County (Texas) which admitted a will and codicil to probate following a jury finding that the instruments were not a result of undue influence on the part of appellee proponent, the testatrix's attorney and financial adviser.


OVERVIEW: Appellee proponent received a direct bequest under the will and codicil of an elderly testatrix for whom he had long served as attorney and financial advisor. The testatrix also left 90 percent of the residual estate to charity, with appellee as trustee. Appellant contestant, the testatrix's only child, brought an action alleging that appellee had exercised undue influence. The jury found that the testatrix was of sound mind when the will and codicil were executed and that the instruments were not the result of undue influence. The trial court entered judgment on the verdict admitting the will and codicil to probate. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that the existence of a fiduciary relationship between appellee and the testatrix did not, in and of itself, give rise to a presumption of undue influence or place upon appellee the burden of establishing the fairness of the transaction. Whatever the testatrix's reasons may have been, the court concluded, the record supported the belief that her bequests to charities and to appellee rather than appellant were her deliberate decisions.


OUTCOME: Finding sufficient evidence to support the jury's finding that the testatrix's will and codicil were not the product of undue influence on the part of appellee proponent, the court affirmed the judgment of the trial court admitting the instruments to probate.

 

1412 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


ETHEREDGE v. STATE


Nos. D14-83-339-CR, D14-83-340-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 6413



October 4, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Appeal from the 262nd District Court of Harris County Cause Nos. 361,895 and 361,858


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment from the 262nd District Court of Harris County (Texas) that convicted him of possession with intent to deliver a controlled substance, methamphetamine, a violation of Controlled Substances Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15, § 4.03, and of theft, a violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 31.03. Appellant contended that his guilty pleas were not voluntary and contested the validity of the possession charge.


OVERVIEW: Appellant pled guilty to possession with intent to deliver a controlled substance, methamphetamine, a violation of the Controlled Substances Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15 § 4.03, and pled nolo contendere to theft, a violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 31.03. The court affirmed the judgment that convicted appellant of both offenses and remanded the possession case for resentencing. The court declared that the facts alleged and proved established the possession offense. Appellant's guilty plea to possession was voluntary because the district court correctly overruled appellant's motion to quash this indictment when his offense violated the Act, which applied despite its unconstitutional amendment. The court found that the plea bargain for possession and theft did not lack consideration because the range of punishment exceeded the recommended term. The court determined that appellant's plea to possession constituted an express waiver of any error, which rendered moot the issue of whether he preserved for review his pretrial motion to suppress the methamphetamine. The district court did not abuse its discretion by denying appellant's motion to set aside his pleas.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that convicted appellant of possession with intent to deliver a controlled substance, methamphetamine, and of theft. The court remanded the possession case for resentencing. Appellant's guilty plea to possession was voluntary because the district court properly overruled his motion to quash the indictment when his offense violated the statute, despite its unconstitutional amendment, and hence the charge was valid.

 

1413 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Stuart v. Tarrant County Child Welfare Unit


No. 2-84-102-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Second District, Fort Worth


677 S.W.2d 273; 1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 6354



September 27, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From the 323rd District Court of Tarrant County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant parents sought review of an order by 323rd District Court, Tarrant County, Texas, which terminated their parental rights after termination proceedings were instituted by appellee Texas Department of Human Resources pursuant to Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 15.02.


OVERVIEW: Appellee Texas Department of Human Resources instituted an action against appellant parents to terminate their parental rights over their minor child pursuant to Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 15.02. After making several findings, the trial court entered a decree of termination. Appellants challenged the sufficiency of the evidence upon which the decree was based. Upon appeal, the court affirmed the judgment. The court held that evidence that appellants abused the child's deceased sibling in the child's presence was clear and convincing evidence that appellants engaged in conduct that was dangerous to the child's physical and emotional well being, pursuant to Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 15.02(1)(E). The court held that the Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 15.02(1) termination requirement was satisfied under § 15.02(1)(E) and therefore the trial court did not err in determining that termination of the parent-child relationship was in the child's best interest.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decree terminating the parental rights of appellant parents in termination proceedings instituted by appellee Texas Department of Human Resources. The court held that evidence of appellants' abuse of the child's sibling in his presence was clear and convincing evidence that appellants engaged in conduct dangerous to the child's emotional and physical well being. Therefore, termination was in the best interests of the child.

 

1414 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Garland by Mayor & City Council v. Louton


No. 05-84-00036-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


683 S.W.2d 725; 1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 6925



September 21, 1984 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied January 2, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM A DISTRICT COURT OF DALLAS COUNTY, TEXAS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellees moved to dismiss an appeal of a judgment from the District Court of Dallas County (Texas), granting a writ of mandate directing appellant city to hold an election on the issue of firefighter pay raises and refusing to grant appellant city's request for declaratory relief.


OVERVIEW: Appellees, a fireman and the local professional firefighters association, brought a petition for a writ of mandamus to direct appellant city to hold an election on the issue of firefighter pay raises pursuant to Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 1269q. Appellant counterclaimed for declaratory relief, alleging that article 1269q was unconstitutional. The trial court granted the writ of mandamus and dismissed the request for declaratory relief. Appellant held election, but sought appellate review. Appellees moved to dismiss the appeal on the grounds of mootness. The court granted the motion, holding that there was no longer any actual controversy between the parties on the date of submission to the court.The court further held that because appellant failed to serve the attorney general with the action for declaratory relief as mandated by Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 2524-1, § 11, the trial court lacked jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The court granted appellees' motion to dismiss the appeal, holding that because appellant city carried out the election ordered by the trial court in the writ of mandamus, the appeal was moot. The court further held that because appellant failed to serve the attorney general with its request for declaratory relief, the trial court properly dismissed the complaint for lack of jurisdiction.

 

1415 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


ADAMS v. STATE


No. 01-83-00385-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 6212



September 13, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] On Appeal from the 184th District Court of Harris County, Texas Trial Court cause No. 362,355


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the order of the 184th District Court of Harris County (Texas), which convicted him of delivering methamphetamine and sentenced him to confinement and a fine. Defendant contended that his sentence was illegal because the statute under which he had been sentenced was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of delivering methamphetamine and was sentenced to confinement and a fine under a sentencing statute that was later held to be unconstitutional. The court sustained defendant's claim that the sentence was improper and remanded the matter to the trial court for resentencing. The statutory amendment under which he was sentenced was held to be unconstitutional, thus restoring the original statute to effect. Under that statute, defendant's sentence would have been different, and he would not have been fined. The court held that it could not reform a sentence that was void at its inception. The court overruled defendant's other claims of error, finding the hearsay testimony of extraneous offenses was properly admitted as part of the res gestae of the offense. Further, he had not preserved other evidentiary arguments for appeal, nor had he shown that the admissions were prejudicial to him. The court held that his counsel had effectively represented him, noting that counsel made an objection to testimony on defendant's extraneous offense which was properly overruled.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the cause to the trial court to resentence defendant under the statute that was in effect before an amendment to the statute, under which defendant was sentenced, was found to be unconstitutional and therefore void. The court could not reform a sentence that had been rendered under a void statute.

 

1416 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


SANDERS v. STATE


No. 01-81-0276-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 6214



September 13, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 7 of Harris County, Texas Trial Court Cause No. 595,217


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 7 of Harris County, Texas, convicting him of exhibiting obscene material in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 43.23 (Supp. 1984).


OVERVIEW: Appellant, the projectionist at an adult movie theater, was convicted of exhibiting obscene material in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 43.23. Section 43.23(e) contains a presumption that a person who promoted obscene material in the course of his business was presumed to do so with knowledge of its content and character. That section has been found unconstitutional. Nevertheless, the trial court instructed the jury that it could find appellant guilty solely by applying the presumption contained in § 43.23(e).On appeal, the court reversed the judgment, holding that where the promoted material, a film, was presumptively protected by the United States or Texas Constitutions and the trial court erroneously instructed the jury that it could apply the unconstitutional presumption, reversible error occurred.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded the case for a new trial, holding that because the promoted material was presumptively protected by the United States or Texas Constitutions, the trial court erred in instructing the jury that it could find the appellant guilty solely by applying the presumption that a person who promoted obscene material in the course of his business was presumed to do so with knowledge of its content and character.

 

1417 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Public Utility Com. v. Pedernales Electric Cooperative, Inc.


No. 14,024


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


678 S.W.2d 214; 1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 6536



September 12, 1984 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied October 24, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the District Court of Travis County, 147th Judicial District No. 349,050, Honorable Charles D. Mathews, Judge Presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant utility commission sought review of the decision from the District Court of Travis County, 147th District (Texas), which granted an injunction pendite lite on the application of appellee utility company in its suit against appellant seeking permanent and injunctive relief related to utility rates charged by appellee.


OVERVIEW: Appellee utility company's rates had not been fixed by any action of appellant utility commission. After an inquiry into its billing practices, an order required appellee to make changes. Appellee filed a motion that appellant, under authority of Public Utility Regulation Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 1446c, § 43(d), could have established temporary rates. The examiner concluded that appellee failed to make a prima facie case to justify those rates. Review of that decision was sustained. Appellee filed a lawsuit in the district court and alleged that the residuum of its rates, permitted to be charged after the requisite changes in its billing practices, were unconstitutional and confiscatory. The district court granted appellee's request for an injunction pendente lite. The court reversed the injunction order and dissolved the injunction pendite lite because any loss sustained by appellee was properly considered not as a violation of appellee's constitutional rights, but as a necessary incident of rate regulation. The court held that injury claimed by appellee did not justify judicial subordination of the purposes underlying the exhaustion doctrine.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the injunction order and dissolved the injunction pendite lite because the trial court abused its discretion as any loss sustained by appellee utility company was properly considered not as a violation of its constitutional rights, but as a necessary incident of rate regulation. The court held that injury claimed by appellee did not justify judicial subordination of the purposes underlying the exhaustion doctrine.

 

1418 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


RepublicBank Dallas, N.A. v. Interkal, Inc.


No. 05-83-00794-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


677 S.W.2d 759; 1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 6466



September 7, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From a District Court of Dallas County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant non-beneficiary bank challenged the grant of summary judgment from a district court of Dallas County, Texas, which granted judgment to appellee beneficiary-materialman in an action to recover money declared to be trust funds under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 5472e, § 1.


OVERVIEW: A contractor entered a security agreement on its accounts receivable in order to obtain promissory notes from appellant non-beneficiary bank. The contractor ordered materials from appellee beneficiary-materialman. The property owners partially paid, and the trial court entered an injunction ordering that the checks be placed in an escrow account with appellant. Appellant and appellee entered into a dispute about which party was entitled to the money. The trial court granted summary judgment to appellee, and the court of appeals affirmed. The court held that Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 5472e, § 4 did not operate to terminate a trust created by Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 5472e, § 1 when appellant claimed a non-beneficiary interest in money declared to be a trust fund in accordance with art. 5472e, § 1. Art. 5472e, § 4 specifically stated that the mechanics' lien statute did not apply to banks. Art. 5472e, § 4 was intended to protect lenders and title companies from criminal charges. The money became impressed with a trust status, and it could not be available to pay appellant for the contractor's loans.


OUTCOME: Summary judgment in favor of appellee beneficiary-materialman affirmed in an action between appellee and appellant non-beneficiary bank to recover funds placed in a trust account by the contractor. The mechanics' lien statute applied to contracts for construction, not banks which lended money to contractors. The money became impressed with a trust status which could not be used to pay the contractor's loans from appellant.

 

1419 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Leal v. Ford Motor Credit Co.


No. 13-83-003-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Thirteenth District, Corpus Christi


683 S.W.2d 719; 1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 6159



August 31, 1984 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied November 1, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from County Court at Law No. 3 of Nueces County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant consumer challenged the judgment from the County Court at Law No. 3 of Nueces County (Texas), in favor of appellee credit company on appellant's claim that appellee violated the Texas Consumer Credit Code, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 5069-7.01, et seq. (1984). Appellant attacked certain provisions of a form installment contract that he had signed in connection with his purchase of a vehicle.


OVERVIEW: Appellee credit company was the assignee of an installment contract for the appellant's purchase of a car. The contract was performed in accordance with its terms. Appellant alleged that the installment contract contained technical violations of the Texas Consumer Credit Code, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 5069-7.01, et seq. (1984), and filed an action against appellee. The trial court found that there were no violations of the statute, and the appellate court affirmed. The court noted that many of appellant's points of error had already been disposed of in prior decisions of the Texas Supreme Court and intermediate appellate courts. For example, appellant attacked a notice sent by appellee to correct a contract provision that had been ruled objectionable, because it was made pursuant to a statute that appellant asserted was unconstitutional. The court pointed out that the Texas Supreme Court had already rejected such a challenge to the underlying statute. The court rejected appellant's claim that the installment contract's insurance requirement was not clear and conspicuous, because the court found it to be both.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the judgment for appellee credit company. The court noted that most of appellant's attacks on the form installment credit contract had already been the subject of a series of court decisions, and had been rejected. As for appellant's other points of error, the court found sufficient evidence in the record to support the trial court's findings.

 

1420 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Garza v. State


No. 04-81-00162-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourth District, San Antonio


678 S.W.2d 183; 1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 6453



August 31, 1984 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied September 28, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 216th District Court of Kendall County Trial Court No. 2117 Honorable Robert R. Barton, Judge Presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant accused sought review of the decision from the 216th Court of Kendall County Trial Court (Texas), which convicted him of burglary of a habitation and sentenced him to 75 years' imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: There had been several burglaries in a subdivision. Police officer had been told appellant was responsible for the burglaries. Police officer saw a vehicle which matched the description of appellant's car and bore the license number of his car. Appellant accused was stopped, questioned, and arrested. A search of appellant's car revealed a number of items taken in recent burglaries. Witness told officials that six days before the arrest, he had been with appellant when appellant emerged from a mobile home carrying a television set and some guns. The lower court convicted appellant of burglary of a habitation. The court reversed and remanded the lower court's conviction of appellant because the unconstitutional intrusion could not have been justified retroactively by the evidence uncovered as a result of the intrusion on appellant's constitutional rights. Such vague and meager information could not have, merely by being relayed to the officer, be converted into "articulable facts" sufficient to justify the stop of appellant. Thus, the stop, detention, and arrest of appellant was in violation of appellant's rights under U.S. Const. amend. IV and the Texas constitution.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the lower court's conviction of appellant accused for burglary of a habitation because the unconstitutional intrusion could not have been justified retroactively by the evidence uncovered as a result of the intrusion on appellant's Fourth Amendment rights.

 

1421 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


ORLANDO GONZALES v. STATE


No. 01-82-0035-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 6073



August 30, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 3 of Harris County, Texas Trial Court Cause No. 631,035


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a decision from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 3 of Harris County (Texas) that convicted him of promotion of obscenity and assessed punishment at 10 days' confinement.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of promotion of obscenity for selling an obscene magazine and was assessed a punishment of 10 days' confinement. Upon review, appellant argued that the evidence was insufficient to establish that he knew the content and character of the material because state relied upon the presumption contained in Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 43.23 (1984). Under that section, a person commits the offense if, knowing the contents and character, he promotes or possesses with intent to promote any obscene material. The presumption provided that a person who promoted obscene material was presumed to do so with knowledge of its content and character. That presumption was declared unconstitutional. In the trial court, appellant stipulated that he intentionally sold the magazine in the county in which he was charged. The court held that state requested the trial court to consider the evidence along with the statutory presumption, but state could not rely on the presumption to prove its case. As such, the judgment was reversed, and the cause remanded for a new trial void of the presumption.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court that found appellant guilty of promotion of obscenity and remanded the cause for a new trial because state requested the trial court use a presumption in determining guilt that had previously been found to be unconstitutional.

 

1422 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Juarez v. State


No. 01-82-0950-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


677 S.W.2d 285; 1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 6091



 August 30, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 10th Judicial District Court of Galveston County, Texas Trial Court Cause No. 38,423.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the decision of the 10th Judicial District Court of Galveston County, Texas, which convicted appellant of possession of a controlled substance, cocaine, with intent to deliver and assessed punishment at 25 years' in confinement.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of possession of a controlled substance, cocaine, with intent to deliver. Appellant argued error in the indictment and charge to jury, ineffective assistance of counsel and claimed that the Controlled Substances Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15, § 4.03 was unconstitutional. The court affirmed and held that the amendments to art. 4476-15 were declared unconstitutional, and, therefore, the act remained in full force even where there was no savings clause. The court held that the trial court conducted the trial under the pre-amended version of art. 4476-15 and that its charge to the jury did not contain any reference to the weight of controlled substance as was required by the amendment. The court held that appellants allegation that there was fundamental variance between the indictment and charge without specifically stating what the variance was, provided nothing for the court to review. The court held that appellant knowingly and voluntarily waived any conflict of interest of representation of both appellant and co-defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction of possession of a controlled substance, cocaine, with intent to deliver because the trial court properly applied the pre-amended version of the Controlled Substances Act. The court held that appellant waived any conflict of interest when he was made aware of the conflict, realized the consequences of continuing with counsel and was aware of his right to obtain other counsel.

 

1423 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


MCINNIS v. STATE


No. 01-81-0274-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 6094



August 30, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 7 of Harris County, Texas Trial Court Cause No. 595,218


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his conviction in the trial court for commercial obscenity. The appellate court reversed and remanded for a new trial. The Texas Court of Criminal Appeals granted state's petition for discretionary review, reversed, and remanded to the appellate court for a determination of the remaining points of error.


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged his conviction for commercial obscenity. Appellant was an employee at an adult theater, which displayed a sexually explicit film. The appellate court reversed and remanded for a new trial, holding that the affidavits for a search warrant and an arrest warrant were invalid and that the admission into evidence of a certain photograph was error. The court of criminal appeals granted the state's petition for review and reversed the holdings of the appellate court. The case was remanded to the appellate court to decide appellant's remaining grounds of error and the appellate court again reversed and remanded for a new trial. The appellate court initially concluded that the material at issue, the film, was protected under U.S. Const. amend. I. The appellate court then held that the trial court committed reversible error by instructing the jury that appellant's knowledge of the content of the promoted material could be presumed under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 43.23(e). An acquittal was not warranted because the evidence was sufficient to establish guilt. Also, a film constituted "material" within Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 43.21(a)(3).


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed appellant's conviction for commercial obscenity and remanded for a new trial because the material at issue, a sexually explicit film was protected by the First Amendment, and the trial court's committed reversible error when it charged the jury that it could presume that appellant had knowledge of the content of the material. The evidence was sufficient to establish guilt and an acquittal was not required.

 

1424 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


GRAVES v. STATE


No. 01-83-0694-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 6097



August 30, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Appeal from the 262nd District Court of Harris County, Texas Trial Court Cause Number 379,408


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction in the 262nd District Court of Harris County (Texas) for the offense of injury to a child under the age of 14 years and his sentence to 15 years' confinement.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of injuring his live-in girlfriend's 17 month-old child. He had confessed to causing a number of injuries to the child, including bite marks, burns from a hot fork, and bruises. He also admitted shaking and shoving the child. He was convicted of injury to a child under the age of 14 years. The court affirmed because appellant's admission of roughly shaking the child and the medical testimony that the cause of death was a shaking syndrome were sufficient to sustain the jury's finding of guilt of causing serious bodily injury by shaking. The court held that appellant's own testimony and the jury's own common experience as to the heat of cooking utensils used for frying foods were sufficient for the jury to conclude that appellant's exculpatory assertion, that he did not know the fork was hot, was false. The court held that, even if there had been insufficient evidence to convict appellant under each of the theories charged by the trial court, that insufficiency would not render the evidence insufficient to sustain the general verdict rendered by the jury. Finally, court held statute addressing disfigurement of the child was not unconstitutionally vague.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction for the offense of injury to a child under the age of 14 years and his sentence to 15 years' confinement, holding that the evidence adequately supported the conviction and that the statute concerning causing the disfigurement of a child was not unconstitutionally vague.

Whitworth v. Bynum


No. 01-84-00213-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


679 S.W.2d 608; 1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 6099



August 30, 1984 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied September 27, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 234th District Court of Harris County, Texas Trial Court Cause No. 82-1791.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant nephew sought review of the decision of the 234th District Court of Harris County, Texas, which granted appellee uncle summary judgment on grounds that appellant was precluded from recovery against appellee under the Texas Guest Statute, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6710b, § 1(a) (1975), in appellant's action for injuries resulting from an automobile accident.


OVERVIEW: Appellant nephew was riding as a passenger in appellee uncle's car when he sustained injuries in an automobile accident. Appellant sued appellee, and the trial court granted summary judgment in favor of appellee because appellant was precluded from recovery under the Texas Guest Statute, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6710b, § 1(a) (1975). Appellant argued that the statute violated equal protection of the law and that the wrong method of computing degree of affinity was used. The court affirmed and held that the Texas Guest Statute was constitutional and that the court could not redraft legislation because another version may be more equitable. The court held that Texas had followed the common law method of computing degrees of kinship and that appellant was within the second degree of consanguinity or affinity with appellee and was, therefore, precluded from suing appellee as host-driver.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order granting appellee uncle summary judgment on the ground that appellant nephew was precluded from suing under Texas Guest Statute. The court held that the statute was constitutional and that the legislature was the proper body to repeal the law. The court held that Texas used the common law method of determining degrees of affinity and that appellant was within second degree with appellee.

 

1426 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Lucario v. State


No. 01-82-0659-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


677 S.W.2d 693; 1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 6113



August 30, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 184th District Court of Harris County, Texas Trial Court Cause No. 351,064.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction in the 184th District Court of Harris County (Texas), of engaging in organized criminal activity. The case was remanded from the Court of Criminal Appeals, which vacated the appellate court's judgment and directed a review of appellant's argument that the organized crime statute was vague.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of engaging in organized criminal activity, in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 71.02(a)(1). The court affirmed, holding that it was not necessary, even when a motion to quash was presented, to specifically allege the manner and means of acting in the course of committing theft in an indictment for aggravated robbery. The court held that the statute was not unconstitutionally vague, since the statute required an accused to know of the criminal activity of the group, specific terms in the statute could be understood by persons of reasonable intelligence, and prosecution was not given unbridled discretion. The court found that the legislature's intent to punish organized criminal activity more severely than random crime was legitimate. Finally, the court overruled appellant's final ground of error that he should have been prosecuted for attempted aggravated robbery or for conspiracy to commit aggravated robbery, rather than the more general offense of engaging in organized criminal activity, holding that the statutes regarding attempt and conspiracy did not govern the same subject matter as does the organized criminal activity statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment, holding that the statute was not unconstitutionally vague, that appellant was not improperly indicted for engaging in organized criminal activity, and that the punishment scheme was legitimate.

Welch v. State


No. 01-82-0908-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


680 S.W.2d 834; 1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 6115



August 30, 1984 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied November 29, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 240th District Court of Fort Bend County, Texas Trial Court Cause Number 12,809.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the sufficiency of the evidence in the verdict from the 240th District Court of Fort Bend County (Texas), that convicted appellant of intentionally and knowingly possessing with the intent to deliver a controlled substance in violation of the Controlled Substances Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15, § 4.03.


OVERVIEW: A police informant had arranged to purchase drugs from appellant. The officers had pre-arranged that once appellant had offered informant the drugs, she would raise her hand. Upon observing the informant's raised hand, the officers approached appellant. During the search, drugs were discovered in appellant's shoe and he was arrested for intentionally and knowingly possessing with the intent to deliver a controlled substance. At appellant's trial the informant did not testify. After appellant was convicted, he sought review and argued that because the informant did not testify, there was insufficient evidence that he intended to "sell" the drugs. The appellate court found that the only evidence that appellant intended to deliver the substance was the informant's alleged hand signal and without her testimony, the state failed to carry its burden of proving beyond a reasonable doubt that appellant possessed with the intent to deliver the drugs. The appellate court reversed the trial court's judgment and ordered appellant acquitted because there was insufficient evidence to warrant the jury's finding of appellant's guilt for the intent to transfer a controlled substance.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the appellant's conviction for intentionally and knowingly possessing with the intent to deliver a controlled substance because the fact that appellant possessed drugs and met with a police informant was insufficient evidence to warrant the jury's finding of appellant's guilt beyond a reasonable doubt for the intent to transfer a controlled substance. The appellate court ordered appellant acquitted.

WILSON v. STATE


No. 01-83-0413-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 6123



August 30, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] On Appeal from the 208th District Court of Harris County, Texas Trial Court Cause No. 380,742


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order of the 208th District Court of Harris County (Texas), which convicted him of unauthorized use of a motor vehicle.


OVERVIEW: After a jury trial, appellant was convicted of unauthorized use of a motor vehicle. The appellate court affirmed, holding that there was sufficient evidence to find that appellant operated the vehicle in the county in which he was charged. In so ruling, the appellate court first noted that the term "operated" as used in Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 31.07(a) meant actual physical control. The appellate court then noted that appellant was stopped by two police officers (prior to the vehicle being reported as stolen) in the county in which he was convicted. Further, the trial court did not err in refusing to instruct the jury on the law of circumstantial evidence, as such instruction was no longer required. Because appellant did not raise the issues of whether the enhancement paragraph was sufficiently specific, or whether the previous convictions were final, in the trial court, he waived such issues. The appellate court held that appellant's life sentence under the recidivist statute, Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 12.42(d) (1974) was constitutional on its face and as applied.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's conviction of appellant for unauthorized use of a motor vehicle, because there was sufficient evidence to find that appellant operated the vehicle in the county in which he was charged, the instruction of circumstantial evidence was not required, he waived any error with respect to the enhancement paragraph by failing to object in the trial court, and his life sentence was constitutional.

GRUESSING v. STATE


No. 01-82-0865-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston

OVERVIEW: After the trial court admonished defendant of he range of his potential punishment pursuant to Tex. Crim. Proc. On appeal, defendant contended that the admonishment was for the wrong range, because the portion of the statute defining the range was previously found unconstitutional. OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for possession of cocaine and remanded for a new trial. The trial court did not properly admonish defendant before accepting his guilty plea. The trial court advised defendant of the incorrect penalty range that excluded the possibility of probation or deferred adjudication.

PRATT v. STATE


No. 01-83-0668-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 6127



August 30, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] On Appeal from the 339th District Court of Harris County, Texas Trial Court Cause No. 381,737


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the 339th District Court of Harris County (Texas), which convicted him of injury to a child, under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 22.01.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of injury to a child, under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 22.01. The complainant, defendant's son, suffered second and third degree burns. The physician found that the injuries were inconsistent with defendant's explanation and concluded that the child had been abused. Defendant admitted to police that he had dipped the child in a tub of hot water to punish him, but he claimed that he had not intended to injure the child and was unaware of the extreme temperature of the water. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. It was necessary for state to prove that it was defendant's conscious objective or desire to cause serious bodily injury to the child or, in the alternative, that defendant was aware that his conduct was reasonably certain to cause the resultant injury. There was sufficient circumstantial evidence on the issue of intent to support the jury's finding that defendant was aware that his conduct was reasonably certain to cause serious bodily injury. The court held that the terms "disfigurement" and "deformity," as used in Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 22.04(a), were not unconstitutionally vague but were terms with ordinary meaning.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court, convicting defendant of injury to a child, was affirmed. There was sufficient circumstantial evidence on the issue of intent to support the jury's finding that defendant was aware that his conduct was reasonably certain to cause serious bodily injury. The court held that the terms "disfigurement" and "deformity," as used in the applicable statute, were not unconstitutionally vague.

Wahl v. State


No. 01-83-0035-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


679 S.W.2d 598; 1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 6133



August 30, 1984 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied September 27, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 183rd District Court of Harris County, Texas Trial Court Cause Number 357,229.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order of the 183rd District Court of Harris County (Texas), which convicted him of possessing and manufacturing methamphetamine, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15, § 4.04(a)(c)(d)(2) (1981).


OVERVIEW: After a jury trial, appellant was convicted of possessing and manufacturing methamphetamine, under the Controlled Substances Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15, § 4.04(a), (c), (d)(2) (1981). The appellate court reversed, holding that the indictment upon which appellant was charged was void. In so ruling, the appellate court noted that the indictment alleged a violation of H.B. 730, which had been declared unconstitutional. Although the statute amended by H.B. 730, the Controlled Substances Act, was still valid, the appellate court noted that punishment was assessed according to H.B. 730. Because appellant was entitled to begin his criminal matter with a correct indictment, the matter was remanded. The appellate court further held that the trial court did not err in refusing to allow a psychologist testify as to appellant's lack of mental capacity to set-up a methamphetamine laboratory. In so ruling, the appellate court noted that appellant did not plea insanity or mental incompetency to stand trial, and specific intent was not an element of the offense charged.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the judgment of the trial court that convicted appellant of possessing and manufacturing methamphetamine, and remanded the matter, because the statute under which appellant was indicted had been declared unconstitutional, and even though the old statute was still valid, appellant was entitled to begin his criminal matter with a corrected indictment.

University of Houston v. Sabeti


No. 01-83-782-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


676 S.W.2d 685; 1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 6172



August 30, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 151st District Court of Harris County, Texas Trial Court Cause Number 83-53101.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant university sought review of an order of the 151st District Court of Harris County (Texas), which, in an action brought by appellee student against appellant challenging his expulsion, held that appellant denied appellee due process of law.


OVERVIEW: Appellant university permanently expelled appellee student for misrepresenting as his own work certain papers that were prepared by another. After a hearing by the engineering department, which recommended expulsion, a hearing was held before the college honesty board. At this hearing, appellee was allowed counsel of his choice, a law student. However, the law student could only attend and advise appellee during the hearing; he could not speak argue, or question witnesses. Appellant was not represented by counsel. The appeal to the university provost was unsuccessful. Appellee brought an action against appellant to have his expulsion set-aside, claiming the hearing before the college honesty board denied him due process of law. The trial court granted appellee relief. The appellate court reversed, holding that due process of law guaranteed by U.S. Const. amend. XIV was not violated. In so ruling, the appellate court noted that appellee received the basic elements of due process - notice and an opportunity to be heard. He was given notice of the hearing, testified fully, and was allowed a form of cross-examination.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the order of the trial court, which held that appellant university denied appellee student due process of law in an expulsion hearing, because appellee received notice and an opportunity to be heard.

HUNT v. STATE

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the decision of the 272nd District Court of Brazos County (Texas), which convicted appellant of aggravated rape and denied appellant's motion to disqualify the trial judge under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 200a, § 5a.


OVERVIEW: At appellant's trial for aggravated rape, appellant sought to disqualify the trial judge under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 200a, § 5a. The motion was denied and appellant was convicted. He sought review and argued that there was insufficient evidence for his rape conviction and that the trial court erred in denying his motion to disqualify because there was no formal order of assignment from the presiding judge. The appellate court affirmed appellant's conviction and determined that under § 5a, it made no difference if the judge of the trial court to which assignment was made was presiding over the transferring trial court at the same time. The appellate court held that there was evidence of the victim's forcible abduction, as well as testimony showing that a rape had been committed, and therefore the evidence was sufficient to sustain the jury's verdict.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed appellant's conviction for aggravated rape because the fact that appellant gave a different account of the rape incident did not render the state's evidence insufficient and there was sufficient evidence to have found appellant guilty beyond a reasonable doubt, and appellant failed to show that the assignment of his case to another trial judge was made improperly and not pursuant to all statutory requirements.

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied September 19, 1984.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff judge appealed from an adverse summary judgment rendered by a Texas trial court in his libel action against defendants, newspaper and staff writer, after a trial which resulted in a mistrial when the jury was unable to reach a verdict.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff judge brought an action for libel against defendants, newspaper and writer, for their publication of an article accusing plaintiff of engaging in political gamesmanship by selecting a biased grand jury to influence the outcome of a probe into missing funds from the county attorney's office, and implying that plaintiff violated the law governing grand jury appointments by selecting not only the grand jury commissioners but also the members making up the jury panel. Plaintiff sought actual and punitive damages. After a trial at which the jury was unable to arrive at a verdict and the judge ordered a mistrial, defendants filed a motion for summary judgment, which was granted largely on the basis of defendant writer's affidavit that she believed what she wrote to be true. The court on appeal reversed and remanded, finding that the record was not devoid of any genuine issues of fact, accepting as true the proof offered by plaintiff and making every inference in plaintiff's favor as required on review of a grant of summary judgment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's grant of summary judgment and remanded for a new trial on the merits of plaintiff judge's libel claims, finding that summary judgment should not have been granted based on defendant writer's affidavit attempting to establish the absence of actual malice and that the record raised genuine issues of fact when the court made every inference in the non-movant plaintiff's favor.

Air Curtain Destructor Corp. v. Austin


No. 12-83-0108-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Twelfth District, Tyler


675 S.W.2d 615; 1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 6908



August 23, 1984 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied September 13, 1984.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant trench burner manufacturer challenged the trial court's take-nothing judgment against appellant in appellant's suit for a declaratory judgment to void and a permanent injunction against enforcement of Austin, Tex. Code § 13-10(e), a penal ordinance prohibiting the construction, operation, and use of trench burners within the corporate limits of the city, or within 5,000 feet thereof, and declaring trench burners a public nuisance.


OVERVIEW: Appellant trench burner manufacturer filed suit for a declaratory judgment to void and a permanent injunction against enforcement of Austin, Tex. Code § 13-10(e), a penal ordinance prohibiting construction, operation, and use of trench burners within the corporate limits of the city of Austin, or within 5,000 feet thereof, and declaring them a public nuisance. The trial court made findings of fact and conclusions of law that appellant had no ongoing business within the city that which was destroyed, limited, or impaired by the ordinance; that the ordinance was a reasonable exercise by the city of its police powers; and that the construction, operation, and use of a trench burner within the corporate limits of the city constituted a nuisance in fact. In reversing and rendering judgment for appellant, the court held that continued enforcement of § 13-10(e) would irreparably damage appellant's vested property rights because it was highly unlikely, due to its penal nature, that § 13-10(e) would ever be tested in criminal court. Further, the court found trench burners not to be public nuisance per se.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and rendered judgment for appellant. Continued enforcement of the ordinance would have irreparably damaged appellant trench burner manufacturer's vested property rights to manufacture and sell trench burners in the city of Austin because the ordinance's penal nature made it highly unlikely to be tested in criminal court. Trench burners were also not public nuisances per se.

 

1436 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Vanderburg v. State


No. Cl4-83-708-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


681 S.W.2d 713; 1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 6005



August 16, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the 232nd District Court of Harris County Cause No. 299,355.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the order of the District Court of Harris County (Texas), which revoked his probation and ordered for him to pay restitution to the State of Texas as a condition of parole under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. art. 42.12, § 15(g) (1984).


OVERVIEW: Defendant pleaded guilty to burglary of a building and was placed on probation. Thereafter, he was convicted of other crimes in other states. He violated other conditions of his probation by failing to contact his probation officer, failing to pay supervisory fees, and failing to reimburse the county for his court appointed attorney. The trial court revoked defendant's probation, and ordered him to pay restitution for extradition fees from California in the amount of $ 1,180 as a condition of any subsequent parole. The court affirmed the revocation of defendant's probation, holding that by pleading guilty, defendant made a judicial confession. The court held that a judicial confession standing alone would sustain a conviction subsequent to a guilty plea and satisfy the prerequisites of Tex. Code Crim. Proc. art. 1.15 (1977), and a violation of one condition of probation provided sufficient cause for revocation. The court struck the order to pay restitution, holding that the record was devoid of evidence sustaining the costs of extradition and that due process required sufficient evidence to show the amount ordered by the trial court had a factual basis.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the revocation of probation, because defendant's guilty plea to other crimes was a sufficient basis for revocation. The court struck the order that defendant pay extradition costs, holding that due process required sufficient evidence in the record to show the amount ordered by the trial court had a factual basis.

 

1437 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Michelle Corp. v. El Paso Retailers Asso.


No. 08-83-00063-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Eighth District, El Paso


675 S.W.2d 610; 1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 5933



August 15, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from 168th District Court of El Paso County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant retail store challenged the judgment of the 168th District Court of El Paso County, Texas, which granted a permanent injunction in favor of appellee retailer's association. Appellant argued that the trial court erred in not granting summary judgment based on appellant's charitable purposes and the unconstitutional vagueness of the statute prohibiting retail sales on consecutive Saturdays and Sundays.


OVERVIEW: Appellee retail association obtained a permanent injunction to prohibit appellant retailer from selling items on consecutive Saturdays and Sundays, pursuant to Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 9001 (1984). Appellant challenged the injunction, and argued that the trial court failed to consider its affirmative defense of charitable purpose and that the statute was unconstitutionally vague in its description of the items covered by the statute. The court affirmed the injunction. The court held that there was no legal basis for a defense of charitable purposes to the prohibition of selling goods on consecutive Saturdays and Sundays when only a portion of the profit went to charity. The court held that all of the proceeds must go to charity for the sales to be excluded from the prohibition. The court distinguished the Texas statute from an Arkansas statute that had been held unconstitutionally vague and held that Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 9001, § 1 (1984), adequately described the items for which a prohibition existed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the injunction, and held that the charitable purposes defense did not apply because appellant did not donate all of the net proceeds to charity. The court held that the statute adequately described the items which were not to be sold on consecutive Saturdays and Sundays, so the statute was not unconstitutionally vague.

Adkins v. State


No. 08-83-00092-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Eighth District, El Paso


675 S.W.2d 604; 1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 5852



August 1, 1984 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied September 5, 1984, Reported at: 675 S.W.2d 604 at 609.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from 83rd District Court of Upton County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant offender appealed from 83rd District Court of Upton County (Texas),that entered a conviction for possession of a controlled substance. Defendant asserted that the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress evidence, defendant was denied a right to a speedy trial, and that there was prosecutorial misconduct.


OVERVIEW: Defendant offender was originally indicted when the applicable law was in transition and the indictment was brought under the new law later found to be unconstitutional. The court held that the indictment was valid, stating an offense under the prior provisions; however, defendant received a penalty greater than that authorized by the prior provisions of Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15, § 4.04(b)(2). Defendant asserted that the court erred in denying his motion to suppress all evidence seized pursuant to the warrant utilized by the state and defendant claimed that the affidavit offered in support of the warrant failed to establish probable cause. The court held that it could not find the warrant invalid and then find that the officers were confronted with exigent circumstances depriving them of an opportunity to secure a warrant. Defendant asserted that the court should have declared a mistrial when the prosecutor injected his personal opinion into the voir dire by advising the prospective jurors of his opposition to probation in this case. The court held that the defense objection was sustained, the jury panel instructed to disregard the comment, thus the error was cured.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed and the cause remanded to the trial court for further proceedings because the court found the warrant invalid and that the evidence obtained should have been suppressed, that there was no showing that the state was unprepared for trial or cause unnecessary delays, and the error caused by the prosecutor's comments had been cured.
