1440 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


American Bank & Trust Co. v. Dallas County


No. 20915


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


679 S.W.2d 566; 1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 6708



July 23, 1984 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied October 31, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM A DISTRICT COURT OF DALLAS COUNTY, TEXAS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The United States Supreme Court remanded the action after it reversed the court's judgment that had affirmed the trial court's decision upholding the validity of ad valorem assessments of shares of banking corporations.


OVERVIEW: The United States Supreme Court declared illegal ad valorem assessments of the shares of appellant banks and reversed and remanded the court's judgment upholding the validity of the assessments. On remand, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment denying appellant shareholders injunctive relief, holding that, although the illegality resulted from disregard of a federal statute, it was not sufficient without proof that a lower tax would be due under a proper assessment. The court noted that the use of the "equity capital formula" to compute and assess value was contrary to 31 U.S.C.S. § 742 because it took into account the federal obligations held by appellant banks. However, the Supreme Court did not hold that the Texas statute, Tex. Tax.-Gen. Ann. art. 7166 (1960), imposing the tax on bank shares was unconstitutional. The court held that the market value of the shares was the only proper basis for assessment and found that appellant shareholders had failed to establish substantial injury entitling them to injunctive relief. However, in accordance with the Supreme Court's opinion, the trial court's judgment was modified and declaratory relief was granted.


OUTCOME: The court acknowledged the United States Supreme Court holding that declared ad valorem assessments of shares of banking corporations were illegal. The court affirmed the trial court's order denying appellant shareholders injunctive relief because they failed to establish that they would have incurred an equal or greater tax liability under a proper assessment.

 

1441 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


YORKO v. STATE


No. 01-83-0518-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 5811



July 19, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] On Appeal from County Criminal Court at Law No. 7 of Harris County, Texas

Trial Court Cause No. 684,424


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the County Criminal Court at Law No. 7 of Harris County (Texas) which convicted him for selling an obscene magazine and assessed his punishment at a fine.


OVERVIEW: The appellant was charged with selling an obscene magazine. A jury found him guilty and assessed his punishment at a fine. Appellant challenged the constitutionality of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 43.23(e), and contended that the trial court committed reversible error in charging the jury on the basis of the presumption of knowledge contained in that statute. The court agreed, reversed the judgment, and ordered a new trial because the statutory presumption of knowledge contained in § 43.23(e) had been declared unconstitutional. The material which appellant sold was protected by both the state and federal constitutions, and by instructing the jury that the unconstitutional presumption applied, the trial court committed reversible error, even where there was other evidence of knowledge that supported a conviction. The burden rested upon the prosecution to prove that the appellant had knowledge of the content and character of the allegedly obscene material and such knowledge could not have been inferred merely by viewing the cover of the magazine.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court, which convicted appellant for selling an obscene magazine and assessed his punishment at a fine because the trial court erred in charging the jury on the basis of the presumption of knowledge contained in the statute which was declared unconstitutional.

 

1442 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Thompson v. State


No. C14-81-351-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


676 S.W.2d 173; 1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 5875



July 19, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the County Criminal Court of Law No. 2 of Harris County Cause No. 601,172.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a conviction and sentence to the charge of criminally negligent homicide under Tex. Penal Code Ann § 19.07 (1974) in the County Criminal Court of Law No. 2 of Harris County (Texas).


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought review of the conviction and sentence after appellant pleaded guilty to criminally negligent homicide under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 19.07 (1974) based upon the mental state defined in Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 6.03. The court affirmed and found that the criminal appellate court found that §§ 6.03, 19.07 were constitutional. The court also found that § 19.07 only required that appellee state prove beyond a reasonable doubt that appellant should have been aware of the substantial and unjustifiable risk of appellant's conduct and not that appellant actually perceived the risk. The burden was met by sufficient circumstantial evidence that appellant sped through a residential neighborhood, and not by a presumption in § 19.07. The court also held that the information did not have to plead the exact terminology of § 19.07 to apprise appellant of the charges. The jury instructions were correct because whether there was an accident or contributory negligence was not a defense to § 19.07 and lack of voluntary conduct was not supported by the evidence. Appellant failed to preserve the issue of appellee's witness's alleged improper testimony because he failed to object.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for criminally negligent homicide and held that appellee state only had to prove that appellant should have been aware of a substantial risk, which was shown through sufficient circumstantial evidence, that the information was sufficient to place appellant on notice of the charge, and where appellant failed to object, appellant failed to preserve for appeal the issue of improper witness testimony.

YORKO v. STATE


No. 01-83-0517-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 5906



July 19, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] On Appeal from County Criminal Court at Law No. 7 of Harris County, Texas

Trial Court Cause No. 683,917


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the County Criminal Court at Law No. 7 of Harris County (Texas), which convicted him of selling an obscene magazine.


OVERVIEW: Following conviction for selling an obscene magazine, appellant contended that his conviction had to be reversed because the state failed to prove that the appellant sold the material knowing its content and character was obscene. The judgment of the trial court was reversed and the cause was remanded for new trial because it was undisputed that the following words were crossed out of the statement of evidence: "and character," "unlawfully," and "patently offensive." Thus, the stipulation of evidence presented to the trial court stated only that appellant had sold the material in question knowing its "content." The court held that the stipulation in its final form did not set forth the requisite elements of the statute and, therefore, was insufficient to support the appellant's conviction. The conviction could not be upheld on the basis of any presumption of knowledge, since section Tex. Pen. Code Ann. § 43.23(e) had been declared unconstitutional and there was no other evidence in the record to supply the missing element of proof.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court, which convicted appellant of selling an obscene magazine because the stipulation of evidence stated on the appellant did not set forth the requisite elements of the statute and, therefore, was insufficient to support the appellant's conviction. The court remanded the case for a new trial rather than ordering an acquittal.

 

1444 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Gonzales v. State


No. 01-82-00552-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


676 S.W.2d 437; 1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 5813



July 12, 1984 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied August 30, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 6 of Harris County, Texas

Trial Court Cause No. 654,707


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the County Criminal Court, Harris County, Texas, following his conviction of obscenity in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 43.23(c)(1) (1981). Defendant claimed that an instruction to the jury which included the language of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 43.34(e) was reversible error.


OVERVIEW: After a police officer entered an adult bookstore where defendant worked as a cashier, and observed numerous magazines depicting sexually oriented acts on their covers, the officer purchased a magazine, obtained an arrest warrant, and arrested defendant several days later. At defendant's trial for obscenity in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 43.23(c)(1) (1981), an instruction was given to the jury containing the exact language of Tex. Penal Code § 43.23(e) (1981), to wit: A person who promoted obscene material or possessed the same with intent to promote it in the course of his business was presumed to do so with knowledge of its content and character. In reversing defendant's conviction, the court found that this instruction was reversible error because the material in question were magazines which were afforded the protection of free speech under both U.S. Const. amend. I and Tex. Const. art. I, § 8. The court also found that the state's reliance on the constitutionality of § 43.23(e) was reasonable and therefore, the state had the right to retry defendant and to present any evidence that it may have withheld at the initial trial based on this reliance.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's obscenity conviction, as it was error to give a jury instruction which included a presumption on intent in an obscenity case dealing with magazines, where the material was protected by freedom of speech, guaranteed by both the U.S. and Texas constitutions. Because the state's reliance on the constitutionality of the statute containing the presumption was reasonable, the state had the right to retry the defendant.

Willacy County Appraisal Dist. v. North Alamo Water Supply Corp.


No. 13-83-318-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Thirteenth District, Corpus Christi


676 S.W.2d 632; 1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 5749



June 28, 1984 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motions for Rehearing Denied August 31, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the 107th District Court of Willacy County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, county appraisal district and its board of review, sought review of the judgment from the 107th District Court, Willacy County, Texas, declaring that appellee public utility was exempt from ad valorem taxation under Tex. Prop. Code Ann. § 11.18 (1984) and awarding appellee attorney's fees. Appellants contended that appellee had failed to meet the statutory requirements necessary for exemption entitlement.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, county appraisal district and its board of review, denied appellee public utility's application for exemption from ad valorem taxation of its property. Appellee claimed that it was exempt under Tex. Prop. Code Ann. § 11.18 (1984) as a "charitable organization." Appellee sought review from appellants' administrative decision. Appellants filed an answer and a cross-petition for declaratory judgment, alleging that § 11.18 exceeded its constitutional authority by creating the exemption for properties of organizations like appellee. The trial court found in favor of appellee and declined to rule on appellants' cross-petition. The court on appeal reversed, holding that appellee failed to meet its burden to establish that it met all the requirements for the tax exemption under § 11.18 by allowing its members to realize private gain through the sale of their memberships at a premium, and by failing to provide for a direct transfer of its assets upon discontinuance to a charitable organization as defined under I.R.C. § 501(c)(3) (1954), as amended. The court found that in light of its holding, appellee was not entitled to attorney's fees.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment which had declared that appellee public utility was exempt from ad valorem taxation and which awarded it attorney's fees. The court held that the record showed that appellee had failed to establish that it met all the requirements to qualify for the exemption and that, because appellee was not entitled to judgment, it was not entitled to attorney's fees.

Duhrkopf v. State


No. 2-83-105-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Second District, Fort Worth


671 S.W.2d 147; 1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 5773



June 27, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE 297TH DISTRICT COURT OF TARRANT COUNTY.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment of the 297th District Court of Tarrant County (Texas), which revoked his probation. He argued that it was error to permit proof of his probation record through the use of business records and that the constitutional and statutory protections against double jeopardy were violated by imposing additional probation conditions for three offenses and then using the same offenses as grounds for revocation.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, a probationer, was arrested for three offenses and returned to the trial court, which imposed additional probation conditions. The state then filed a petition to revoke probation which cited the three offenses as grounds for revocation. At the revocation proceeding, the state was permitted to prove appellant's probation record through a record authenticated under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 3737e (1984). Appellant challenged the judgment revoking his probation, claiming that use of an authenticated business record violated his rights of confrontation and cross-examination and that use of the three offenses as grounds to revoke probation after the imposition of additional conditions of probation placed him in double jeopardy. The court affirmed the judgment because it held that the authenticated records were so trustworthy as to guarantee the same protection afforded by confrontation and cross-examination and that the protection against double jeopardy did not apply to the revocation of probation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed because it found that the authenticated probation record was sufficiently trustworthy to guarantee the same protection provided by the rights of confrontation and cross-examination, and double jeopardy protection did not apply in probation revocation proceedings.

Rowden v. Texas Catastrophe Property Ins. Asso.


No. 13-83-467-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Thirteenth District, Corpus Christi


677 S.W.2d 83; 1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 5673



June 14, 1984 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied August 31, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the 105th District Court of Nueces County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owner sought review of an order of the 105th District Court of Nueces County (Texas) that dismissed her cause, without prejudice, against appellee insurance association that alleged that appellee's representations, acts, and denials of liability amounted to deceptive trade practices, for want of jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: Appellant property owner made a claim on her insurance policy issued by appellee insurance association for losses sustained by her property during a hurricane. She brought suit against appellee when the settlement of her claim could not be negotiated, alleging that its acts and denial of liability constituted deceptive trade practices. The trial court dismissed her case without prejudice, on the basis that she failed to exhaust her statutory remedy provided by the Texas Catastrophe Property Insurance Pool Act, Tex. Ins. Code Ann. art. 21.49 §9 (1981). She argued that the trial court erred in dismissing her suit because it had jurisdiction and venue of the case. The court disagreed, finding that the issue on appeal was the subject matter jurisdiction of the trial court. Where a cause of action and its remedy were derived from statute, the statutory provisions must be complied with or the action was not maintainable. Here, appellant brought suit in the district court before initiating a proceeding at the State Board of Insurance, and, thus, failed to exhaust her administrative remedies. The court overruled appellant's other points of error and affirmed the order of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court that dismissed appellant property owners' action against appellee insurance association that alleged acts by appellee that constituted deceptive trade practices, where appellant failed to exhaust her statutory remedies as she was required to do by initiating a proceeding at the State Board of Insurance before bringing suit in the district court.

 

1449 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


COUNCIL OF CO-OWNERS OF SAIDA IT TOWERS CONDO. ASSN. v. TEXAS CATASTROPHE PROP. INS. ASSN.


No. 12,970


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 5659



June 13, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 126TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT NO. 337,150A, HONORABLE CHARLES D. MATHEWS, JUDGE PRESIDING


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owners appealed a judgment of the 126th District Court of Travis County (Texas), which dismissed plaintiffs' actions alleging that defendant insurance association wrongfully refused to pay plaintiffs' insurance claims for property losses resulting from a hurricane.


OVERVIEW: Within 30 days of the State Board of Insurance's decision validating defendant insurance association's denial of plaintiff property owners' claims for loss resulting from a hurricane, plaintiffs filed actions against defendant alleging that their claims were wrongfully denied. The trial court dismissed the actions on the ground that it did not have jurisdiction. On appeal, the court reversed the dismissals and remanded the cause. The court held that even though plaintiffs did not name the state board as a defendant, the trial court had jurisdiction over plaintiffs' actions whether the actions on the insurance contracts were inherently common law causes of action or whether they were purely statutory in character. The court held that the timely filing of the actions against defendant tolled the running of the 30 day limitation period for purposes of correcting a defect of parties. The court ruled that Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6252-13a, § 19 (1984), and Tex. Ins. Code Ann. arts. 21.49, § 9 and 1.04(f), could not be interpreted to mean that the naming of the state board as a defendant was a jurisdictional element of plaintiffs' actions without violating Tex. Const. art I, § 13.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment dismissing plaintiff property owners' actions and remanded the cause for trial because the trial court erred in finding that it did not have jurisdiction. The court held that the trial court had subject-matter jurisdiction because within 30 days of the State Board of Insurance's order validating defendant insurance association's denial of coverage, plaintiffs requested a de novo review of the board's order.

Adley v. State


No. 05-83-00720-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


675 S.W.2d 240; 1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 6182



June 12, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From a District Court of Dallas County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the decision from the District Court of Dallas County (Texas) which convicted him of gambling promotion and sentenced him to three years probated.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of promoting gambling under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 47.03(a)(2) and he challenged the conviction arguing that the indictment was unconstitutionally vague. The court rejected this argument noting that the wording of the indictment tracked the wording of the statute. The court found that the face of the instrument set forth in plain and intelligible language sufficient information to enable the accused to prepare a defense. The court also rejected appellant's other contention that the statute meant that a bet had to be made between two or more persons other than appellant. The court found that the number involved in the bet was irrelevant and it could be just appellant and another. The other contentions, based upon his erroneous argument regarding the number of people, were summarily overruled. The court therefore affirmed the conviction.


OUTCOME: Appellant's conviction for promoting gambling was affirmed because the wording of the indictment tracked the wording of the statute, and because it set forth in plain and intelligible language sufficient information to allow appellant to prepare a defense.

Valentino v. Houston


No. 01-83-0085-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


674 S.W.2d 813; 1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 5623



June 7, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the 125th District Court of Harris County, Texas Trial Court Cause Number 81-27093.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment from the 125th District Court, Harris County (Texas), in an administrative action where the trial court had upheld a decision from the civil service commission ordering appellant indefinitely suspended, that is fired from the police force.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, a city police officer, sued under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 1269m § 18 to set aside an order from the Civil Service Commission (commission) indefinitely suspending, that is, firing, him from the police department for striking an arrestee in custody. The trial court held that there was substantial evidence to affirm the commission's order. Appellant contended, among other things, that the trial court had erred in holding that the order of the commission, which upheld appellant's indefinite suspension, was supported by substantial evidence. The court affirmed. The trial court heard and considered evidence to determine whether reasonable support for the administrative order existed. The agency itself was the primary fact-finding body, and the question to be determined by the trial court was strictly one of law. The record was sufficient to withstand a "substantial evidence" attack. Reasonable minds, discounting the "self defense" version of the episode in favor of other witness' testimony, could also have reached the commission's conclusion. Under the applicable standard of review, nothing further was required.


OUTCOME: The court upheld the judgment from the trial court, upholding the decision from the civil service commission indefinitely suspending, that is firing, appellant because substantial evidence had existed to support the trial court.

 

1452 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Estate of Ross


No. 11-83-250-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Eleventh District, Eastland


672 S.W.2d 315; 1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 5635



June 7, 1984 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied June 7, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Eastland County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, daughters, challenged the judgment from the Eastland County (Texas) trial court that overruled their motion to set aside an order probating their father's will and appointing appellee, a son, as executor of his estate and for a new trial. Appellant's claim that the notice provisions of Tex. Prob. Code Ann. § 128 (1980) was unconstitutional and appellee's failure to give them personal notice deprived them of due process.


OVERVIEW: The day after the parties' father died, appellee, the father's son, applied to probate his father's will that disinherited appellants, the father's daughters, and to be executor of his father's estate pursuant to the will. Appellee provided the only notice of his application by posting notice in the county courthouse pursuant to Tex. Prob. Code Ann. § 128(a) (1980), and the trial court signed an order probating the will and appointing appellee. Appellants filed a motion to set aside the order and for a new trial, but the motion was overruled by operation of law. On appeal, the court held that because appellants did not serve the state attorney general pursuant to Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 2524-1, § 11 (1965), they waived their claim that Tex. Prob. Code Ann. § 128 was unconstitutional. The court held that the posted notice was sufficient because probate proceedings were in rem proceedings that bound all persons, and that appellants due process rights were not violated by not being served because they still could contest the will under Tex. Prob. Code Ann. § 93 (1980). Therefore, the court affirmed the judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order overruling the motion of appellants, daughters, to set aside an order probating their father's will and appointing appellee, a son, as executor of his estate and for a new trial. The court held that the failure to serve the state attorney general preclude review of the constitutionality of the notice statute, and appellee's notice by posting rather than serving notice on appellants did not deprive them of due process.

 

1453 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Young Sun Lee v. State


No. B14-83-281-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


681 S.W.2d 656; 1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 5651



June 7, 1984 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied June 28, 1984. Discretionary Review Refused November 7, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from County Criminal Court at Law No. 8 of Harris County Cause No. 697,749.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged decision from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 8, Harris County (Texas) for conviction of prostitution. Appellant argued that the information was defective, that the charge was improper, that there was a variance between the information and the court's charge, that the prostitution statute was unconstitutional, that the evidence was insufficient and that the trial court erred in overruling appellant's motion for mistrial.


OVERVIEW: Appellant raised numerous arguments in appeal of a prostitution conviction. The court rejected an argument that the information was defective because appellant failed to preserve those grounds for review. Appellant also argued that the jury charge was improper by failing to allege a culpable mental state and improperly defining deviate sexual intercourse. The court held that appellant did not object to the jury charge, and preserved nothing for review. The court found that the evidence was sufficient to show that appellant offered or agreed to sexual conduct for a fee. The court rejected arguments that the prostitution statute was unconstitutional by holding that any incidental restriction of free expression was no greater that necessary to further a substantial government interest in protecting citizens' health and safety and that the statute was not vague. It was argued that appellant could not be convicted through the uncorroborated testimony of an accomplice to the offense, the police officer. The court held that an undercover agent was not an accomplice so long as he did not bring about the crime, but merely obtained evidence of it.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed conviction of prostitution, holding that most grounds were not preserved for appeal. The court held that the prostitution statute was constitutional because any incidental restriction of free expression was no greater that necessary to further a substantial government interest in protecting citizens' health and safety. Further, the court held that the statute was not unconstitutionally vague.

 

1454 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Hurwitz v. State


No. 3-83-090-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


673 S.W.2d 347; 1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 5645



June 6, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From the District Court of Williamson County, 277th Judicial District No. 82-279-K, Honorable John R. Carter, Judge Presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment from the 277th Judicial District Court of Williamson County (Texas) that convicted him of marihuana possession under § 4.051(b)(4) of the Texas Controlled Substances Act, 1981 Tex. Gen. Laws, ch. 268. Appellant claimed that his trial was beyond the time limit in the Texas Speedy Trial Act, Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 32A.02 (Supp. 1984), the marihuana was found illegally, and his guilty plea was involuntary.


OVERVIEW: A police officer climbed over a locked fence in order to reach appellant's marihuana field, which was not visible from the road. As a result, appellant was convicted upon his guilty plea of possession of marihuana under § 4.051(b)(4) of the Texas Controlled Substances Act, 1981 Tex. Gen. Laws, ch. 268. On appeal, the court held that the fenced area was not part of appellant's protected curtilage and that property rights against trespass were irrelevant to U.S. Const. amend. IV. Thus, the search was valid under the open fields doctrine. Because appellee, the state, filed a statement of readiness for trial within the time limit of the Texas Speedy Trial Act, Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 32A.02 (Supp. 1984), appellant's speedy trial rights were not violated although the trial was not held within the time limit. Because appellant received the minimum sentence for either a third degree or a second degree felony, he was not harmed when the trial court admonished him under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 26.13(1) (Supp. 1984) on the punishment range for a second degree felony when appellant's crime was a third degree felony. Therefore, the court affirmed the judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction for marihuana possession. The court held that the readiness of appellee, the state, for trial within the statutory time limit made appellant's trial speedy regardless of the trial date, the search of the marihuana field was valid under the open field doctrine despite the fence, and the trial court's inaccurate admonishment on the punishment range was harmless and did not make appellant's guilty plea involuntary.

 

1455 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Ford v. State


No. 09-83-151 CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Ninth District, Beaumont


676 S.W.2d 609; 1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 6285



June 6, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Jefferson County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment from the Jefferson County (Texas) trial court that convicted him of dispensing a controlled substance without a medical reason under the Texas Controlled Substances Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15, §§ 3.02(g) and 4.08(a)(1) (Supp. 1984). Appellant claimed that the indictment was defective, and that suppressed evidence, witnesses' testimony and a copy of a videotape were improperly admitted.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, an ophthalmologist who had weight control and drug treatment clinics, was convicted of unlawfully dispensing a controlled substance without a valid medical reason in violation of the Texas Controlled Substances Act (Act), Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15, §§ 3.02(g) and 4.08(a)(1) (Supp. 1984). On appeal, the court held that the recent amendments to the Act expressly proscribed appellant's conduct and that the indictment tracked the language of the statute. Thus, the indictment was not defective. Because there was nothing in the record to show what evidence was suppressed, and because appellant objected to witnesses' testimony before, but not after, the expected objectionable testimony was given, appellant did not preserve the issues on whether the suppressed evidence and the testimony were improperly admitted. Because the use of a copy of the videotape of a reporter's interview with appellant, rather than the original videotape, was introduced only at the punishment phase and did not contribute to the punishment, any error in its admission was harmless. Therefore, the court affirmed the judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction for dispensing a controlled substance without a medical reason. The court held that the statute proscribed appellant's conduct, that the indictment properly tracked the statutory language, that appellant's failure to identify suppressed evidence or to object to testimony after it was made precluded review of their admission, and that admission of a videotape copy did not affect the conviction or the punishment.

 

1456 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Daniels v. State


No. 3-83-150-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


674 S.W.2d 388; 1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 5614



May 30, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From the District Court of Burnet County, 33rd Judicial District No. 5884, Honorable D. V. Hammond, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the District Court of Burnet County, 33rd Judicial District (Texas), which convicted him of constructive delivery of marijuana under Texas Controlled Substances Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15, § 4.05 (d) & (e) (1976), and sentenced him to five years in prison.


OVERVIEW: After appellant was convicted of constructive delivery of more than one-fourth ounce of marijuana under the Texas Controlled Substances Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15, § 4.05 (d) & (e) (1976), and sentenced to five years in prison, appellant sought review. The court reversed conviction and remanded with instructions to dismiss the indictment. The trial court erred in overruling appellant's motion to quash the indictment. It was obvious that the trial court permitted the jury to convict appellant for actual delivery, either by his own conduct or as a party to actual delivery. Nowhere was the jury authorized to convict under the theory alleged in the indictment: constructive delivery. The manner and means of such transfer were not alleged. Appellant was left to guess or assume that appellee state was going to prove one or all of the types of conduct that would in legal, not statutory, construction constitute constructive transfer. An indictment on its face had to charge the offense in plain and intelligible words so as to enable a person of common understanding to know what was meant.


OUTCOME: The court reversed conviction and remanded because the trial court erred in overruling appellant's motion to quash an indictment and trial court permitted the jury to convict appellant for actual delivery, either by his own conduct or as a party to actual delivery, not the indictment theory of constructive delivery.

 

1457 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Gonzales v. State


No. 07-82-0328-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Seventh District, Amarillo


672 S.W.2d 618; 1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 5617



May 30, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From the District Court of Hockley County; 286th Judicial District; No. 2402; Honorable Frank B. Kiser Jr., Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant appealed a judgment from the 286th District Court, Hockley County, Texas, that convicted him of delivery of more than four ounces and less than five pounds of marihuana under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15, § 4.05(a) (Supp. 1982) and assessed punishment at three years confinement in the penitentiary under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15, § 4.05(b)(4) (Supp. 1982) and Tex. Penal Code § 12.33 (1974).


OVERVIEW: A jury convicted appellant of delivery of more than four ounces and less than five pounds of marihuana, in violation of Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15, § 4.05(a). On appeal, the court noted that the bill amending art. 4476-15, § 4.05(a) was found to be unconstitutional. Although the three-year sentence assessed was still within the range for either the pre- or post-amendment version of the statute, appellant was entitled to a new trial because the jury was erroneously instructed that the maximum punishment was greater than the law allowed and it assessed more than the minimum punishment available under a correct instruction. Appellant was not entitled to a limiting instruction on extraneous evidence, because he first placed the extraneous offenses into evidence. Two missing ounces from the quantity of marihuana did not break the chain of custody and preclude the admission of the remaining amount. The trial court did not err in refusing to permit appellant to question the officer on missing amounts from other seizures. It was remote from any significant issue in the case and would only distract the jury. The conviction was reversed and the case remanded.


OUTCOME: The court reversed appellant's conviction for delivery of marihuana and remanded to the trial court, because a bill elevating appellant's offense to a second-degree felony was found to be unconstitutional, and the jury was thus erroneously instructed that the maximum punishment was greater than the law allowed and it assessed more than the minimum punishment available under a correct instruction.

Saltarelli v. Saltarelli


No. 2-83-210-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Second District, Fort Worth


670 S.W.2d 785; 1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 5536



May 24, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From the 303rd District Court of Dallas County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant husband sought review of a decision of the 303rd District Court of Dallas County (Texas), granting a no fault divorce to appellee wife, pursuant to Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 3.01. Appellant argued that this statute was unconstitutional in that it offered no judicial protection for the institution of marriage.


OVERVIEW: Appellee wife was granted a no fault divorce under Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 3.01. Appellant husband alleged that § 3.01 violated his rights under U.S. Const. amend. XIV in that it offered no judicial protection for the institution of marriage. The court affirmed the trial court decision, thereby rejecting appellant's argument. The court found that the parties had been living apart and supporting themselves for 22 months before the divorce was granted. Appellee testified that the marriage had become insupportable and that there was no hope they could get back together. Appellant asserted that so long as one of the parties to the marriage was willing to work on resolving all problems until reconciliation was achieved, the divorce should not be granted. The court found that the fact appellant was willing to work at reconciliation did not mean there was a reasonable expectation that it would occur. The court held that the trial judge had sufficient evidence before him to determine that the statutory requirements for no fault divorce were met, and he did not abuse his discretion in granting the divorce.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a trial court judgment granting a no fault divorce to appellee wife. The court found that the trial judge had sufficient evidence before him to determine that the statutory requirements for divorce were met. The court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in granting the divorce.

Upon the hearing of the motion for revocation, the trial court found that appellant had violated a number of conditions of his probation and revoked his probation. He was sentenced to ten years in the Texas Department of Corrections. Appellant asserted that the action of the trial court in allowing the state to prove his probation record through the use of business records was error, in that the failure to have a witness with first-hand knowledge denied him his right of confrontation in cross-examination of the witnesses against him. The court held that the probation record was of such trustworthiness as to guarantee the same protection provided by the rights of confrontation and cross-examination. Appellant also asserted that it was error to revoke his probation for failure to report in that he had no driver's license. The court stated that there was no testimony which showed that appellant's failure to report was due to any difficulties in obtaining transportation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the ruling of the trial court which revoked appellant's probation. On appeal, the court stated that the probation record was of such trustworthiness as to guarantee the same protection provided by the rights of confrontation and cross-examination.

 

1460 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Lynch v. Port of Houston Authority


No. A14-83-610CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


671 S.W.2d 954; 1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 5607



May 24, 1984 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied June 14, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 152nd District Court of Harris County Trial Court No. 81-38520A.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, next of kin, challenged the order of the 152nd District Court of Harris County (Texas), which granted summary judgment to appellees, port authority and three employees, under the doctrine of sovereign immunity pursuant to the Texas Tort Claims Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6252-19, in a wrongful death action.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, next of kin, brought an action against appellees, port authority and three employees, based on the deaths of their relatives while working for appellees. The court affirmed summary judgment in favor of appellees, holding that they were immune under the doctrine of sovereign immunity. The court rejected the argument that the Texas Tort Claims Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6252-19 (act) violated the constitutional right to equal protection of the law. The court found no suspect class or fundamental right in the action, and the act met the test of being rationally related to a legitimate governmental purpose. The court found that Tex. Const. art. XVI, § 26, which provided that any person who committed homicide was liable for exemplary damages, did not support the action. Construing art. XVI, § 26 under the common law at the time it was adopted, the court found that the provision was not a waiver of sovereign immunity. Immunity was not impliedly waived by subsequent legislation because a waiver could only be made by unambiguous language. An argument that appellees were exercising proprietary functions failed because appellees performed only governmental functions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed summary judgment for appellees, port authority and three employees, against appellants, next of kin, in an action for the wrongful death of appellants' relatives because appellees were immune from suit under the doctrine of sovereign immunity. The applicable statutory authority for the finding of immunity did not violate constitutional rights to equal protection.

Showery v. State


No. 08-82-00280-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Eighth District, El Paso


678 S.W.2d 103; 1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 5564



May 23, 1984 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied July 3, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from 65th District Court of El Paso County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a jury verdict, handed down in the 65th District Court, El Paso County (Texas), convicting defendant of misapplication of fiduciary property over $ 200.00 in value, on the basis of which verdict defendant was sentenced to four years imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a physician, performed medical procedures on the victim, for which she paid in cash. Although defendant submitted health insurance claims for the victim and received full payment in insurance checks, he refused to remit the proceeds to her. He was charged with, and convicted of, having misapplied fiduciary property over $ 200.00 in value, and he appealed. The court affirmed the conviction. The court rejected defendant's claim that the evidence was insufficient to support the verdict, finding that the testimony of the victim and defendant's office staff, whom defendant had asked to lie for him, adequately supported the verdict. The court rejected a claim that certain expert testimony was improper because the grounds urged on appeal were not those raised at trial. The court also rejected defense arguments concerning evidentiary rulings and sustained the lower court's rulings concerning proposed jury charges. The court found no merit in defendant's constitutional challenge to the governing statute because the court found that the statute gave fair notice of proscribed conduct, as well as finding no merit in a constitutional challenge to the sentence as cruel and unusual.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed because the statute under which he was charged gave fair notice of the proscribed conduct. The verdict was adequately supported by testimony from the victim as well as from defendant's own employee, who testified that defendant asked her to lie for him. The court sustained the lower court's evidentiary rulings and found that the lower court's rulings concerning the jury charges also were correct.

Earle v. Program Centers of Grace Union Presbytery, Inc.


No. 2-83-077-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Second District, Fort Worth


670 S.W.2d 777; 1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 5532



May 23, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From the 16th District Court of Denton County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxing authority sought review of a judgment, entered on a jury verdict in the 16th District Court, Denton County (Texas), exempting appellee nonprofit group from liability for property taxes, based on the land's use for religious worship, pursuant to Tex. Const. art. VIII, § 2, and Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 11.20 (1982). The lower court had reversed earlier agency rulings exempting only one acre of the land from such taxes.


OVERVIEW: Appellant taxing authority imposed property taxes on land owned by appellee church group, and used by it for a retreat center. Appellee paid the taxes under protest, and asked for an appraisal review board hearing. When the board denied the exemption except for a one-acre portion thereof, appellee sought review in the trial court, and the lower court ruled that the land was wholly exempt from property taxes, pursuant to Tex. Const. art. VIII, § 2, and Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 11.20 (1982), because the land actually was used for religious worship. Appellant sought review, and the court reversed and remanded. Although the court rejected appellant's claim that the definition of "religious worship" was unconstitutionally broad, the court agreed with appellant that the lower court erred in its submission of special issues to the jury. First, the lower court failed to include both statutory prongs of the statutory test, which required "regular use" and "primary use." Second, the lower court incorrectly used the name of the retreat center instead of the name of the property owner in other special submissions. As a result of these errors, the court reversed and remanded.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's ruling granting a property tax exemption for land owned by appellee church group, based on a claim that it was used for religious worship. While it rejected appellant taxing authority's claim that the statutory definition of "religious worship" was unconstitutionally broad, the court agreed with appellant that the misidentification of the taxpayer, in special issues given to the jury, was reversible error.

Baptist Hospital of Southeast Texas, Inc. v. Baber


No. 09 83 203 CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Ninth District, Beaumont


672 S.W.2d 296; 1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 5763



May 10, 1984 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied June 7, 1984.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant hospital challenged a judgment of a trial court (Texas), which entered judgment in accordance with a jury verdict that held appellant and its doctor jointly and severally liable in a medical malpractice action brought by appellees, a widow and her child. Appellant argued that the trial court erred when it refused to limit damages on the grounds that Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4590i, § 11.02 (1984), was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellant hospital challenged a trial court judgment in a medical malpractice action brought by appellees, a widow and her child. In the action, appellees alleged professional negligence by appellant and its doctor caused the death of her husband and their father. Appellant hospital had filed a cross-action against its doctor. Prior to trial, the doctor stipulated his liability. A jury found appellant liable and awarded damages. The trial court granted appellees' motion for judgment and entered judgment in accordance with the jury verdict, holding appellant and its doctor jointly and severally liable. Appellant argued that the trial court erred in refusing to limit damages based on its ruling that Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4590i, § 11.02 (1984), was unconstitutional. OUTCOME: The judgment of the lower court was affirmed because under a restrained standard of review the legislative limitation on the right to recover in tort was unconstitutional as violating equal protection. The court held that the portions of the statute at issue unconstitutionally limited recovery for litigants with meritorious claims while doing the opposite for some seriously injured claimants.

 

1464 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


NUNLEY v. PAN AMERICAN LIVESTOCK EXPOSITION


MOTION NO. 18,575, NO. 13,579, NO. 13,700


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 5427



May 2, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 53RD JUDICIAL DISTRICT NO. 314,470, HONORABLE HARLEY CLARK, JUDGE PRESIDING


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a decision from the District Court of Travis County, 53rd Judicial District (Texas) that overruled his pleas of privilege to be sued in another county.


OVERVIEW: Appellee livestock shows initiated a declaratory relief action against appellant contending that Texas Animal Health Commission's rules regarding animal disease control applied to appellant. Pursuant to Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6252-13a, § 12, appellant asserted pleas of privilege to be sued in another county. The trial court overruled appellant's pleas of privilege. On appeal, the court affirmed the decision. The nonapplication of the Commission's rules to appellant came within the provisions of § 12, which provided that the validity of any rule may be determined in a declaratory judgment action in Travis County. Appellees claimed that the application of the rules against them and not appellant impaired their legal rights and threatened application of the rule, as required for § 12 claims. As such, the venue was properly fixed by § 12 in a Travis County court. In addition, appellant could be sued in Travis County pursuant to Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 2524-1, § 11.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision. Under a provision found in the Administrative Procedure Act, any declaratory action challenging the applicability of a rule was to be determined in a district court of Travis County. Such provision applied to appellee livestock shows' action challenging the nonapplicability of Animal Health Commission rules to appellant.

PAN AMERICAN LIVESTOCK EXPOSITION v. NUNLEY


MOTION NO. 18,575, NO. 13,807


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 5428



May 2, 1984

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant livestock shows filed a motion to dismiss their appeal of a decision from the District Court of Travis County, 53rd Judicial District (Texas) on the grounds that such appeal was moot.


OVERVIEW: Appellant livestock shows initiated an action for declaratory relief alleging that the Texas Animal Health Commission's rules regarding bovine brucellosis applied to appellee. Appellee filed a motion for summary judgment contending that the rules were unenforceable and invalid. The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of appellee finding that the rules were unconstitutional. Appellants challenged the decision. The rules were then expressly repealed and new rules were simultaneously adopted, so appellants filed a motion to dismiss their appeal as moot. On appeal, the court granted appellants' motion to dismiss. It would be a useless act for the court to affirm or reverse the trial court's decision because the administrative rules, upon which the decision was made, were no longer in existence. Appellants no longer needed to know whether the former rules were valid and applicable to appellee because the rules were specifically repealed.


OUTCOME: The court granted appellant livestock shows' motion to dismiss because the appeal was moot. The appeal was based upon a decision, which found that certain rules regarding animal disease control were unconstitutional. The rules were expressly repealed, so that there was no justiciable controversy.

In the Estate of Ross


No. 11-83-250-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Eleventh District, Eastland


681 S.W.2d 134; 1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 5408



April 26, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Eastland County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant daughters challenged an order from the probate court of Eastland County (Texas) that denied a motion to set aside an order admitting a will to probate and for new trial and that appointed appellee son independent executor of their father's will.


OVERVIEW: Decedent executed a new will that specifically excluded appellant daughters, left everything to appellee son, and appointed appellee independent executor. Appellee gave notice of probating the will, solely, by posting at the county courthouse as provided by Tex. Prob. Code Ann. § 128(a) (1980). The court affirmed the order that denied appellants' motion to set aside an order to probate decedent's will, for new trial, and that appointed appellee independent executor. There was no error committed when appellants' request for additional findings of fact and conclusions of law were refused, which related only to evidentiary issues, conflicted with the original findings and conclusions, or had no supporting evidence. The refusal to set aside the order of probate and to grant a new trial was not an abuse of discretion where appellants failed to allege a willingness to reimburse appellee for reasonable expenses that could be incurred. Thus, appellants failed to show that appellee would not have been injured by such order. Due process was satisfied by appellee's posting notice of the application for probate, when the will was produced, without personal notice to appellants.


OUTCOME: The order denying appellant daughters' motion to set aside an order admitting a will to probate and for a new trial and that appointed appellee son as independent executor was affirmed as there was no error when appellants' requested additional findings and conclusions were refused. Moreover, appellants failed prove that new trial would not injure appellee and that the posting of notice for probate at courthouse was sufficient personal notice.

Johnston v. State


Nos. 3-83-051-CR, 3-83-053-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


670 S.W.2d 394; 1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 5417



April 25, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From the District Court of Travis County, 147th Judicial District No. 66,437, Honorable Mace B. Thurman, Jr., Judge Presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sought review of the decision of the District Court of Travis County, 147th Judicial District (Texas), which found that appellants were guilty of possession of 200 pounds or less but more than 50 pounds of marihuana after appellants pled guilty to the charge and assessed punishment at five years' imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Appellants pled guilty to possession of marihuana of 200 pounds or less but more than 50 pounds of marihuana, pursuant to a plea agreement made with state. Appellants argued that they were erroneously admonished before their pleas of guilty were accepted. The court reversed and remanded for a new trial and held that the admonishment was erroneous. The court held that under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 26.13(c), the primary focus of admonishment was on substantial compliance by the court and not harmless error. The court held that state's offer to proceed on the lesser included offense and to recommend the minimum punishment of imprisonment for five years was generous and that the generosity of the offer and advisability of accepting the offer and pleading guilty was underscored by the erroneous admonishment concerning the punishment range. The court held that the error in admonishment was material to the voluntariness of appellants' guilty pleas and did not substantially comply with art. 26.13(a)(1).


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded appellants' convictions of possession of marihuana of 200 pounds or less but more than 50 pounds because the error in the trial court's admonishment as to the range of punishment was material to the voluntariness of the guilty pleas and did not substantially comply with statutory requirements.

 

1469 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Keller v. Judd


No. 04-83-00096-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourth District, San Antonio


671 S.W.2d 604; 1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 5378



April 18, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the 166th District Court of Bexar County Trial Court No. 81-CI-8166 Honorable James A. McKay, Judge Presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant vehicle seller challenged the judgment of the 166th District Court of Bexar County (Texas), rendered in favor of appellee vehicle buyer in appellee's action for breach of warranty and misrepresentation in the sale of a stolen automobile.


OVERVIEW: Appellant purchased a vehicle in a private sale and received a certificate of title from the state of Texas. Thereafter, appellant sold the vehicle to appellee buyer. It was determined that the vehicle had been stolen before it was sold to appellant. Appellee brought an action against appellant for breach of warranty and misrepresentation. The trial court entered judgment for appellee. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment and held that when the state of Texas issued a certificate of title under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art 6687-1 (Supp. 1984), it did not warrant title to the vehicle in the person named on the certificate. Thus, appellant was not entitled to rely on the information stated on the certificate of title. The court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying appellant's motion to bring a cross-action against the state of Texas because the cross-motion faced the legal hurdles of res judicata and sovereign immunity. Further, appellant's cross-action involve facts preceding appellant's transaction with appellee, namely the issuance of the certificate of title.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment rendered in favor of appellee vehicle buyer in his action against appellant vehicle seller for breach of warranty and misrepresentation in the sale of a stolen vehicle. The certificate of title issued by the state of Texas was not a warranty of vehicle ownership. Trial court's denial of joinder of state of Texas was not abuse of discretion because the cross-claim did not involve common issues of fact and law.

 

1470 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Huett v. State


Nos. 05-82-00834-CR, 05-82-00857-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


672 S.W.2d 533; 1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 5418



April 18, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From a District Court of Dallas County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought a review of a decision of the District Court of Dallas County, Texas, which convicted appellant of securities violations pursuant to Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 581-29(C)(1) (1984) and Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 581-4(F) (1984).


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged his conviction of securities fraud on constitutional and other grounds. The court affirmed appellant's conviction and found that Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 581-29(C)(1) (1984), when coupled with Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 581-4(F) (1984), was not unconstitutional vague because although the phrase, "material fact" in art. 581-4(F) was not elaborated upon by the statute, when considered in conjunction with art. 581-29(C)(1), which proscribed the use of fraud in the sales of securities, and when considered in light of the common understanding and practices in selling securities, a seller of securities would have been well aware that his three prior felony theft convictions, as was the case here, were material facts required to be disclosed to a prospective purchaser of the securities. The court found that although the revocation of appellant's probation pursuant to his three theft convictions was on appeal, appellant was not relieved of the duty to disclose his convictions to prospective purchasers because until that appeal was determined his probation still existed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction of securities fraud because the fraud statute was not unconstitutionally vague and appellant should have known that his three convictions for felony theft were material facts that needed to be disclosed to prospective purchasers.

 

1471 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Kerrville Independent School Dist. v. Southwest Texas Encampment Asso.


Appeal No. 04-82-00435-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourth District, San Antonio


673 S.W.2d 256; 1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 5376



April 18, 1984 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Granted in Part, Denied in Part May 16, 1984, Reported at: 673 S.W.2d 256 at 261.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 198th District Court of Kerr County Trial Court No. 79-252-B Honorable Merlin Johnson, Judge Presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant school district sought review of a judgment by the 198th District of Kerr County (Texas), which exempted properties owned by appellee church association from taxation. The judgment was based on jury findings that the properties were used as actual places of worship. Appellant challenged the constitutionality of the legislature's definition of worship and the sufficiency of evidence to support the jury findings.


OVERVIEW: Appellee church organization received land as a gift for purposes of establishing a religious camp. Appellee was unable to develop the entire tract of land, so appellee sold portions of the land. Appellant school district sought to tax the property retained by appellee. Based on a jury finding that the land was used as a place of worship, the trial court held that the property was tax exempt. Appellant sought review, asserting that the legislature's definition of worship was unconstitutional because it was overly broad. The court held that the definition set forth in Tex. Tax. Code Ann. § 1120(e) (1982), was constitutional. Appellant also contended in two points of error that the evidence was legally insufficient to support the jury findings. The court found that the evidence established that part of the land was used only to further the atmosphere of the rustic hill country, and was thus, not a place of worship. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment regarding that portion of the land being used as a place of worship, but reversed that portion of the judgment that provided for tax exempt status for the portion of property that was not being used for worship.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed part of the trial court judgment which held that the portion of land which was used by appellee church organization as a place of worship was exempt from taxes, because the legislative definition of worship was constitutional. The court reversed part of the judgment which held that the land used to further the atmosphere of the rustic hill country was tax exempt, because the land was not actually used as a place of worship.

 

1472 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Simpson v. State


No. 01-83-0368-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


668 S.W.2d 915; 1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 5365



April 12, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 228th District Court of Harris County, Texas Trial Court Cause No. 369,030.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a decision by the 228th District Court of Harris County (Texas), which found him guilty of possession of cocaine. Appellant claimed that the trial court's denial of his motion to suppress certain evidence was reversible error; that evidence was insufficient to support the jury's verdict; that the jury's verdict was coerced; and that his life sentence violated U.S. Const. amend. VIII.


OVERVIEW: Police officers observed a car parked in a dark stall of a car wash. The officer investigated and found appellant in the back seat apparently using cocaine. Cocaine was found in the car. A jury found appellant guilty of possession of cocaine, and upon finding enhancement allegations of two prior felony convictions to be true, assessed appellant's punishment at life imprisonment as required by Tex. Penal Code sec. 12.42(d). Appellant claimed that the trial court's denial of his motion to suppress certain evidence was reversible error. The court found that the officers took swift action predicated upon on-the-spot observations as permitted under the guidance of Terry, and overruled appellant's point of error. The court also found that there was sufficient evidence to support the jury's verdict and that the jury's verdict was not coerced by an Allen charge. The court also held that appellant's life sentence did not violate U.S. Const. amend VIII and the guidelines established by Solem. The court affirmed the judgment.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court which convicted appellant of possession of cocaine and imposed a life sentence was affirmed, because the evidence was lawfully obtained in a stop and frisk situation and the life sentence was not cruel and unusual.

 

1473 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Williams v. State


Appeal No. 04-83-00030-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourth District, San Antonio


670 S.W.2d 717; 1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 5344



April 11, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the 186th District Court of Bexar County Trial Court No. 81-SF-0044 Honorable James Barlow, Judge Presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant bail bond surety sought review of a decision by the 186th District Court of Bexar County (Texas), which granted remittitur to appellant in the amount of 85 percent of the bond appellant had issued for defendant, rather than the amount appellant requested under Tex. Rev. Stat. Ann. art. 2372p-3, § 13(b) (1984) of at least 95 percent, after having forfeited the entire bond for defendant's failure to appear.


OVERVIEW: After forfeiting a bail bond, appellant bail bond surety filed a request for a remittitur of at least 95 percent of the bond amount pursuant to Tex. Rev. Stat. Ann. art. 2372p-3, § 13(b) (1984), but the trial court denied his request and granted 85 percent remittitur instead. The court affirmed and found that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in issuing a smaller remittitur than required under § 13(b) because § 13(b) was an unconstitutional infringement on judicial power. The court found that Tex. Const. art. V, § 1 and Tex. Const. art. V, § 8 gave the judicial branch power over bail bond forfeitures and that the judiciary's power over bail bond forfeitures historically involved its exercise of discretion. The court held that the 95 percent minimum remittitur requirement of § 13(b) usurped that discretion over bail bond forfeitures in violation of Tex. Const. art. II, § 1 because it violated the separation of the judiciary from the legislature, and therefore the minimum mandatory remittitur infringed upon the judiciary's function. The court held that § 13(b) was unconstitutional insofar as it set a mandatory minimum percent for bail bond remittiturs.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed because the Texas constitution gave the judicial branch the power over bail bond forfeitures, which historically involved discretion, and the legislature's usurpation of that discretion by setting the mandatory bail bond remittitur of at least 95 percent violated the Texas constitution. The statutory minimum mandatory remittitur infringed upon the judiciary's function.

Scott v. State


No. 2-83-311-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Second District, Fort Worth


668 S.W.2d 901; 1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 5366



April 11, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From the 30th District of Wichita County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order of the 30th District Court of Witchita County (Texas) which revoked his probation and sentenced him to confinement.


OVERVIEW: Appellant plead guilty to the offense of sexual abuse of a child, Tex. Penal Code § 21.10, and was sentenced to a term in jail and a fine. The jail term was probated. Later, the state filed a motion to revoke appellant's probation, in which the state alleged that appellant had violated the law by having engaged in sexual abuse of a child. The court revoked appellant's probation. Appellant challenged the constitutionality of the statute under which he was charged and alleged that that statute violated U.S. Const. amend XIV, and Tex. Const. art. I, § 3(a) because it limited the promiscuity defense to heterosexual conduct. The child involved in the incident was of the same sex as the defendant. The court affirmed the judgment of the district court and held that the evidence was insufficient to support a promiscuity defense even if the appellant had been involved in heterosexual conduct, and appellant was without standing to challenge the statute's constitutionality on a sexual preference basis. The court found that the child was not shown to have engaged promiscuously in sexual intercourse.


OUTCOME: The judgement of the district court which revoked appellant's probation was affirmed because the evidence was insufficient to support the promiscuity defense which appellant wished to offer.

 

1475 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Lowry v. State


No. 05-83-00171-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


671 S.W.2d 601; 1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 5419



April 11, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM A DISTRICT COURT OF DALLAS COUNTY, TEXAS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from a District Court of Dallas County (Texas), which convicted defendant of criminal nonsupport.


OVERVIEW: The court reversed defendant's conviction for criminal nonsupport because it found that he was charged under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 25.05 (1974), which unconstitutionally shifted to defendant the burden of disproving an element of the offense. The court remanded to the trial court for a new trial under the prior statute, Tex. Penal Code Ann. art. 602 (1925). The court found § 25.05 denied defendant due process protection under U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Tex. Const. art. 1, § 19 because it allowed the trial court to charge the jury on both the elements of the offense and defendant's affirmative defense. The court found that the instructions were inherently contradictory and denied defendant due process because it shifted the burden of disproving an element of the offense to defendant. The court held that both the state and defendant could not carry the burden of proof regarding a single issue because it could confuse the jury and fail to accord due consideration to evidential matters relating to the affirmative defense.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded for a new trial because the statute that defendant was tried under was unconstitutional since it shifted the burden of disproving an element of the offense to defendant and resulted in a denial of due process under the Fourteenth Amendment.

 

1476 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Pullen v. Swanson


No. C14-82-853CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


667 S.W.2d 359; 1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 5295



April 5, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the 157th District Court of Harris County Trial Court No. 80-34778.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant promisee challenged the judgment from the 157th District Court of Harris County (Texas), which granted appellee executrix's motion to dismiss, striking appellant's pleadings and abating the action to collect on a series of promissory notes executed by the deceased. Appellant contended that the district court had original jurisdiction over the suit and, alternatively, that the motion was untimely filed and, therefore, waived.


OVERVIEW: The district court abated appellant's promisee's action in favor of appellee executrix. After a motion for rehearing, appellant contended that the district court had original jurisdiction over her litigation regarding the promissory notes that she sought to collect on from appellee executrix, who administered the deceased promisor's estate. In a substitute opinion, the court held that once the jurisdiction of the statutory probate court had attached and was adequate to grant the requested relief, the district court should have refrained from exercising its concurrent jurisdiction. Contrary to appellant's contention, the suit was definitely appertaining to or incident to an estate since it necessarily involved the assets of the estate. The court found that probate proceedings had been instituted in statutory probate court before the suit was filed in the district court and that the statutory probate court had subject matter jurisdiction over the cause of action. The court found that the plea was timely. The judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the district court. Appellant was incorrect about the jurisdiction of the district court, because proceedings had been instituted in statutory probate court before her suit was filed in the district court, so the statutory probate court had subject matter jurisdiction. The district court did not err when it abated the action in favor of appellee executrix.

GARCIA ORUE v. STATE


NO. 01-83-00418-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 5306



April 5, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] On Appeal from the 208th District Court of Harris County, Texas Trial Court Cause No. 349,683


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment from the 208th District Court of Harris County, Texas, which convicted appellant of delivery of more than 400 grams of cocaine.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of delivery of more than 400 grams of cocaine. The court remanded the case for resentencing because appellant was eligible for probation and received the minimum sentence permitted by law. The court held that the drug itself corroborated the offer to sell because it tended to connect appellant with the offense and made the testimony of the offeree, a police officer, more likely true than not. The court held that the evidence was sufficient to establish that the substance delivered was cocaine. The court found that the trial court did not err in considering the testimony of a chemist because the chemist was qualified as an expert witness and performed several tests that established that the substance was cocaine. The court determined that appellant was convicted under a valid statute that made delivery of cocaine a criminal offense punishable by imprisonment for a period of 5 to 99 years or life.


OUTCOME: The cause was remanded to the trial court for resentencing because appellant was eligible for probation and received the minimum sentence permitted by law. The drug itself tended to connect appellant with the offense of delivery of more than 400 grams of cocaine and the evidence was sufficient to establish that the substance delivered was cocaine.

Rodriguez v. State

March 29, 1984

CASE SUMMARY:

OVERVIEW: The court dismissed defendant's appeal of the guilty plea for possession of heroin because it found that defendant did not have a right to appeal under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 44.02 (1984). The court found that the trial court properly entered defendant's plea pursuant to the plea bargain agreement, assessed punishment that did not exceed that recommended by the state, and that defendant personally agreed to the plea bargain. The court held that under art. 44.02, defendant could not appeal his conviction because he had pled guilty to the offense, personally agreed to the plea bargain, and the punishment did not exceed the state recommendation. In addition, the court held that defendant did not plead guilty to an unconstitutional statute and dismissed defendant's appeal.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed defendant's appeal of the lower court's judgment entering his plea of guilty to the offense of possession of heroin because he had personally agreed to the plea bargain and the lower court had assessed punishment that did not exceed the state's recommendation.

Babcock v. State


No. 14,047


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


668 S.W.2d 857; 1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 5255



March 28, 1984 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied March 28, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the District Court of Travis County, 53rd Judicial District No. 340,730, Honorable Charles D. Mathews, Judge Presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mobile home installers sought review of the District Court of Travis County, 53rd Judicial District, Texas, which convicted appellants of violations of Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 911b (1964), the Motor Carrier Act, and imposed fines and injunctive relief. The trial court held that Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 5221f, § 18(f) (1982), the Texas Manufactured Housing Standards Act, was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellees, state and mobile home transit corporation, brought suit against appellant mobile home installers for violations of Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art 911b (1964), the Motor Carrier Act. The trial court convicted appellants and imposed fines and injunctive relief, holding that Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 5221f, § 18(f), the Texas Manufactured Housing Standards Act, was unconstitutional as it violated the provisions of art. 911b. The suit alleged that appellants transported mobile homes within the state without proper permits. The court held that the particular manner of regulation adopted in § 18(f) could not reasonably have been said to be foreign, unrelated, different, unconnected, separate, or inappropriate, in comparison to the broad expression contained in the title: regulation of the transportation of manufactured housing. How the state's regulation of such transportation was to be effectuated was merely a matter of detail that need not have been expressed in the title. The court held that the title of the act was in compliance with Tex. Const. Ann. art. III, § 35. The judgment of the trial court was reversed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's conviction of appellant mobile home installers. The court held that the section of the Texas Manufactured Housing Standards Act which was in conflict with the Motor Carrier Act, was not unconstitutional because the title of the Texas Manufactured Housing Standards Act was related to the subject of that statute.
