Las Vegas Pecan & Cattle Co. v. Zavala County


No. 04-83-00037-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourth District, San Antonio


669 S.W.2d 808; 1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 5259



March 28, 1984 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied May 1, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 38th District Court of Zavala County Trial Court No. 6339 Honorable Ben Martinez, Judge Presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowner sought review of a declaratory judgment from the 38th District Court, Zavala County, Texas, that rendered a verdict to appellee county after a bench trial, whereby appellant sought to enjoin appellee from interfering with appellant's attempt to close a purported private road, used by the public for more than 65 years, that ran through its property.


OVERVIEW: Appellant landowner sought a declaration that a road running through its property was a private road and sought to restrain appellee county from interfering with its attempt to close the road due to vandalism losses. The trial court found that the subject road, which ran approximately one and one-half miles, had been used by the public since 1911; and, therefore, entered judgment in favor of appellee, but did not issue findings of fact or conclusions of law. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment and overruled appellant's points of error. The court initially rejected appellant's contention that the trial court erred by not making findings of fact and conclusions of law because appellant, in failing to comply with Tex. R. Civ. P. 296 and 297, waived its rights to complain of any such omission. On the controlling issues, the court held that the evidence established that the public had used the road since 1911, and that appellee had maintained the road since about that time. As such, there was an implied public dedication of the road, which Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6812h (1982-83) did not prohibit, since that statute was enacted after the road became public.


OUTCOME: The declaratory judgment, in appellee county's favor, of appellant landowner's declaratory judgment action was affirmed, and appellant's 21 points of error were overruled, because there was sufficient evidence in the record to support the trial court's implied finding that, at the time of the lawsuit, the subject road had become a public road by implied dedication.

Reynolds v. Kessler


No. 08-82-00234-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Eighth District, El Paso


669 S.W.2d 801; 1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 5260



March 28, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from 205th District Court of El Paso County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant creditor appealed an order from the 205th District Court of El Paso County, Texas, which decreed a removal of the cloud of defendant's judgment lien from plaintiff deed holder's title to certain realty. The trial court also denied defendant's counterclaim for foreclosure of the lien. Defendant held that it's lien was valid and the trial court's judgment was therefore improper.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff deed holder and an individual were tenants in common of rental real estate. Plaintiff obtained a judgment against the individual and bought the individual's one-half interest in the property at the sale under execution. Defendant creditor obtained a judgment against the individual that was the tenant in common with plaintiff. Defendant's judgment was dated approximately three weeks before plaintiff received the deed to the property. Plaintiff filed suit to remove the cloud of the defendant's judgment lien from the property and defendant countersued for foreclosure. The trial court decreed a removal of the cloud and denied defendant's foreclosure. The court held that nowhere did the index reflect the names of plaintiff and defendant entered in the opposite columns, as statutorily required in the abstract. Therefore, neither the abstract nor the indexation complied with Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. arts. 5447 and 5448. The court held that no lien was created because the abstract of judgment was not properly filed and it was the proper registry of the abstract of judgment that would have created the lien. The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order that decreed the removal of the cloud of defendant creditor's judgment lien from plaintiff deed holder's title to real property. The court held that because the abstract of judgment was not properly indexed, that no lien had been created.

State v. Revco, D.S., Inc.


No. 05-83-00599-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


675 S.W.2d 219; 1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 5284



March 28, 1984 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied May 1, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: From a District Court of Dallas County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state sought review of a decision of a district court, Dallas County (Texas), which concluded that the Texas Blue Law, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 9001 (1982-1983) was unconstitutional and granted summary judgment in favor of appellee retailers.


OVERVIEW: Appellant state challenged the grant of summary judgment to appellee retailers and judgment that the Texas Blue Law was unconstitutional. The court reversed the judgment and remanded to the trial court for further proceedings. The only evidence offered by appellees was an expert's affidavit on the statute's effect on the Texas economy. The court held that the summary judgment evidence was insufficient as it failed to sustain as a matter of law the trial court's conclusions that the selection of merchandise regulated by the statute was arbitrary and capricious; that mere regulation of the sale of certain merchandise under the statute bore no rational relation to the promotion of a day of rest and failed to provide the Texas retail work force with a day of rest; and that the statute discriminated against retailers who sold merchandise regulated by the statute. The court found that the affidavit contained speculative statements, conclusions, and hearsay which were insufficient to support summary judgment and that the study's exclusion of merchants with fewer than 10 employees contradicted appellees' assertion that the study reflected the universe of retail establishments.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the grant of summary judgment to appellee retailers and remanded the case for further proceedings. The court held that the trial court erred in finding the Texas Blue Law unconstitutional as the evidence did not show as a matter of law that there was no reasonable relation between the statute and the health, welfare, and recreation of the state's people, and the affidavit contained speculations, conclusions, and hearsay.

Baggett v. State


No. 09-83-027 CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Ninth District, Beaumont


673 S.W.2d 908; 1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 5565



March 28, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Jefferson County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Jefferson County Court at Law (Texas), which convicted him of intentionally and knowingly possessing a package of imported redfish and speckled sea trout which were not identified as to its contents and that he refused inspection of the products. Defendant was fined and sentenced to 30 days in jail.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with one count each of knowingly possessing a package of imported Speckled Sea Trout and a package of imported redfish, which contents were not identified as required by Tex. Parks & Wild. Code Ann. § 66.201(h) (1984). Defendant was also charged with refusing to allow inspection of aquatic products in the possession of a wholesale fish dealer under Tex. Parks & Wild. Code Ann. § 47.037 (1976) and was assessed a fine and sentenced to 30 days in jail by the trial court. The court reversed. The court held that Tex. Const. art. Const. art. III, § 36, was not violated as the caption to the statute gave fair notice regarding the matters and penalties included therein. The court, however, concluded that defendant was denied reasonably effective assistance of trial counsel as guaranteed by U.S. Const. amend. VI, U.S. Const. amend. XIV, and Tex. Const. art. I, § 10, due to the cumulative effects of 40 alleged deficiencies cited by defendant regarding his defense.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment, holding that defendant had been denied reasonably effective assistance of counsel based on the numerous alleged errors cited by defendant regarding his representation.

 

1484 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Morrison v. Chan


No. 2-83-050-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Second District, Fort Worth


668 S.W.2d 483; 1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 5235



March 22, 1984 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied April 19, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the 17th District Court of Tarrant County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant administratrix sought review of a decision of the 17th District Court, Tarrant County (Texas), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellees, physician and other treatment providers, in appellant's medical malpractice suit.


OVERVIEW: Before her death, a patient filed suit for medical malpractice against appellees, physician and other treatment providers. Appellees were granted summary judgment due to the limitations statute, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4590i, § 10.01 (1984). Appellant administratrix continued the decedent's challenge. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, holding that appellant's claim was barred by the limitations statute. The court rejected appellant's contention that the limitation period began running when the decedent suffered "legally cognizable damage" as there was no basis in the record for the assertion that the injury did not occur earlier. The court interpreted art. 4590i, § 10.01 to mean that the limitations would begin to run from the date of the occurrence of a tort or breach or the date of the treatment's completion. The court held that "breach" or "tort" were used designate the act or omission on which the claim was founded, rather than the accrual of a right to a judicial remedy, because using the occurrence of a more readily ascertainable act or omission clarified the determination of the time from which the limitations began running on a health care claim.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment, finding that the limitations statute barred the medical malpractice claim of appellant administratrix because notice of the claim was given more than two years after the completion of the treatment and more than two years from any breach of duty on the part of appellees, physician and other treatment providers.

Ford v. State


No. 6-83-033-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Sixth District, Texarkana


668 S.W.2d 477; 1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 5230



March 20, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the County Court at Law of Comal County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the County Court at Law, Comal County, Texas, which denied his motion to dismiss and to quash the complaint on speedy trial grounds and that the speeding statute was unconstitutional, and convicted defendant for speeding.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of speeding after he was charged with driving 72 miles per hour in a 55 miles per hour speed zone. Defendant appealed his conviction because he contended he was denied a speedy trial and the statute on which the conviction was based was unconstitutional. The court affirmed and held that defendant had waived his speedy trial motion by filing the motion and then failing to pursue it. The court found that Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art 6701d, §§ 166 and 169B allow the State Highway Commission to set speed limits that were reasonable and prudent for the state and to consider certain enumerated factors in setting those limits. One of the factors permitted was the loss of federal highway funds if the speed limit was set above 55 miles per hour. Defendant challenged this economic factor as not rationally related to public safety considerations, and therefore not rationally connected to a reasonable and prudent speed, making his conviction a due process violation. The court, however, found that safety considerations were not the only reasonable and prudent considerations contemplated by the statutes, but other considerations were part of the public welfare as well.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court because defendant filed but never pursued his motion for a speedy trial, thereby waiving the motion, and the presumption that defendant's speed in excess of the posted speed limit was unreasonable and imprudent did not infringe upon defendant's due process rights.

 

1486 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Flores v. State


No. A14-82-570-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


681 S.W.2d 94; 1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 5220



March 15, 1984 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied April 12, 1984. Discretionary Review Granted November 21, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from 10th District Court of Galveston County Cause No. 38,375.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment of the 10th District Court of Galveston County (Texas), which found him guilty of murder and assessed punishment at life imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: A jury found appellant guilty of murder and assessed punishment at life imprisonment. The trial court found in its judgment that a deadly weapon, a handgun, was used and exhibited during the commission of the offense. On appeal, the court reformed and corrected the judgment by deleting the trial court's finding that a deadly weapon was used and exhibited during the commission of the offense. As reformed, the court affirmed the judgment. The court held that evidence revealed that four men conspired to burglarize a home, that appellant entered the home for that purpose, and that the victim was shot during the burglary. The court found evidence of appellant's guilt connecting him with the commission of the crime. The court held that the trial court found that a handgun was used and exhibited during the commission of the offense, but not by appellant. The trial court erred in this finding because the jury was the exclusive judge of the facts, but the error was harmless because the finding did not activate any penalty provoking provisions against appellant.


OUTCOME: The court reformed and corrected the judgment by deleting the trial court's finding that a deadly weapon, a handgun, was used and exhibited during the commission of the offense. As reformed, the court affirmed the judgment. The court held that the uncontradicted evidence revealed that four men conspired to burglarize the home, that appellant entered the home for that purpose, and that the victim was shot during the burglary.

STEWART v. STATE


No. B14-83-203-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 5224



March 15, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Appeal from the 232nd District Court of Harris County Trial Cause No. 366,361


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the 232nd District Court of Harris County (Texas), which convicted him for illegally manufacturing methamphetamine in violation of the Controlled Substances Act, Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 4476-15, § 403(d)(1) (Supp. 1982-1983), imposed probated incarceration, and assessed a fine of $ 4,000.


OVERVIEW: After appellant was convicted and fined for manufacturing methamphetamine, he appealed arguing that (1) the evidence was insufficient to support his conviction; (2) the Controlled Substances Act, Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 4476-15, § 403(d)(1) (Supp. 1982-1983) was unconstitutional; and (3) the search was invalid. Based upon a written stipulation of the evidence, the court found that an emergency existed, thus the officer's entry into appellant's apartment was authorized, and the search was valid. Further, the court found that there was sufficient evidence to support appellant's conviction, and nothing was presented for review with regard to appellant's last ground of error. However, the court concluded that the imposition of a fine in this case was improper, therefore the judgment was reformed. Accordingly, as reformed, the judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was reformed to delete the trial court's unauthorized fine of $ 4,000 because, while appellant's conviction was valid under the Controlled Substances Act, the statute did not authorize the assessment of a fine in addition to confinement for a first degree felony. As reformed, the judgment was affirmed.

Knighton v. State


No. 01-82-0057-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


666 S.W.2d 386; 1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 5161



March 8, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from County Criminal Court at Law No. 6 of Harris County Trial Court Cause Number 631,233.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his conviction, in the County Criminal Court at Law No. 6, Harris County (Texas), for the offense of exhibiting obscene materials.


OVERVIEW: A jury convicted appellant of the offense of exhibiting obscene materials consisting of two motion picture films. On review, the court reversed appellant's conviction. In finding the evidence insufficient to support appellant's conviction, the court held that, based upon a review of the facts, it was not clear that appellant saw the seized films or knew of their "obscene content and character." The court explained that the state was required to prove more than appellant's "exhibition" of the films, particularly when the record showed that appellant did not maintain a strict vigilance over the projector's sight and sound. Furthermore the court held that the trial court erroneously charged the jury as to the patent offensiveness of the alleged "representation of actual or simulated acts of oral sodomy and sexual intercourse," thereby assuming and instructing the jury as to a requisite element of the offense. The court remanded the case to the trial court for entry of a judgment of acquittal.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment, holding that the evidence was insufficient to support the conviction and that the trial court erred in a jury charge which, as provided, assumed and instructed the jury as to a requisite element of the offense. The court remanded the case and instructed the trial court to enter a judgment of acquittal.

Wilson v. State

OVERVIEW: Appellants were tried together and convicted of engaging in the organized criminal activity of conspiring to manufacture amphetamine. Appellants sought review of the convictions. Appellants contended that their convictions must be reversed because the trial court instructed the jury that it could assess punishment of up to 99 years or life imprisonment in the Texas Department of Corrections and a fine of up to $ 10,000. Texas Conference Asso. of Seventh-Day Adventists v. Leander Independent School Dist.


No. 13,779


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


669 S.W.2d 353; 1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 5148



March 7, 1984 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied April 18, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF WILLIAMSON COUNTY, 26TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT NO. 78-158-C, HONORABLE WILLIAM S. LOTT, JUDGE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant association challenged a decision from the District Court of Williamson County, 26th Judicial District (Texas), rendering judgment non obstante veredicto in favor of appellee school district, in appellant's action seeking a declaratory judgment to determine whether any part of certain real property qualified for exemption from ad valorem taxes under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 7150, § 2a and Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 11.19, 11.20.


OVERVIEW: The trial court, in an ad valorem tax suit, rendered judgment non obstante veredicto in favor of appellee school district. Appellant association's suit sought a declaratory judgment to determine whether all or any part of certain real property, a ranch, qualified for exemption from ad valorem taxes. The trial court ruled that several special issues answered favorably to appellant were either immaterial or unsupported by the evidence. The trial court decreed that the ranch was not exempt from taxation under neither Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 7150, § 2a nor Tex. Tax. Code Ann. § 11.19, 11.20. The court overruled appellant's contention that the trial court erred in failing to render judgment that the entire ranch was tax exempt for 1980 under § 11.19. The court otherwise affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court reformed the judgment of the trial court that appellant association's property was not exempt from taxation; the property was exempt from ad valorem taxation during the years 1977-79, and a portion of the property was exempt from ad valorem taxation from January 1, 1980 until the trial's conclusion.

 

1491 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Yorko v. State


No. A14-83-442CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


681 S.W.2d 633; 1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 5142



March 1, 1984 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Discretionary Review Granted October 17, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 7 of Harris County Trial Court No. 667,746.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 7 of Harris County (Texas), in which he was convicted of possession with intent to sell of a dildo, an obscene device under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 43.23(c)(1) (1977). Appellant contended that Tex. Penal Code Ann. §§ 43.23(a) and 43.23(c)(1) (1977) both were unconstitutional as violative of the right to privacy.


OVERVIEW: On review, appellant asserted that he was entitled to reversal because his conviction under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 43.23(c)(1) (1977) was invalid as a violation of the right to privacy guaranteed under U.S. Const. amend. XIV and as an example of the excessive use of police power under the Texas Constitution. The appellate court rejected appellant's assignments of error and affirmed, holding that the right of citizens to possess obscene materials in their homes did not create a right to sell that material publicly. The appellate court accordingly found that the legislature had not exceeded its police power mandate in making commercial distribution of dildoes, defined as a obscene device, a criminal offense. The appellate court concluded that neither of the statutory provisions cited by appellant were unconstitutional, noting that there was no need to prove whether appellee state had a compelling state interest in banning the sale of such obscene devices because appellee had a long recognized legitimate interest in regulating the use of obscene material in local commerce and in places of public accommodation.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed appellant's conviction, finding that appellant, despite having a right to possess obscene materials in his own home, had no constitutionally protected right to make a commercial sale of sexual devices properly determined to be obscene. Appellee state had a legitimate interest in regulating the commercial distribution of obscene material in public places.

 

1492 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Fuentes v. State


No. C14-83-252-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


681 S.W.2d 91; 1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 5172



March 1, 1984 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Discretionary Review Granted October 31, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 182nd District Court of Harris County Cause No. 364,110.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment of the 182nd District Court of Harris County (Texas), which convicted him of possession with intent to deliver cocaine pursuant to the Controlled Substances Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15, § 4.03(c), where appellant argued that House Bill 730 was unconstitutional and that the trial court erred by accepting appellant's nolo contendere plea and by overruling his motion to suppress the evidence.


OVERVIEW: Appellant pleaded nolo contendere to possession with intent to deliver cocaine. Thereafter, appellant sought review, contending that House Bill 730 was unconstitutional and that the trial court erred by accepting his plea, which was conditioned upon the right to appeal matters raised by motion prior to the time of trial, and by overruling his motion to suppress the evidence. On review, the court affirmed the conviction. The court ruled that although House Bill 730 was unconstitutional, the prior act remained in full force and effect. Thus, under the prior act, possession of cocaine was an offense, and appellant's punishment was within the prior act's punishment range. The court found that the trial court did not err by accepting appellant's nolo contendere plea, because there was nothing in the record that showed that appellant entered his plea in reliance upon any defined agreement with the trial court giving him a right to appeal. Therefore, appellant was bound by his confession. The court also ruled that, based on his confession, appellant had waived any error regarding the trial court erroneously admitting evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for possession with intent to deliver cocaine. The court ruled that while certain legislation was unconstitutional, the prior act remained in full force and effect and, thus, possession of cocaine was an offense. The court also ruled that there was no showing that appellant had entered his plea in reliance upon any defined agreement with the trial court giving him a right to appeal.

 

1493 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Sanchez v. State


No. 3-83-177-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


666 S.W.2d 659; 1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 5133



February 29, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From the District Court of Lampasas County, 27th Judicial District No. 5211, Honorable C. W. Duncan, Jr., Judge Presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment of the District Court of Lampasas County, 27th Judicial District (Texas), which convicted him of delivery of an amount of marihuana weighing five pounds or less but more than four ounces, where appellant contended that the trial court erred in instructing the jury in regard to the range of punishment which could be imposed.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of delivery of an amount of marihuana weighing five pounds or less but more than four ounces. Prior to sentencing, the trial court instructed the jury that because the current conviction was of a second-degree felony and appellant had previously been convicted of a felony, the jury could assess punishment as that of a first-degree felony, namely, confinement for life or for any term of not more than 99 years or less than five years. Thereafter, the jury assessed punishment at confinement for 15 years. Appellant then sought review, regarding the trial court's instruction. On review, the court, in view of case precedent, reversed and remanded the cause for a new trial. The court found that the jury was incorrectly instructed in regard to the minimum range of punishment and that such instruction was reversible error. The court noted that the offense constituted a third-degree felony and that, applying the prior conviction, the range of punishment for the offense was that specified for a second-degree felony, that is, confinement for a term of not more than 20 years or less than two years.


OUTCOME: The court reversed appellant's conviction for delivery of an amount of marihuana weighing five pounds or less but more than four ounces and remanded the cause for a new trial. The court ruled that the trial court's instruction to the jury regarding the range of punishment was incorrect in that the minimum range of punishment was higher than it should have been for the offense charged and, thus, such error required reversal.

Mejia v. State


Nos. C14-83-498-CR, C14-83-499-CR, Consolidated


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


681 S.W.2d 88; 1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 5112



February 23, 1984 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied March 22, 1984. Discretionary Review Refused October 31, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from County Criminal Court at Law No. 4 of Harris County Cause Nos. 716,891 and 716,892.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sought review of an order from the County Criminal Court at Law, Harris County, Texas, which denied habeas corpus relief to appellants and refused to discharge them from prosecution for intentionally and knowingly causing game roosters to fight in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 42.11(a)(6). Appellants claimed that § 42.11(a)(6) did not prohibit cockfighting and that § 42.11(a)(6) was unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: Appellants were charged with intentionally and knowingly causing game roosters to fight in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 42.11(a)(6). The trial court denied their petition for habeas corpus relief and refused to discontinue their prosecution. On review, appellants claimed that § 42.11(a)(6) did not prohibit cockfighting because the statute referred to animals, not fowl, and that it was otherwise was unconstitutionally vague. The court reviewed various revisions to the penal code statutes regarding animal cruelty and found that the revisions merely consolidated many scattered statutes into a workable scheme that was enacted to protect animals. The court held that for purposes of § 42.11(a)(6), the term "animal" included fowl. The court also held that § 42.11(a)(6) was not unconstitutionally vague because the term "animal" as defined in § 42.11 and the phrase "causing one animal to fight with another" were clear and unambiguous. Finally, the court held that the proposed testimony of appellants' witness, who offered his opinion on the legality of cockfighting, was irrelevant and immaterial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court that denied each appellant the requested discharge from further prosecution. The court held that the animal cruelty statute, under which appellants were prosecuted, was not unconstitutionally vague. The court also held that for purposes of that statute, fowl were included within the definition of the term animal.

 

1495 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Develo-cepts, Inc. v. City of Galveston


No. B14-83-302-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


668 S.W.2d 790; 1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 5054



February 16, 1984 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied March 15, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 122nd District Court of Galveston County Cause No. 120,665.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant corporation sought review of an order of the 122nd District Court of Galveston County (Texas), that dismissed appellant's cause of action against appellee municipality over appellee's denial of a specific use permit for a group home. The trial court held that appellant lacked standing to sue.


OVERVIEW: Appellant corporation brought an action for a declaratory judgment, injunctive relief and for damages caused by appellee municipality when it denied a specific use permit for property that appellant wanted to lease for a group home. The trial court held that appellant lacked standing to sue and the court affirmed. The court found that zoning determinations relate solely to real estate and its use and not to who owns or intends to occupy it. One had to have a legal right that was breached to have standing to seek redress for an injury. Without an interest in the property, appellant had no legal right to be breached and no standing to challenge zoning decisions. Appellant also claimed that it was entitled to bring suit as a person injured under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 5547-300, § 3(26). The court held that the statute clearly restricted recovery to mentally retarded persons and to those entitled to bring suit in their behalf pursuant to Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 5547-300, § 64(a), (d). A corporation was not listed in those sections, and was not entitled to recovery. Finally, appellant could not assert the legal interests of others to obtain relief for its own injury.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that held that appellant corporation lacked standing to sue because appellant had no contractual or property interest in the property that was affected by appellee municipality's zoning decision, had no standing in its own right to sue, and had no standing to represent the mentally retarded people who might have lived in the group home.

 

1496 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Moreno v. State


No. B14-83-278-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


668 S.W.2d 784; 1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 5076



February 16, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the 179th District Court of Harris County Cause No. 364,292.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant was convicted of the felony offense of possession of methaqualone with intent to deliver in the 179th District Court of Harris County (Texas). The punishment was five years confinement. At issue on appeal was the conviction's validity under the Controlled Substances Act, as amended by House Bill 730, 67th Leg., 1981, ch. 268. Under H.B. 730 the offense constituted an aggravated offense punishable by life or any lesser term of years.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of possession of methaqualone with intent to deliver. The punishment was five years confinement. Appellant challenged the validity of a conviction under the Controlled Substances Act as amended by House Bill 730, 67th Leg., 1981, Ch. 268. The court affirmed the conviction, but remanded for appropriate punishment. Methaqualone was listed in Penalty Group 3, pursuant to Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15, § 4.02(d)(2) (1982-1983). Under H.B. 730 such was punishable by life or any lesser term and a fine. On motion of the state, the charge was reduced as to the amount of the substance possessed, which was still an aggravated offense punishable by life or any lesser term and a lower fine. H.B. 730 was unconstitutional, but the Controlled Substances Act should have stood as though H.B. 730 had never been enacted. Prior to the passage of H.B. 730, possession of such substance with intent to deliver was a felony, and possession alone was a Class A misdemeanor. The allegation of the indictment was sufficient to allege the misdemeanor. The trial court had jurisdiction of the offense alleged, so it also had jurisdiction over any lesser-included offense.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment as reformed, so the judgment reflected, instead of a finding that appellant was adjudged guilty of "a felony," that the offense of which appellant was convicted was "a misdemeanor." As the trial court had jurisdiction of the offense alleged, it also had jurisdiction over any lesser included offense. The court remanded the matter to the trial court for the assessment of punishment in accordance with the statute.

Drummond v. State


No. B14-83-245CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


675 S.W.2d 545; 1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 5026



February 9, 1984 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Discretionary Review Refused July 18, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 10 Harris County, Trial Court No. 663,955.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 10, Harris County (Texas), which convicted him of promoting obscenity and assessed him a fine.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was found guilty of promoting obscenity and appealed his conviction arguing that the trial court erred in denying his request for a statement of facts due to his inability to pay. Appellant also argued insufficiency of the evidence as well as the constitutionality of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 43.21 and § 43.23 (1974). The court noted that the trial court had ample evidence upon which to base its denial of his petition for indigent status. The court noted that he made sufficient money to pay his legal fees and that the appeal was actually being pursued by appellant's employer. The court also found that, without the statement of facts they had to assume that there was sufficient evidence to support the verdict and the finding that the material depicted simulated sexual intercourse and sodomy. The court further held that the actual jury instruction given to the jury tracked the wording of appellant's request, therefore he could not later argue error. The court finally held that the word "decency" actually stated a common meaning of what governed current community standards and therefore the statute was constitutional. The court then affirmed the judgment.


OUTCOME: Appellant's conviction for promoting obscenity was affirmed because there was ample evidence to support the denial of his indigency petition, there was sufficient evidence to support the conviction, and the statute in question was constitutional because the word "decency" stated a common meaning of what governed current community standards for obscenity.

COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 4987



February 1, 1984

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mobile home carriers challenged the ruling of the District Court of Travis County (Texas) which convicted appellants of violations of the Motor Carrier Act and imposed upon them fines and injunctive relief.


OVERVIEW: Appellee state and appellee mobile home transit alleged in their suit that appellants had by various acts effectuated the transportation of mobile homes upon public highways and between incorporated areas of the state without official authority in the form of a permit or a certificate of convenience and necessity. Appellants contended that they were legally excused from obtaining a permit or a certificate of convenience and necessity based on provisions of the Texas Manufactured Housing Standards Act. OUTCOME: The court reversed the ruling of the trial court which held that appellants had violated the Motor Carrier Act by transporting motor homes without a permit. On review, the court held that appellants' reliance on the Texas Manufacturing Housing Standards Act was not misplaced and the title of the statute was in compliance with the Texas Constitution.

College Station v. Turtle Rock Corp.


No. C14-82-895-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


666 S.W.2d 318; 1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 4955



January 26, 1984 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied February 23, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 272nd District Court of Brazos County Cause No. 23,446.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review of the judgment from the 272nd District Court of Brazos County (Texas), which granted appellee real estate development corporation's motion for summary judgment and declared appellant's park land dedication ordinance unconstitutional as a violation of Tex. Const. art. 1, § 17.


OVERVIEW: Appellant city challenged a judgment that declared appellant's park land dedication ordinance unconstitutional as a violation of Tex. Const. art. 1, § 17. The ordinance's stated purpose was to provide recreational areas in the form of neighborhood parks as a function of subdivision development. Appellee real estate developer elected to pay monies in lieu of dedicating the required amount of land. The court affirmed, holding that the ordinance unquestionably sanctioned an unconstitutional taking of private property for public use. Appellant was a home rule city that enjoyed full power of self government and enabling statutes operated only as limitations to that authority. The court held that Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 1175, § 15, specified the procedure for exercising power and it did not allow appellant to acquire land for parks under its police power. The parks did not benefit the general public and did not bear a substantial relation to the safety and health of the community under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 1175. The ordinance violated Tex. Const. art. 1, § 17, because it required a dedication of land, or money paid in lieu thereof, as a prerequisite to plat approval.


OUTCOME: The judgment granting appellee real estate development corporation's motion for summary judgment and declaring appellant city's park land dedication ordinance unconstitutional was affirmed, because appellant's park land dedication ordinance was an unconstitutional taking of private property for public use that was not authorized by appellant's police power.

 

1500 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


McElroy v. State


No. 05-83-00036-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


667 S.W.2d 856; 1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 4968



January 23, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From a District Court of Dallas County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought to overturn a judgment of the District Court of Dallas County (Texas), which convicted appellant for misapplication of funds. Appellant asserted error on nine different grounds, including insufficiency of the evidence.


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged his conviction for misapplication of construction trust funds, raising nine different grounds for relief. The court reversed his conviction on insufficient evidence grounds and remanded his case with instructions to enter an order of acquittal. The prosecution arose when one of appellant's business checks bounced, and it was revealed that appellant used that account for both personal and business expenses. The court held that appellee state government had failed to prove that appellant knew that certain checks used by appellant for private purposes came out of funds earmarked for workers and construction materials. In addition, appellee failed to prove that certain payments made by appellant were unrelated to the construction project itself. Since it was appellee's burden to prove beyond a reasonable doubt that appellant acted with the intent of defrauding others, its evidence was legally insufficient. Accordingly, appellant's conviction was ordered set aside.


OUTCOME: The judgment convicting appellant for misapplication of funds was reversed, because there was insufficient evidence of his intent to defraud. The case was remanded with instructions that the lower court enter a judgment of acquittal.

 

1501 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Cessna Finance Corp. v. Morrison


No. 01-83-0204-CV


Court of Civil Appeals of Texas, First District, Houston


667 S.W.2d 580; 1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 4882



January 19, 1984 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied February 16, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from Probate Court No. 2 of Harris County, Texas Trial Court Cause No. 168,688.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant secured creditor challenged an order of the Probate Court No. 2, Harris County (Texas), which classified appellant's claim against an estate as a preferred debt and lien claim, and which granted appellee estate administrator summary judgment on appellee's counterclaim for usury.


OVERVIEW: Appellant secured creditor brought an action against appellee estate administrator after appellee rejected appellant's claim against the estate. The trial court granted judgment to appellant but classified its claim as a preferred debt and lien claim under Tex. Prob. Code Ann. § 306. The trial court also granted judgment to appellee on a counterclaim of usury. Appellant sought review. The court found that because appellant's claim was not timely presented within the meaning of Tex. Prob. Code Ann. § 306(b), and appellant failed to amend its claim in response to appellee's objections, the probate court was authorized to treat appellant's claim as a preferred debt and lien against the specific property used as security for the debt on which the claim was based. The court also found, however, that the underlying transaction was governed by Kansas law and was exempt from the Kansas usury statute. Accordingly, the court affirmed the classification of appellant's claim as a preferred debt and lien claim but reversed the award of damages against appellant on appellee's counterclaim for usury.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed that part of the trial court's decision classifying appellant secured creditor's claim as a preferred debt and lien claim against the specific property given as security for the debt on which the claim was based, reversed summary judgment on appellee estate administrator's counterclaim for usury, and rendered judgment that appellee take nothing against appellant on said counterclaim.

 

1502 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Hayes v. State


No. 09-83-051 CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Ninth District, Beaumont


672 S.W.2d 246; 1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 5776



January 11, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Jefferson County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed judgment from a Jefferson County trial court (Texas), convicting defendant of the misdemeanor offense of unlawfully carrying a weapon pursuant to Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 46.02.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of unlawfully carrying a weapon pursuant to Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 46.02. Defendant appealed his conviction and contended that Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 46.02(6)(B), which defined "illegal knife" was so vague and indefinite that it violated his constitution right to know the nature and cause of the accusation against him as guaranteed by Tex. Const. art. I, § 10. The reviewing court held that the statute was not unconstitutionally void for vagueness and that it is not so indefinite so as to deprive a person of due process of law. The statute was written clearly, in precise and definite terms and aptly described what instruments constituted illegal knives. The statutory language was easily comprehendible and a person of ordinary intelligence had adequate notice of what conduct was proscribed by the statute. Defendant's ignorance of the law did not excuse his violation. Defendant's contention that a police officer's testimony as to prior trouble with appellant constituted evidence of an extraneous offense was without merit. Because defendant failed to support his fourth ground of error it was not preserved for review. Judgment of conviction was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Judgment convicting defendant of unlawfully carrying a weapon was affirmed. The statute against carrying unlawful weapons was not so indefinite that it deprived persons of due process of law and defendant's ignorance of the statute did not excuse his violation.

 

1503 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Forte v. State


No. 2-84-012-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Second District, Fort Worth


683 S.W.2d 145; 1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 6887



January 10, 1984 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] The Document Reported at this Citation has been Withdrawn from the Bound Volume.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM COUNTY CRIMINAL COURT NO. 5 OF TARRANT COUNTY


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the County Criminal Court No. 5 of Tarrant County (Texas), which found defendant guilty by a jury of driving while intoxicated, in violation of Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6701L-1(b) (Supp. 1984). The court assessed punishment at 30 days confinement and a fine.


OVERVIEW: A jury found defendant guilty of driving while intoxicated, and defendant appealed. The appellate court reversed and remanded because defendant was improperly denied a limited right to counsel prior to making a decision as to whether to take an intoxilyzer examination. The court found that Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6701L-1(a)(2)(B) (Supp. 1984)was not an impermissible conclusive presumption that violated the federal or state constitutions. The statute did not violate the "fair notice" standard, and was not unconstitutionally vague or overbroad. However, the trial court erred in admitting evidence of the results of an intoxilyzer test which was administered after appellant had requested and been denied the presence of counsel. The court found that the error was clearly not harmless, and mandated reversal. The court thereafter examined defendant's challenge to the sufficiency of the evidence because a challenge to the sufficiency of the evidence, if sustained, barred a retrial. However, the court found that there was sufficient evidence to support his conviction for driving while intoxicated, without regard to the evidence concerning the challenged intoxilyzer test results.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for driving while intoxicated was reversed and remanded because defendant was improperly denied a limited right to counsel prior to making a decision as to whether to take an intoxilyzer examination. There was a reasonable possibility that the evidence complained of might have contributed to the conviction or affected the punishment assessed, therefore, the error was not harmless, and mandated reversal.

 

1504 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Smith v. Cornelius


No. 05-83-00425-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


665 S.W.2d 182; 1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 4868



January 4, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From a District Court of Dallas County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff mother challenged a judgment from a District Court of Dallas County (Texas) that granted defendant father summary judgment in plaintiff's suit to establish the parent-child relationship between her son and defendant. The trial court determined that plaintiff's suit was time barred under Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 13.01 (1982-1983). Plaintiff claimed that the four-year limitation period of § 13.01 was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff mother appealed a judgment that, based upon the four-year limitation period under Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 13.01 (1982-1983), granted defendant father summary judgment and dismissed as time-bared plaintiff's paternity action. The court reversed the judgment. The court ruled that the limitation period under § 13.01, as that statute existed at the time of plaintiff's suit, was unconstitutional. The court observed that two requirements had to be satisfied: (1) the period for obtaining support granted by Texas to illegitimate children had to be sufficiently long in duration to present a reasonable opportunity for those with an interest in such children to assert claims on their behalf, and; (2) any time limitation placed on that opportunity had to be substantially related to the state's interest in avoiding the litigation of stale or fraudulent claims. The court ruled that neither test was satisfied. The four-year period was arbitrary and insufficient. Moreover, the court reasoned, the fact that § 13.01 was amended to permit a much longer limitation period was evidence that the state's valid interest was not necessarily defeated by a limitations period longer than four years.


OUTCOME: The court reversed a judgment that granted defendant father summary judgment in plaintiff mother's paternity suit. The statutory four-year limitation period applicable to plaintiff's suit was unconstitutional because it was an insufficient period of time to enable a party such as plaintiff to present a claim on behalf of the child. Moreover, the statute was not substantially related to the state's interest in avoiding stale or fraudulent claims.

Phillips v. Sharpstown General Hospital


No. 01-82-0828-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


664 S.W.2d 162; 1983 Tex. App. LEXIS 5633



December 30, 1983 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied December 30, 1983.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 125th District Court of Harris County, Texas Trial Court Cause Number 81-8864.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant patient sought review of a judgment from the 125th District Court of Harris County (Texas), which found that appellants' health care liability claim, which was governed by the Medical Liability and Insurance Improvement Act of Texas, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4590i (1982-1983), was barred by the applicable statute of limitations, and which granted appellees hospital and physician summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: Appellant patient asserted a health care liability claim against appellees hospital and doctor, pursuant to the Medical Liability and Insurance Improvement Act of Texas, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4590i (1982-1983). The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of appellees on the basis that appellants' claim was barred by the applicable statute of limitations. On appeal, the issue was whether Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4590i, § 4.01(c) extended only the expiration date of the limitation statute, otherwise allowing it to run, or suspended the running of the limitation statute. The court agreed with appellant's contention and held that the Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4590i, § 10.01 statute of limitations was suspended for the 75-day period following the giving of Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4590i, § 4.01(a). notice, at the expiration of which time the remaining period of the original two-year limitations continued to run. Accordingly, the court reversed the holding of the trial court and remanded for trial.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court that granted appellees hospital and physician summary judgment. The court remanded for trial. The court found that the giving of notice of a health care claim within 60-days of the expiration of the two-year limitations period suspended the running of the limitation statute.

Wininger v. Department of Human Resources


No. 2-82-186-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Second District, Fort Worth


663 S.W.2d 913; 1983 Tex. App. LEXIS 5638



December 29, 1983 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied January 26, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE 30TH DISTRICT COURT OF WICHITA COUNTY.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant child caregiver challenged the order of the 30th District Court of Wichita County (Texas), which issued a permanent injunction prohibiting her from operating a child care facility.


OVERVIEW: Appellant child caregiver's son was removed from her home by appellee, the Department of Human Resources, upon allegations that appellant's husband had sexually abused the son. The criminal charges against appellant's husband were dropped when he was found incompetent to stand trial. Thereafter, appellant and her husband moved and continued to reside together. Subsequently, appellant began providing care in her home to a child unrelated to either appellant or her husband. Appellant provided such care. The trial court granted appellee's application for a permanent injunction enjoining appellant from operating a child-care facility. Upon appellant's challenge, the court reversed, on an unassigned error, because the pleadings referred to licensing requirements whereas registered family homes were exempt from licensing requirements. The supreme court reversed and remanded. On remand the court affirmed the permanent injunction, finding Tex. Hum. Res. Code Ann. § 42.002(3) was not unconstitutionally vague and regulations promulgated by appellee under the statute represented a fulfillment of its duty delegated by the legislature.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's issuance of a permanent order enjoining appellant child caregiver from operating a childcare facility because the statute under which the injunction was issued was not unconstitutionally vague. Appellee, the Department of Human Resources, exercised authority properly delegated by the legislature in regulating such facilities.

Neie v. Stevenson


No. 07-82-0227-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Seventh District, Amarillo


663 S.W.2d 917; 1983 Tex. App. LEXIS 5650



December 29, 1983 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF HALL COUNTY: 100TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT: NO. 5,515; HONORABLE ROBERT E. MONTGOMERY, JUDGE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant patient sought review of the summary judgment granted appellee doctor in the medical malpractice suit she brought in the District Court of Hall County, 100th Judicial District (Texas). She argued that the suit was filed within the two-year statute of limitations, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4590i, § 10.01 (Supp. 1982), within two years of discovery, or the statute was unconstitutional as applied in her suit.


OVERVIEW: Appellee doctor performed a tubal ligation on appellant patient in 1977. She became pregnant in 1980, and sued in 1982. The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment for appellee, based on the two-year statute of limitations, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4590i, § 10.01 (Supp. 1982). The court ruled that § 10.01 was unambiguous, and no allowance was made for the judicially created discovery rule exception. The court also rejected appellant's claim that the statute was unconstitutional as applied to her, under the 14th Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. XIV, and Tex. Const. art. I, §§ 13 and 19. The court concluded that there was a reasonable basis for the classification created by the statute and a legitimate state interest in the matter. The court noted that appellant's suit was filed more than two years after appellee could have been guilty of malpractice, and was therefore barred by § 10.01.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment granted appellee doctor in the malpractice suit brought by appellant patient after she became pregnant three years after appellee performed a tubal ligation. The court ruled the suit was barred by the two-year statute of limitations, the discovery rule was not available, and the application of the statute to appellant's situation was not unconstitutional.

Torres v. State


No. 13-82-205-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Thirteenth District, Corpus Christi


667 S.W.2d 190; 1983 Tex. App. LEXIS 5672



December 29, 1983 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Reported at: 667 S.W.2d 190 at 199.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original Opinion of November 17, 1983, Reported at: 667 S.W.2d 190. On appeal from the 367th District Court of Aransas County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a decision from the 367th District Court of Arkansas County (Texas) after being convicted of delivery of marijuana of more than 50, but less than 200 pounds, seeking a rehearing as to the sentence imposed.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of delivery of marijuana between 50 and 200 pounds. After the court affirmed appellant's conviction, appellant sought review requesting a rehearing asserting that the jury was allowed to assess a punishment under a statute that had been held to be unconstitutional. The court held that the evidence was sufficient to support the conviction and the indictment supported the jury's conviction for the offense alleged under a pre-amended act. Further, the court held that the jury imposed a sentence based upon its findings and imposed neither the maximum nor the minimum punishment authorized by the charge, but instead weighted the evidence and arrived at an appropriate sentence for the offense committed. As such, the court denied the motion for rehearing finding that the sentence was within the allowable range of punishment.


OUTCOME: The court denied appellant's motion for a rehearing, which contended the sentence imposed was improper because both the evidence and the indictment supported the jury's conviction and the sentence imposed was within the allowable range of punishment.

Moya v. State


No. 13-83-024-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Thirteenth District, Corpus Christi


663 S.W.2d 680; 1983 Tex. App. LEXIS 5674



December 29, 1983 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On appeal from the 36th District Court of Live Oak County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the decision of the 36th District Court of Live Oak County (Texas), which entered judgment against appellant after a jury convicted him of intentionally and knowingly delivering by actual transfer a controlled substance listed in Penalty Group 1, to wit, cocaine of more than 28 grams but less than 200 grams, a violation of Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15, § 4.03(d)(1) (1982-1983).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was indicted for intentionally and knowingly delivering by actual transfer a controlled substance listed in Penalty Group 1, to wit, cocaine of more than 28 grams but less than 200 grams, under the Texas Controlled Substances Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15, § 4.03(d)(1) (1982-1983), and a jury found appellant guilty as charged in the indictment. Appellant challenged his conviction and the court affirmed. The legislature later amended the statute. The court held that the indictment alleged an offense under the law as it existed before the amendment and was therefore valid. The court also held that appellant was not harmed by the charge given the jury on punishment. The court further held that appellee state did not improperly suppress evidence that was required to have been turned over to appellant because the evidence appellant requested was not exculpatory evidence and appellant was not denied his rights under either Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 27.11 (1966), or U.S. Const. amend. VI. The court also held that the trial court's instructions to the jury to disregard cured any errors, and there was sufficient evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for unlawful delivery of cocaine and held that the indictment was valid because it alleged an offense under the law as it existed before the legislature amended the statute, appellant was not harmed by the charge given to the jury regarding punishment, and the evidence appellant requested was not exculpatory and therefore appellee state did not have to turn over that evidence.

Power v. Cablevision Investor's


NO. 10-83-236-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, TENTH DISTRICT, WACO


929 S.W.2d 15; 1983 Tex. App. LEXIS 5752



December 29, 1983, Decided  
December 29, 1983, filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 30, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: From 19th Judicial District Court. McLennan County, Texas. Trial Court # 83-156-1.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant apartment owners sought review of a decision from the 19th Judicial District Court, McLennan County (Texas) that granted a declaratory judgment and permanent injunction against appellant, and in favor of appellee, cable company.


OVERVIEW: Appellant apartment owners built a complex of apartments several years ago requesting appellee cable company to install wiring and the necessary equipment to supply cable service to the units. Years later, appellants ordered appellee to discontinue its cable television service. A cause of action was filed wherein the trial court found in favor of appellee. Upon review, appellant argued that the license to operate the cable system was not supported by consideration rendering it irrevocable. Additionally, appellant asserted that the trial court erred in finding significant expenditures by appellee in reliance on the license's continuance, and in declaring that the equipment installed on appellants' property should remain appellee's property. The court held that irrevocability based on reliance rests upon equitable estoppel which is particularly supportable when a licensor has joined in the enterprise with licensee and accepts the benefits of licensee's labor and expenditures. Further, the court held that property affixed to the realty of another remained the licensee's personal property and did not become part of the realty. Thus, the judgment of the trial court was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court because appellant apartment owners entered into a license agreement with appellee cable company and accepted the benefits of appellee's labor and expenditures.

Medina v. State


No. 04-81-00490-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourth District, San Antonio


665 S.W.2d 148; 1983 Tex. App. LEXIS 5583



December 21, 1983 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Discretionary Review Refused May 9, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 63rd District Court of Val Verde County, Honorable George M. Thurmond, Judge Presiding. Trial Court No. 4656.



DISPOSITION:  Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the 63rd District Court of Val Verde County (Texas), which convicted him of delivery of marihuana for remuneration and assessed punishment at four years of confinement and a fine. Appellant claimed that the trial court's charge to the jury on punishment was defective because it did not comply with Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 42.12, § 6 (1982-1983).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of delivery of marihuana for remuneration, and received a punishment of four years of confinement and a fine. The court affirmed the conviction and sentence, and held that there was no error in the jury charge on punishment. The court held that appellant waived all but fundamental error in the charge because appellant made no objection to the charge and did not submit a requested charge. The court found that although the trial court gave an incomplete listing of the conditions of probation under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 42.12, § 6 (1982-1983), the jury was informed of the proper range of punishment under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15, § 4.05(d)(e) (1976). The court also found that the trial court properly instructed the jury that probation could be granted in certain circumstances under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 42.12, § 3a (1982-1983). The court determined that the trial court's charge as a whole did not contain any fundamental error, adequately protected appellant's rights, and did not deny a fair and impartial trial under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 36.19 (1981).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction and punishment for delivery of marihuana for remuneration. The court held that appellant waived all but fundamental error in the jury charge on punishment because he did not object to the charge or submit a requested charge. The court found that, as a whole, the trial court's charge informing the jury of the proper range of punishment and the law on probation contained no fundamental error.

December 8, 1983

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the decision of the trial court (Texas), which denied his post-conviction writ of habeas corpus in an action invoking the court's jurisdiction to hear challenges from post conviction habeas corpus proceedings in misdemeanor cases. Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 44.34 (1982-1983).


OVERVIEW: The court reversed the decision of the trial court, which denied appellant's post-conviction writ of habeas corpus, in an action invoking the court's jurisdiction to hear challenges from post conviction habeas corpus proceedings in misdemeanor cases. Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 44.34 (1982-1983). Appellant was convicted of misdemeanors, served his jail time, but was kept incarcerated because he was unable to pay his fines. XIV and was therefore impermissible.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's decision to deny appellant's post-conviction writ of habeas corpus. Incarceration of a proven indigent for failure to immediately pay a fine or court costs violated the equal protection clause of the U.S. Constitution and was therefore impermissible.

Whaley v. State


No. 2-83-042-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Second District, Fort Worth


660 S.W.2d 894; 1983 Tex. App. LEXIS 5714



December 7, 1983 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from a trial court in Texas, which convicted appellant for possession of heroin in violation of the Texas Controlled Substances Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15 (1976).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted for possession of heroin in violation of the Texas Controlled Substances Act (Act), Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15 (1976). In light of a recent decision handed down by the criminal appeals court, the court was compelled to examine the constitutionality of the Act upon appellant's conviction. The court held that the constitutionality of the amendment to the Act did not render appellant's conviction invalid because at the time when appellant committed the crime there was a valid statute in effect, which made it a criminal offense to possess heroin regardless of the amount. The court held that there were sufficient circumstances that affirmatively linked appellant to the contraband, and established more than a mere suspicion of his unlawful possession of the contraband. The court held that the evidence was sufficient that a rational trier of fact could find the essential elements of possession of heroin beyond a reasonable doubt. The court held that the evidence was also sufficient in establishing appellant's knowledge of the substance in the cloth pouch was contraband. The court affirmed appellant's conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, which convicted appellant for possession of heroin in violation of the Texas Controlled Substances Act, because the constitutionality of the amendment did not invalidate appellant's conviction, and sufficient evidence supported the conviction.

Wolf v. State


No. 2-83-069-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Second District, Fort Worth


661 S.W.2d 765; 1983 Tex. App. LEXIS 5456



December 1, 1983 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied December 29, 1983.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the 17th District Court of Tarrant County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought a review of the decision by the 17th District Court of Tarrant County (Texas), which granted appellee state injunctive relief against appellant for violation of Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 9001 (1983), selling certain items on the consecutive days of Saturday and Sunday.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted for violation of Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 9001 (1983), selling certain items on the consecutive days of Saturday and Sunday or Blue Law, and the state sought injunctive relief against appellant. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment enjoining appellant from further violation of art. 9001. The court concluded that the evidence established as a matter of law that appellant violated the statute by selling home furniture items on consecutive days of Saturday and Sunday. Appellant testified that he owned a furniture company and that his stores was open on consecutive days prohibited under the statute. The court concluded that appellant failed to establish the defense of selective prosecution since he failed to show that he was singled out for selective prosecution, which others similarly situated and committing the same acts had not. Appellant also failed to establish that such discriminatory selection for prosecution had been invidious or in bad faith by resting upon such impermissible considerations as race, religion, or the desire to prevent his exercise of constitutional rights. The court concluded that art. 9001 was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court enjoining appellant from further violations of a statute prohibiting the selling of certain items on consecutive days of Saturday and Sunday. The court concluded that the evidence was sufficient to establish a violation by appellant of the statute as a matter of law and held that the evidence did not raise a fact issue for the jury regarding any improper motive for selective prosecution.

 

1516 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Moore v. State


No. 07-82-0054-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Seventh District, Amarillo


677 S.W.2d 550; 1983 Tex. App. LEXIS 5448



November 30, 1983 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From the District Court of Lubbock County; 237th Judicial District; No. 22,476; Honorable Robert C. Wright, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment from the District Court of Lubbock County, 237th Judicial District (Texas), which convicted him on three counts of felony theft of property. He attacked the jurisdiction of appellate court, the sufficiency of the evidence, and the prosecution for three offenses in an alleged criminal episode.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of three counts of felony theft of property, alleged in a single indictment. The charges arose when his checks for the purchase of three pieces of farm equipment at an auction were returned unpaid. The court reformed the judgment and sentence and, as reformed, affirmed. The court held that it had jurisdiction over the appeal and that the appellate scheme, which became effective after appellant filed his notice of appeal, was not an ex post facto law. The court found that the evidence supported the conviction on count one because appellant's intent was presumed upon proof that he acquired the property by issuing a check, he did not have funds on deposit to pay the check in full, he had notice of the bank's dishonor, and he did not pay the holder after notification of its dishonor. The court held that in a prosecution for offenses arising out of a single transaction, a conviction could be had on only one count. The multiple convictions did not void the judgment, which was reformed by reversing the convictions on counts two and three.


OUTCOME: The court reformed the judgment and, as reformed, affirmed. The court held that its appellate jurisdiction was proper and that the evidence was sufficient to support a conviction on one count of felony theft of property. The court held that appellant could not be convicted on multiple counts from the same transaction and reformed the judgment by reversing the remaining two convictions.
