Rodriguez v. Ysleta Independent School Dist.


No. 08-82-00219-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Eighth District, El Paso


663 S.W.2d 547; 1983 Tex. App. LEXIS 5470



November 30, 1983 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from 34th District Court of El Paso County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant representative of minor child challenged the order of the 34th District Court of El Paso County (Texas) that denied appellant's claims against appellee school district after the minor child was denied admission to the public school.


OVERVIEW: Appellant representative of minor child filed an action against appellee school board after it denied admission to the minor child because she did not reside in the school district with her parent or court-appointed guardian. The trial court found for appellee, and the court affirmed. The court held that Tex. Educ. Code Ann. § 23.26 gave school districts the exclusive power to manage and govern their public schools; the situations in which the school district would need to be certain who had authority over the child supported the judgment. The policy did not violate the equal protection clause of the U.S. and Texas constitutions because the regulations were reasonably related to the needs of the school district. The court also held that appellant's due process argument was meritless.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision because appellee school district had authority to set its own admission policies.

 

1518 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Moya v. State


No. 13-82-242-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Thirteenth District, Corpus Christi


661 S.W.2d 325; 1983 Tex. App. LEXIS 5416



November 23, 1983 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On appeal from the 36th District Court of Live Oak County, Texas.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the 36th District Court, Live Oak County (Texas), which convicted him of possession of cocaine under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15. Defendant, who was tried with his wife, contended that he was provided ineffective assistance of counsel and that there was insufficient evidence to support the conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and wife were tried together for possession of cocaine under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. § 4476-15, and both were convicted after a jury trial. On appeal, defendant argued that he received ineffective assistance of counsel because his attorney, who represented both defendants, had a conflict of interest. He also argued that there was insufficient evidence to support his conviction because the state failed to submit any evidence on the amount of cocaine that he allegedly possessed, and that this was an essential element of the crime. In affirming the judgment, the court found that because defendant had not objected to his counsel at trial, he needed to show an actual conflict of interest which adversely affected his attorney's performance. The court found that defendant failed to meet this burden, and that under the totality of the circumstances, he received reasonably effective assistance which was all that was required. With regard to the amount of cocaine needed for conviction, the court noted that the portion of the statute relied on by defendant had been declared unconstitutional, and thus the previous statute, which made mere possession a crime, was applicable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction for possession of cocaine because under the totality of the circumstances, defendant's counsel had provided him reasonably effective assistance. There was sufficient evidence to support the conviction because under the governing statute, mere possession of cocaine was an offense, and thus the state was not required to prove possession of a specific amount.

 

1519 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Al-Omari v. State


Nos. 09-83-065 CR, 09-83-066 CR, 09-83-067 CR, 09-83-068 CR, 09-83-069 CR, 09-83-070 CR, 09-83-071 CR, 09-83-072 CR, 09-83-073 CR, 09-83-074 CR, 09-83-075 CR, 09-83-076 CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Ninth District, Beaumont


673 S.W.2d 892; 1983 Tex. App. LEXIS 5734



November 23, 1983 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Discretionary Review Refused May 2, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Travis County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants sought review of a decision of a trial court (Texas), which entered judgments of conviction in a joint trial for the offense of disrupting a public meeting or process, in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 42.05 (1974), after defendants were removed from a speech given during a symposium on political events in Iran. Defendants allegedly interfered with the gathering by making loud verbal utterances during the speech.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were among 25 people arrested for disrupting a public meeting or procession in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 42.05 (1974) and led out of a speech given by a journalist during a symposium concerning political events in Iran. Defendants allegedly made loud verbal utterances during the speech. Defendants were convicted, and the court affirmed the convictions. On appeal, defendants alleged § 42.05 was overbroad in violation of U.S. Const. amend. I and Tex. Const. art. I, § 8, and vague in violation of the U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Tex. Const. art. I, § 19. The court found that defendants presented nothing for review on the constitutional challenges and further had no standing to assert that § 42.05 was unconstitutional as applied to imaginary third persons. The court found that § 42.05 was applied narrowly and required specific criminal intent so it was not facially vague and had no chilling effect on constitutional freedoms. The court found that the informations were not invalid because specific verbal utterances were not alleged, as under § 42.05, conduct was actionable and not specific words.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendants' convictions for disrupting a public meeting or procession because the offense was narrowly drawn, required specific intent, and provided no chilling effect on constitutional freedoms. The court found that the statute was not facially vague and that the challenges of overbreadth and vagueness were not properly preserved for review. Defendants had no standing to challenge the statute as it applied to third persons.

Cotton v. State


No. 01-82-0537-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


662 S.W.2d 110; 1983 Tex. App. LEXIS 5382



November 17, 1983 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the County Criminal Court of Law No. 6 of Harris County, Texas Trial Court Cause No. 656,123.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the County Criminal Court of Law No. 6, Harris County, (Texas), which convicted him in a non-jury trial of the offense of selling beer to a person showing evidence of intoxication in violation of Tex. Alco. Bev. Code Ann. §§ 61.71(a)(6), 61.77 (1978).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was fined for his conviction for selling beer to a person showing evidence of intoxication in violation of Tex. Alco. Bev. Code Ann. §§ 61.71(a)(6), 61.77 (1978). Defendant contended that § 61.71(a)(6) was unconstitutionally vague and overbroad when applied in a criminal context because neither the phrase "shows evidence of intoxication" nor the word "intoxication" was defined in § 61.71(a)(6) or elsewhere in the code. The court affirmed defendant's conviction and held that the phrase "showing evidence of intoxication" within § 61.71(a)(6) was not unconstitutionally vague because it was sufficiently clear that men of ordinary intelligence did not need to guess at its meaning or be in doubt as to what conduct was prohibited. The court held that § 61.71(a)(6) was not overbroad because it penalized conduct and not inactivity or status and did not intrude into constitutionally protected conduct by banning sales to persons to whom one should reasonably be entitled to sell.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for selling beer to a person showing evidence of intoxication and held that the phrase "showing evidence of intoxication" within the pertinent statute was not unconstitutionally vague but sufficiently clear that men of ordinary intelligence did not need to guess at its meaning or be in doubt as to what conduct was prohibited.

Torres v. State


No. 13-82-205-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Thirteenth District, Corpus Christi


667 S.W.2d 190; 1983 Tex. App. LEXIS 5389



November 17, 1983 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied December 29, 1983, Reported at: 667 S.W.2d 190 at 199. Second Rehearing Denied January 26, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the 36th District Court of Aransas County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his conviction by the 36th District Court of Aransas County, Texas, for delivery of marijuana of 200 pounds or less but more than 50 pounds in violation of Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15, § 4.05(c) (1982).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of delivery of marijuana of 200 pounds or less but more than 50 pounds in violation of Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15, § 4.05(c) (1982). Subsequent to appellant's conviction art. 4476-15 was declared unconstitutional because it failed to apprise readers of the changes effected by its amendments. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that, although art. 4476-15 was unconstitutional, no reversible error was shown because the penalty imposed on appellant was within the range of the pre-amendment statute. The court found that there sufficient evidence that appellant delivered marijuana because he made arrangements with an undercover officer to meet, showed the marijuana which was in his trunk to the officer, and attempted to collect money from the officer before the arrest was made. The court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in refusing to order a new trial because there was conflicting evidence as to whether a juror's passing remark about her personal knowledge about the weight of marijuana was received by the other jurors and was detrimental to appellant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for delivery of marijuana of 200 pounds or less but more than 50 pounds because, though the statute under which he was convicted was subsequently found to be unconstitutional, no reversible error was shown because the penalty imposed on appellant was within the range of the pre-amendment statute.

 

1522 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Travis Heights Improv. Asso. v. Small


No. 13,862


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


662 S.W.2d 406; 1983 Tex. App. LEXIS 5366



November 16, 1983 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 250TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT NO, 333,166, HONORABLE HERMAN JONES, JUDGE PRESIDING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, homeowners and homeowners' association, sought review of the judgment from the District Court of Travis County, 250th Judicial District (Texas), which found in favor of appellee developer in appellants' suit to prevent appellee from erecting a 10-story condominium on land subject to a restrictive covenant.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, homeowners and homeowners' association, brought suit to enforce a restrictive covenant against appellee developer, who planned to erect a 10-story condominium in their subdivision. The covenant provided that property be used for residential purposes only. The trial court found in favor of appellee and held that the restrictive covenant was binding on the property, but that it did not prohibit the building of the multi-unit residential condominium building. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that the covenant did not impose a limit on the number of units which could be placed on a tract. The court found that testimony by homeowners that they understood the covenant to prohibit multi-unit dwellings was not uncontroverted evidence of the intent of the grantor of the covenant and need not be considered because the covenant was unambiguous. The court held that evidence that the existing neighborhood scheme comprised only single-family and duplex structures could not be used to expand the meaning of the covenant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of appellee developer in appellants', homeowners and homeowners' association, suit to prohibit appellee from building a 10-story condominium on property subject to a restrictive covenant providing that property be used for residential purposes only. The court held that the covenant did not impose a limit on the number of residential units that could be placed on a tract.

Kircus v. London

COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


660 S.W.2d 869; 1983 Tex. App. LEXIS 5368

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant developer sought review of a judgement of the 299th District Court, Travis County, Texas, which granted a temporary injunction, in favor of appellee landowners, enjoining the City of Austin from acting upon appellant's application to replat his single lot into five lots. Ann. art. 974a, § 5(c) (1982), were not unconstitutional The court found that appellant failed to show that the consent requirement imposed an adverse impact on his own rights, and therefore, he lacked standing. The court held that, at best, appellant showed a possible future deprivation. Thus, the court held that the case was not ripe for review, and that any ruling would have constituted and illegal advisory opinion.

Reddix v. Eaton Corp.


No. 04-82-00428-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourth District, San Antonio


662 S.W.2d 720; 1983 Tex. App. LEXIS 5371; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P9890



November 16, 1983 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied December 6, 1983.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 25th District Court of Guadalupe County Trial Court No. 79-893 Honorable B.B. Schraub, Judge Presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a gardener who was injured in an out-door elevator, challenged a judgment of the 25th District Court, Guadalupe County, Texas, which granted summary judgment under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann., art. 5536a, in favor of appellees, an elevator manufacturer and chain link manufacturers.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, a gardener who was injured in an out-door elevator, argued that the trial court erred in granting summary judgment under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 5536a, because appellees, an elevator manufacturer and chain link manufacturers, did not establish as a matter of law that the electric hoist and link chain were designed or constructed by registered or licensed engineers or architects within the meaning of Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 5536a, § 1 and that Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 5536a, § 2 did not apply to product manufacturers as a matter of law. On appeal, the court reversed summary judgment in favor of appellees and remanded the case for trial. The court held that appellees were not protected by the provisions of art. 5536a, §§ 1 and 2. The electric hoist and link chain were not designed by a registered architect or engineer, so summary judgment could not be based on of art. 5536a, § 1. Article 5536a, § 2 applied to architects, engineers, and "any person" performing or furnishing construction or repair of any improvement to real property. A materialman who did no more than manufacture or supply materials did not benefit from art. 5536a, § 2.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment in favor of appellees, an elevator manufacturer and chain link manufacturers, because they were not architects or engineers protected by the statute of repose and component part manufacturers were not entitled to protection under the statute.

Garcia v. State


No. 09-83-086 CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Ninth District, Beaumont


661 S.W.2d 754; 1983 Tex. App. LEXIS 5594



November 9, 1983 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Tom Green County.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant juvenile sought review of his conviction for murder entered in Tom Green County (Texas), on the grounds that the trial court committed reversible error in failing to sustain his objection to a photograph of the body of the victim, in overruling his motion to suppress his confession, and in overruling his motion to suppress evidence.


OVERVIEW: Appellant juvenile challenged his conviction for murder on the grounds that the trial court committed reversible error in failing to sustain his objection to a photograph of the body of the victim and in overruling his motion to suppress his confession. Appellant also argued that the trial court erred in overruling his motion to suppress evidence on the grounds that Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 52.01 deprived juveniles equal protection of the law. The court affirmed appellant's conviction for murder because the photograph of the victim's body was not gruesome and it clarified expert testimony, there was no evidence that appellant's confession was not given freely and voluntarily, and that portion of the Family Code allowing custody of a juvenile without an arrest warrant was constitutional. The court stated that although § Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 52.01(a)(3) authorized the taking of juveniles into custody without an arrest warrant, the approach, which differed from treatment of adult criminals, stemmed from benevolence rather than discrimination and was based upon a reasonable and substantial classification and was therefore constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant juvenile's conviction for murder because the photograph of the victim's body was not gruesome and it clarified expert testimony, there was no evidence that appellant's confession was not given freely and voluntarily, and that portion of the Texas Family Code allowing custody of a juvenile without an arrest warrant was constitutional.

 

1526 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Kelley v. State


No. 05-82-00514-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


669 S.W.2d 329; 1983 Tex. App. LEXIS 5340



November 7, 1983 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM A DISTRICT COURT OF DALLAS COUNTY, TEXAS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment of a District Court of Dallas County, Texas, which convicted her of theft in a proceeding conducted by a magistrate appointed pursuant to Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 1918c (1982-1983). Appellant challenged the conviction on the grounds that the tribunal which conducted the hearing, entered judgment, and denied her probation was improperly constituted in violation of the Texas Constitution.


OVERVIEW: Initially indicted for felony theft of property, defendant accepted a plea bargain to misdemeanor theft of property. Defendant waived her right to a jury trial, signed a judicial confession, consented to the introduction of oral and written evidence, and applied for probation, all before a magistrate who signed an order convicting appellant, assigning punishment, and denying probation. A district court judge later signed a final judgment adopting all of the magistrate's rulings, except no mention was made of the matter of probation. Appellant challenged the conviction, contending that the tribunal which conducted the hearing and entered the judgment against appellant was improperly constituted in violation of the Texas Constitution. The court reversed the judgment of the district court and held that under the Texas Constitution only the district court judge held the judicial power to make a final decision on whether appellant should be placed on probation pursuant to Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 42.13, § 3 and that this judicial power could not be delegated to a magistrate.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the district court, which had adopted the rulings of a magistrate to which appellant's indictment for theft had been delegated for hearing. The court held that the magistrate which conducted a hearing on appellant's application for probation and denied with finality that motion was not constitutionally authorized to do so.

 

1527 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


PHILLIPS v. SHARPSTOWN GEN. HOSP.


NO. 01-82-0828-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1983 Tex. App. LEXIS 5262



November 3, 1983 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] On Appeal from the 125th District Court of Harris County, Texas Trial Court Cause Number 81-8864


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, patient and other, sought review of an order of the 125th District Court of Harris County (Texas), which granted the summary judgment motion of appellees, hospital and physician, on the basis that appellants' medical malpractice claim was barred by the two year statute of limitations, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4590i, § 10.01 (1982-1983), when applied with the applicable notice requirement and tolling provisions.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, patient and other, sought review of the trial court's grant of summary judgment in favor of appellees, hospital and physician, on appellants' medical malpractice claim governed by the Medical Liability and Insurance Improvement Act of Texas, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4590i (1982-1983) and based on failure of appellant patient's sterilization operation. The trial court found that appellants' claim was barred by the statute of limitations, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4590i, § 10.01 (1982-1983). The court reversed, holding that the 75 days during which the limitations statute was tolled pursuant to Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4590i, § 4.01(c) (1982-1983) following claim notice under the 60-day provision of Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4590i, § 4.01(a), should not be calculated as part of the two-year limitation period when 48 unexpired days of the two-year limitation period remained at the notice. The court found that upon the expiration of the tolling period, the 48 remaining days ran, making the action timely. The court held that art. 4590i, § 10.01 did not abolish fraudulent concealment as an equitable estoppel to the defense of limitations.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's grant of summary judgment in favor of appellees, hospital and physician, on the medical malpractice claim of appellants, patient and other, holding that appellants' claim was timely filed because 48 days remained in the limitations period when statutory notice of the claim was given, tolling the period for 75 days. The action was then timely filed within the remaining 48 days after the tolling period ended.

Kramer v. State

COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant x-rated movie projectionist challenged his conviction for promotion of obscenity in the County Criminal Court At Law No. 7 of Harris County (Texas), on the basis there was insufficient evidence for the jury to find that he knew the content and character of the film he projected, and the content and character presumption in Tex. Appellant alleged that the statute under which his conviction was obtained was unconstitutional because the caption of House Bill No. 730, which amended the Controlled Substances Act, failed to meet the requirement of Tex. OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court holding that appellant was properly convicted of the crime of possession of heroin because the indictment alleged possession of a quantity of heroin, which was an offense under the law before the House Bill was passed, and the sentence imposed was within the range allowed.

Anderson v. State


Nos. 2-83-074-CR, 2-83-075-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Second District, Fort Worth


659 S.W.2d 932; 1983 Tex. App. LEXIS 5274



November 3, 1983 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From Criminal District Court No. 4 of Tarrant County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction in the Criminal District Court No. 4 of Tarrant County (Texas), for delivery of less than twenty-eight grams of methamphetamine, in violation of Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15 (1976).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15 (1976) of the Texas Controlled Substances Act, for delivery of less than twenty-eight grams of the controlled substance methamphetamine, and the trial court assessed punishment at 14 years imprisonment. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment of the trial court and held that the unconstitutionality of the 1981 amendatory act of the Texas Controlled Substances Act did not render the conviction invalid, as the original act under which defendant committed the offense remained in full force and effect. The court further held that when defendant took the stand to support his application for probation, he waived his U.S. Const. amend. V privilege against self-incrimination, that specific acts of misconduct by the accused which did not result in final conviction generally were not admissible, but that a court would be reluctant to exclude otherwise legally admissible evidence relevant to the determination of an accused's application for probation, and that the trial court was under no duty to announce his finding of guilt prior to the presentation of evidence on punishment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction of defendant for delivery of a controlled substance, because even though the 1981 amendment to the Controlled Substances Act was declared unconstitutional, the conviction was not invalidated as the original act remained in full force and effect. The court also held that defendant waived his Fifth Amendment privilege against self-incrimination when he testified in regard his application for probation.

Doyle v. Harben


No. 16925


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourth District, San Antonio


660 S.W.2d 586; 1983 Tex. App. LEXIS 5226; 38 U.C.C. Rep. Serv. (Callaghan) 21



October 26, 1983 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied November 21, 1983.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 224th District Court of Bexar County Trial Court No. 79-CI-18331 Honorable James A. McKay, Judge Presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant seller challenged a decision from the 224th District Court of Bexar County (Texas) that granted a partial summary judgment for appellee buyer, finding as a matter of law that a breach of warranty of title had been established. Appellee's vehicle was confiscated because it had been stolen before appellant acquired it.


OVERVIEW: Appellant seller challenged the constitutionality of the Texas Certificate of Title Act when applied in conjunction with breach of warranty provisions of the Texas Business and Commerce Code. A used vehicle was sold to appellant, who then sold it to appellee buyer. The vehicle was confiscated by the State Department of Public Safety as a stolen vehicle, the theft having occurred prior to the transactions with appellant. Appellee brought an action against appellant following the confiscation. The trial court granted a partial summary judgment, finding as a matter of law that a breach of warranty of title had been established. By trial amendment appellant raised the constitutional issues presented in the appeal and sought indemnity against the state for its wrongful and negligent acts. It was a settled rule that a purchaser of property from one who had acquired possession by theft acquired no title. Appellant was unable to transfer good title to appellee despite appellant's compliance with the Certificate of Title Act. Although appellant acted innocently, he purchased stolen vehicles and was unable to acquire good title. The judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The decision granting a partial summary judgment to appellee buyer, based on a finding that a breach of title had been established, was affirmed because appellant seller committed legal fraud when he sold stolen property to appellee. Therefore, appellant was liable to appellee for the purchase price of the vehicle.

 

1534 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


James v. State


No. 07-82-0027-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Seventh District, Amarillo


660 S.W.2d 146; 1983 Tex. App. LEXIS 5206



October 21, 1983 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From the District Court of Lubbock County; 99th Judicial District; No. 21,688; Honorable Robert C. Wright, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the District Court of Lubbock County, 99th Judicial District (Texas), that convicted him of delivery of a controlled substance and sentenced him to a ten-year term of incarceration, arguing that the closing argument of his counsel was impermissibly restricted by the trial court and that the trial court erred in refusing to grant a mistrial after the prosecution referred to an extraneous offense.


OVERVIEW: Appellant pled guilty to a charge of delivery of a controlled substance, and a jury assessed punishment of a ten-year term of incarceration. He challenged the judgment of conviction and sentence, arguing that the trial court erred in improperly restricting the closing argument of appellant's counsel and in denying his motion for mistrial when the prosecution referred to an extraneous offense. In affirming, the appellate court concluded that where the record established no unconstitutional restriction of appellant's closing argument and did not reflect what appellant's counsel would have argued if he had not been so restricted, appellant failed to demonstrate harmful error. The appellate court likewise rejected appellant's contention that he was entitled to a mistrial when the prosecution improperly referred to an extraneous offense by using the term "drug dealing." Where appellant pled guilty to delivery of a controlled substance, he admitted to dealing in an illegal drug. As such, the prosecution was entitled to characterize his activity as drug dealing, and such characterization was not improper.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction and sentence was affirmed, as appellant failed to demonstrate harmful error where he failed to establish on the record the argument he was precluded from making in closing. Further, the trial court properly denied appellant's motion for a mistrial, as the prosecution properly characterized appellant's activity as drug dealing, and such term did not improperly refer to an extraneous offense.

 

1535 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Ex parte Robbins


No. 08-83-00077-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Eighth District, El Paso


661 S.W.2d 740; 1983 Tex. App. LEXIS 5219



October 19, 1983 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from 171st District Court of El Paso County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator merchandise seller appealed the judgment of the 171st District Court of El Paso County, Texas, which denied relator habeas corpus relief from the state's action against appellant for violation of the "Blue Law," Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 9001, § 1 (1982), on the ground that the "Blue Law" unconstitutionally infringed upon his right to equal protection in that it unlawfully discriminated against single-item sellers of merchandise.


OVERVIEW: Relator merchandise seller offered to sell trousers on a Saturday and consecutive Sunday, in contravention of the state's "Blue Law," Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 9001, § 1 (1982.). The state charged relator with violation of the "Blue Law." Relator contended that the "Blue Law" infringed upon relator's right to equal protection under U.S. Const. amend. XIV in that it unlawfully discriminated against the single-item seller of merchandise. The trial court rejected relator's habeas corpus challenge to the constitutionality of the statute and denied relator habeas corpus relief. The court affirmed. The court found that the criminal nature of the "Blue Law" provisions invoked did not justify strict scrutiny of the statute. The court held that the proper standard was the minimum scrutiny of the rational relation test because the "Blue Law" did not intrude on fundamental rights and produced no adverse consequence particularly visited upon and recognized suspect category. The court found that the equal protection clause did not require that state regulatory statutes apply to all in the same business with absolute equality.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of relator merchandise seller's petition for habeas corpus relief from his pending trial for violation of the "Blue Law" because minimum scrutiny was proper standard of review because statute did not infringe on fundamental rights, statute rationally related to express legislative purpose, and that equal protection clause did not require equal results.

 

1536 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


WHALEY v. STATE STATE


NO. 2-83-042-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Second District, Fort Worth


1983 Tex. App. LEXIS 5177



October 12, 1983 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Opinion Withdrawn December 7, 1983


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT #4 OF TARRANT COUNTY


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his conviction for possession of heroin in violation of the Texas Controlled Substances Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15, in its form as amended by the legislature in 1981, entered in the Criminal District Court No. 4, Tarrant County, Texas.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted for possession of heroin under the Texas Controlled Substances Act (Act), Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15 (1976), following an incident in which police officers found heroin residue on the floor of appellant's car and heroin capsules in the possession of appellant's wife, a passenger in the car. Appellant alleged insufficient evidence to prove knowing and intentional possession of heroin. Appellant also alleged that because the state did not prove the quantity of heroin in appellant's possession, only a conviction for possession of drug paraphernalia was proper. The court affirmed, finding that evidence that appellant was the driver and owner of the vehicle in which the heroin was found was sufficient to support an inference that appellant was knowingly and intentionally in possession of heroin. The quantity of heroin possessed by appellant was sufficient to support the conviction because mere evidence of heroin residue was a violation under the statute. The court held that although the 1981 amendment to the Act under which appellant was convicted was declared unconstitutional, appellant's conviction was still valid under the original unamended Act.


OUTCOME: The judgment convicting appellant of possession of heroin under the Texas controlled substances statute was affirmed because evidence that appellant was the owner and driver of the car in which the heroin was found was sufficient to support an inference that appellant knowingly and intentionally possessed the substance. Appellant's conviction was not invalid due to the unconstitutionality of the amended act under which he was convicted.

 

1537 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Seay v. Hall


No. 05-82-00574-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


663 S.W.2d 468; 1983 Tex. App. LEXIS 5183



September 30, 1983 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied November 1, 1983.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM A PROBATE COURT OF DALLAS COUNTY, TEXAS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant estate administratrix challenged an order of the Probate Court No. 2, Dallas County (Texas), which dismissed her actions for wrongful death under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4671-4678 (1982-1983) and personal injury pursuant to Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 5525 (1970) for want of jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: Appellant estate administratrix brought actions for wrongful death and personal injuries on behalf of decedent's estate. The probate court dismissed both causes of action for want of jurisdiction, and appellant sought review. The court found that a cause of action for personal injuries survived the death of the injured party and could be asserted by the heirs or administrator on behalf of the estate. A cause of action for personal injuries was an asset of the estate, and therefore the probate court had jurisdiction to determine the status of that asset, as meritorious vel non, as a matter incident to the estate. However, a wrongful death action was a cause of action separate and distinct from a survival cause of action, although both arise from the same transaction, and a wrongful death cause of action was not an asset of the estate. Accordingly, the court reversed that part of the trial court's order dismissing the survival cause of action but affirmed that part of the order dismissing the wrongful death cause of action.


OUTCOME: The court reversed that part of the probate court's order dismissing the survival cause of action for want of jurisdiction, because a cause of action for personal injuries was an asset of the estate and the probate court had jurisdiction to determine the status of that asset. With respect to that part of the probate court's order dismissing the wrongful death action, the court affirmed, because that cause of action was not an estate asset.

 

1538 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Lucario v. State


No. 01-82-0659-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


658 S.W.2d 835; 1983 Tex. App. LEXIS 5120



September 22, 1983 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the 184th District Court of Harris County, Texas Trial Court Cause No. 351,064.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a decision from the 184th District Court, Harris County (Texas), which convicted him of engaging in organized criminal activity in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 71.02(a)(1) (1983). Appellant alleged that the trial court erred in overruling his motion to quash the indictment, that the statute was unconstitutional, and that appellant should have been prosecuted for more specific offenses.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of engaging in organized criminal activity in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 71.02(a)(1) (1983). Appellant sought review of his conviction and the court affirmed. The court determined that, in an indictment for engaging in organized criminal activity, it was not necessary to specifically identify the manner and means of committing the underlying offense. The court found that the statute was not unconstitutionally vague or overbroad because it did not prohibit constitutionally protected conduct and gave notice of the point at which incidental assistance of an activity became a conspiracy to commit an act prohibited by the statute. The court also found that the punishment scheme under the statute was rationally related to the conduct it addressed. Finally, the court concluded that the general rule that a person be prosecuted under a specific statute rather than a general one was not applicable when the general statute was enacted after the specific statute.


OUTCOME: Appellant's conviction for engaging in organized criminal activity was affirmed. It was not necessary for the indictment to specifically allege the manner and means of committing the underlying offense, the statute was not unconstitutionally vague or overbroad, and the rule that a person should be prosecuted under a specific rather than general statute did not apply where the general statute was enacted after the specific statute.

Galen v. State


No. C14-82-327CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


672 S.W.2d 235; 1983 Tex. App. LEXIS 5122



September 22, 1983 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Discretionary Review Refused February 29, 1984. Rehearing Denied April 25, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from County Criminal Court at Law No. 5 of Harris County, Cause No. 641,390.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant filed an appeal from a judgment of the County Criminal Court at Law No. 5 of Harris County (Texas), which after a non-jury trial found appellant guilty of promotion of obscene material, and assessed a fine.


OVERVIEW: A vice officer went to a cinema where he viewed a film that the trial court later held to be obscene. Subsequently, officers returned, seized the film pursuant to a search warrant, and arrested appellant, the alleged manager of the theater. After a non-jury trial, the court found appellant guilty of promotion of obscene material, and assessed a fine. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded with instructions to enter a judgment of acquittal. The court found that the state produced no evidence showing that appellant knew the content and character of the film. The court apparently agreed with appellant's argument that there was no evidence that he was on the premises when the film was exhibited, and that his mere presence on the premises after the offense and his position as alleged manager were not culpatory evidence. The court that noted that the presumption under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 43.23(e) (1982-1983) that a person charged with promotion of obscene material had knowledge of the film's content and character had been held unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court that found appellant guilty of promotion of obscene material, and remanded with instructions to enter a judgment of acquittal, because the court found that the state produced no evidence showing that appellant knew the content and character of the film.

VEGA v. STATE


NO. 01-82-0508-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1983 Tex. App. LEXIS 5081



September 15, 1983 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] On Appeal from the 184th District Court of Harris County, Texas Trial Court Cause No. 350,957


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction from the 184th District Court of Harris County (Texas) for possession of heroin and sentence of 10 years imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged his conviction of possession of heroin. The trial court found defendant guilty and assessed his punishment, enhanced by one prior felony conviction, at 10 years confinement. The court affirmed the judgment of conviction because the indictment alleged the elements of possession of a controlled substance, namely heroin, proscribed by Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15, §§ 4.02(b)(2), 4.04(a)(b) and was sufficient to allege defendant's unlawful conduct. The court also stated that the evidence demonstrated that defendant exercised actual care, custody, and control over the heroin in his pocket, thus establishing that he possessed it within the meaning of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 1.07(28) (1974). Next, the court stated that the recitation of an informant's personal observation of heroin within the residence satisfied the first prong of a test. The second prong of the test was fulfilled by the recitation that the affiant received information from a credible and reliable person who gave information in the past regarding narcotic traffic that proved true and correct.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of possession of heroin because the indictment alleged each of the elements of possession of a controlled substance, namely heroin, proscribed by statute and was sufficient to allege defendant's unlawful conduct. The evidence demonstrated that defendant exercised actual care, custody, and control over the heroin in his pocket.

 

1541 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Kelley v. State


No. 05-82-00514-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


669 S.W.2d 329; 1983 Tex. App. LEXIS 5086



September 12, 1983 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Opinion Withdrawn November 7, 1983.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM A DISTRICT COURT OF DALLAS COUNTY, TEXAS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the decision of the District Court of Dallas County, Texas, which convicted appellant of theft of $ 20.00 or more but less than $ 200.00 and assessed punishment at 180 days in jail pursuant to a negotiated plea agreement.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of theft and assessed 180 days in jail pursuant to a plea agreement. Appellant argued that the tribunal which conducted the hearing and entered judgment was in violation of the Constitution of Texas, because appellant's application for probation was heard and denied solely by a magistrate appointed under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 1918c. The court reversed and remanded and held that art. 1918c was unconstitutional as applied to appellant. The court held that a magistrate was no more than a surrogate for the district court, that art. 1918c did not create a magistrate's court, and merely authorized a procedure whereby the duly constituted district court may dispose of matters before it. The court held that judicial decisions involving the ends of justice and the best interests of the public and defendant required by Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 42.13, § 3 could not be left to a surrogate under Tex. Const. art. V, § 1. The court ruled that only the judge of the trial court held the power to determine whether appellant should be placed on probation pursuant to art. 42.13, § 3 and that could not be delegated to a surrogate.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded appellant's conviction of theft because a magistrate was merely a surrogate for the trial court judge and did not have the power to determine whether appellant should be placed on probation. The court reasoned that judicial decisions involving the ends of justice and best interests of the public and appellant could not be left to a surrogate.

 

1542 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Texas Industrial Traffic League v. Railroad Com. of Texas


No. 13,380


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


672 S.W.2d 548; 1983 Tex. App. LEXIS 5003



September 7, 1983 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Opinion Withdrawn May 9, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the District Court of Travis County, 201st Judicial District No. 302,672, Honorable Charles D. Mathews, Judge Presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant organizations challenged the decision of the District Court of Travis County (Texas), which entered judgment for appellees Railroad Commission of Texas in the action brought by appellants seeking judicial review of appellee railroad commission's final order allowing for rate increases for motor carriers.


OVERVIEW: The trial court entered judgment for appellees Railroad Commission of Texas in the action brought by appellant organizations seeking judicial review of appellee's final order allowing for rate increases for motor carriers for their intrastate service. The court affirmed the judgment, holding that a reviewing court could not invalidate appellee's rate order on the ground that appellee employed an improper method in its ratemaking. The court held that Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 911b, § 20 provided for a trial de novo on judicial review of an exercise by appellee of its ratemaking power. The court held that during this de novo review appellants were required to establish by a preponderance of the evidence that the rate order was unreasonable or unjust to appellant. The court further held that the scope of review provided by law for appellee's order was not governed by the substantial evidence rule, and consequently the court held that the court could not investigate on judicial review the methods or criteria adopted by appellee for determining the carriers' revenue requirements in those rate proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment for appellees Railroad Commission of Texas, in the action brought by appellants seeking judicial review of appellee railroad commission's final order allowing for rate increases for motor carriers, because a reviewing court could not invalidate appellee's rate order on the ground that appellee employed an improper method in its ratemaking.

 

1543 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Aumada v. State


No. 13-82-288-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Thirteenth District, Corpus Christi


657 S.W.2d 890; 1983 Tex. App. LEXIS 4994



September 1, 1983 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 148th District Court of Nueces County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants challenged a judgment of the 184th District Court of Nueces County, Texas, which convicted them of aggravated sexual abuse.


OVERVIEW: Appellants were tried jointly and convicted of aggravated sexual assault. On appeal, the court held that because the evidence showed that several acts of rape were committed by one continuous act of force and threats, state was not required to elect which specific act of rape upon which it relied. The court held that the trial court properly allowed identification testimony after concluding that the pre-trial display of photographs was not impermissibly suggestive. The court held that state's use of peremptory challenges to exclude venireman with Mexican-American surnames was not a systematic exclusion. The court held that Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 21.05 (1973) did not fail to give persons adequate notice of the contents. The indictment adequately charged the offenses under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 21.05(a)3, even though it omitted the statutory phrase "occurring in the presence of the victim" in the portion relating to acts of force and threat. The court held that the trial court's charge, which only abstractly charged on the law of parties did not deny appellants a fair trial because the evidence was sufficient to sustain their conviction as primary actors.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellants' convictions of aggravated sexual abuse because state was not required to elect which act it relied on in a series of acts based on one continuing act of force and threat. The court also held that the identification process was permissible and that there was no systematic exclusion in jury selection. Additionally, the court held that the penal statute, indictment, and jury charge were all proper.

 

1544 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Neagle v. Nelson


No. 13-82-023-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Thirteenth District, Corpus Christi


658 S.W.2d 258; 1983 Tex. App. LEXIS 5701



September 1, 1983 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied October 6, 1983 (overruled).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant patient sought review of summary judgment in favor of appellees, doctors and nurses, in appellant's medical malpractice action arising out of the patient's discovery that a surgical sponge was left in his abdomen after surgery.


OVERVIEW: In December, 1977, appellees, doctors and nurses, allegedly left a surgical sponge in appellant patient's abdomen after surgery. The date of last examination or treatment by any appellee was January, 1978. Appellant filed suit in October, 1980. The trial court granted the appellees summary judgment on the ground that the suit was barred by the two-year statute of limitations under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4590I, § 10.01 (Supp.1982). Appellant sought review. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that summary judgment was correct under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4590i, § 10.01 (Supp.1982), because appellant did not file his suit within two years of the date of last treatment by any appellee. The court held that § 10.01, was an "absolute" statute of limitations. As such, it was unmodified by the "discovery rule," which, if applicable, would have tolled the statute of limitations until appellant discovered the allegedly negligent treatment by appellees. The court also held that the legislative title of § 10.01, was not unconstitutionally insufficient because it gave reasonable notice of its contents to an average legislator or interested citizen.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed summary judgment in favor of appellees, doctors and nurses, because appellant patient did not file his suit within two years of the date of the alleged negligent treatment or the date of last treatment by any of appellees. The legislative title of the applicable statute of limitations was sufficient to give reasonable notice of its contents and was thus constitutional.

 

1545 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Cook v. Slusky


No. A14-82-648-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


659 S.W.2d 110; 1983 Tex. App. LEXIS 4912



August 18, 1983 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied September 15, 1983.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from 151st District Court of Harris County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, former owners, challenged a judgment from the 151st District Court of Harris County (Texas) in favor of appellee purchaser. Appellants claimed that the jury erred in awarding possession of land to appellee under Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 33.54 because retroactive application of this statute was unconstitutional, or, in the alternative, because appellants fell within the savings clause in Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 7345b-3.


OVERVIEW: Appellee purchaser brought suit against appellants, former owners, to establish his right to land he inherited from his brother who obtained it at a tax sale. The jury awarded title to the property to appellee, and appellants sought review. They claimed that appellee's tax deed alone did not establish his title to property because Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 7345b-3 and its successor, Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 33.54, were unconstitutional if applied retroactively. In the alternative, appellants claimed they fell within the savings clause in Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 7345b-3. The court held that art. 7345b-3 and § 33.54 were constitutional and did not bridge any substantive rights because they were procedural in nature. It found that one appellant had asserted a defense to appellee's claim within the three year period in art. 7345b-3(b), so he was entitled to have appellee prove appellee's trespass to try title action. The court reversed on this part of the trial court's judgment, but it also affirmed in part, overruling points of error raised by other appellant who had not brought a cause of action or asserted a defense within the period in art. 7345b-3(b).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment pertaining to one appellant, former owner, who asserted a defense to appellee purchaser's claim to title to land within the savings period. The court affirmed the part of the judgment as to other appellant, former owner, who had not asserted a defense within the savings period. Because the limitations statute was procedural, it did not take away vested rights and was constitutional.

Steeley v. State


No. A14-81-828-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


659 S.W.2d 71; 1983 Tex. App. LEXIS 4877



July 28, 1983 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied August 18, 1983.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from 179th District Court of Harris County Cause No. 342,129.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the 179th District Court, Harris County, Texas, in which a jury found him guilty of the felony offense of possession of a controlled substance, namely, methamphetamine, weighing less than 28 grams by aggregate weight.


OVERVIEW: A jury found defendant guilty of possession of a controlled substance, methamphetamine, weighing less than 28 grams by aggregate weight. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that the evidence was sufficient to show that the substance was methamphetamine, as alleged in the indictment, where a chemist testified that the substance was methamphetamine, which was 34 percent pure and weighed 1.70 grams, and that methamphetamine in its pure form was a non-stable liquid, which must be combined with some kind of a stabilizing agent to convert it to a powder. The evidence was also sufficient to prove that defendant knowingly exercised care, custody, and control of the methamphetamine where police officers found defendant kneeling next to a flushing commode, with two packets of powder by his feet. The court held that defendant's conviction was not based on an unconstitutional statute because the caption to the amendment to Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15 (1982-83) provided adequate notice, as required by Tex. Const. art. III, § 35. Finally, the court held that the court was allowed to charge on the law of parties even though there was no such allegation in the indictment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment, which convicted defendant of possession of a controlled substance, and held that the evidence was sufficient to show that defendant knowingly exercised care, custody, and control of methamphetamine. The court also held that defendant's conviction was not based on an unconstitutional statute and that the court was allowed to charge on the law of parties even though there was no such allegation in the indictment.

Richardson v. State


No. 3-82-078-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


656 S.W.2d 609; 1983 Tex. App. LEXIS 4713



July 20, 1983 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Discretionary Review Granted November 2, 1983.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the District Court of Lampasas County, 27th Judicial District.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment entered by jury trial in the 27th District Court, Lampasas County, Texas, in which he was convicted of aggravated possession of less than 2000 but more than 200 pounds of marijuana and was sentenced to 15 years imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of aggravated possession of less than 2000 but more than 200 pounds of marijuana and was sentenced by the jury to 15 years imprisonment. Defendant appealed challenging the admissibility and sufficiency of the evidence. On appeal, the court reversed defendant's conviction and remanded for a new trial. The court found that defendant was charged after an amendment to the Controlled Substances Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15, § 4.051 (1982) which was held unconstitutional and void under Tex. Const. Ann. art. III, § 35 (1955), for lack of adequate notice of the charges. Also, defendant's punishment was assessed as excessive and was, therefore, not authorized by statute. Further, the court held, from the totality of circumstances, that the affidavit supporting the warrant to search defendant's firm was based on probable cause. Additionally, the court held, based on the totality of the evidence and the reasonable inferences, that the evidence was sufficient to support conviction. Finally, the court held that it could not reform defendant's judgment and instead remanded for a new trial, as the jury rather than the court assessed punishment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded for a new trial the judgment against defendant in which he was convicted of aggravated possession of less than 2000 but more than 200 pounds of marijuana. Defendant's sentence was not authorized by statute and the jury rather than the court assessed defendant's punishment.

 

1548 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Phillips v. State


No. 05-81-00936-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


654 S.W.2d 846; 1983 Tex. App. LEXIS 4762



July 15, 1983 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM A DISTRICT COURT OF HUNT COUNTY, TEXAS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the decision of a district court of Hunt County (Texas), which convicted him of burglary of a building. Appellant alleged the trial court erred by failing to quash the jury venire, to give his requested charges on circumstantial evidence and on a lesser-included offense, and to grant his motion for instructed verdict. Appellant also alleged denial of his right to cross-examine.


OVERVIEW: Following appellant's conviction for burglary of a building, he challenged the decision. The court affirmed. First, the trial court did not err by failing to quash the jury venire because appellant does not cite any portion of the record in support of the alleged error and failed to demonstrate purposeful and systematic exclusion of a cognizable group. Second, the trial court properly instructed the jury because the requirement of a circumstantial evidence charge had been abolished and appellant failed to present evidence that if he was guilty, he was guilty only of a lesser included offense. Third, the trial court's communication with the jury did not amount to additional instructions, and the application portion of the trial court's charge limited theories of convictions to those plead in the indictment, thus there was no fundamental error. Fifth, the evidence was sufficient for the jury to find that appellant entered the building with the intent to commit theft. And finally, the use of penitentiary packets and the testimony of a fingerprint expert to prove appellant was the person twice before convicted did not deny appellant his right to cross-examination.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction holding that appellant failed to demonstrate purposeful exclusion of a cognizable group from the jury pool; appellant had no right to a circumstantial evidence charge of lesser included offense charge; communication with the jury did not amount to additional instructions; and, the introduction of corrections department documents did not violate appellant's right to cross-examination.

 

1549 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Taylor v. State


No. 01-82-0818-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


671 S.W.2d 535; 1983 Tex. App. LEXIS 4581



June 23, 1983 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from Probate Court #3 of Harris County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his mental health commitment that was entered in Probate Court #3 of Harris County (Texas). He argued that the evidence was insufficient to sustain a finding that he was mentally ill and required commitment in a mental hospital, that he was not afforded a probable cause hearing within a reasonable time of his detention, and that he was denied due process of law because the jury's verdict was not unanimous.


OVERVIEW: Appellant disputed his commitment to a mental hospital. The court reviewed the evidence and applicable due process standards. The court held that the testimony of his family members showed that he required hospitalization for his own welfare and protection. His behavior could result in someone acting in a violent manner toward appellant in the future, which could result in injury to himself and to others. His pre-commitment detention complied with Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 5547-66 (1980). He was provided the hearing as required by art. 5547-68(b). Although he did not have a probable cause hearing, he did have an opportunity to be heard and present evidence in his own behalf at the commitment hearing, which incorporated due process requirements. The remedy for failure to provide a probable cause hearing within three days of an emergency commitment was release, pending the temporary commitment hearing. The commitment process was civil, so the rules of civil procedure applied. Tex. R. Civ. P. 292 provided that a verdict could be rendered by five out of the six jurors. Further, appellant had not objected to the jury charge, so he had waived any objection. The court affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed. The testimony of appellant's family members tended to show that he required hospitalization for his own welfare and protection and that of others. He was afforded an opportunity to be heard and present evidence in the commitment hearing, which incorporated due process requirements. The civil rules applied to the commitment process, so a verdict could be rendered by five out of the six jurors.

Gholson v. State


No. C14-81-420-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


667 S.W.2d 168; 1983 Tex. App. LEXIS 4672



June 23, 1983 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied July 28, 1983. Petition for Discretionary Review Refused January 6, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 9 of Harris County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 9 of Harris County (Texas), which convicted him of promoting obscene material in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 43.23 (1982-1983) and assessed punishment at one year in jail and a $ 2000.00 fine.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of promoting obscene material in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 43.23 (1982-1983). The trial court assessed punishment at one year in jail and a $ 2000.00 fine. The court affirmed the judgment, finding that the trial court properly approved the transcript of the court reporter's notes despite a multitude of spelling errors. The court did not find the errors in the statement of facts to be so serious as to render the document unintelligible. The court also held that Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 43.21(a)(4) and (a)(5) were not unconstitutional. The definition of "patently offensive" in § 43.21(a)(4) was constitutionally valid and was not overbroad. The court held that the trial court did not err in overruling defendant's motion to quash the information, concluding that the definition of "promote" contained in § 43.21(a)(5) was not constitutionally overbroad on its face. Additionally, the court held that the affidavit underlying the information was valid. Finally, the court found that the evidence was sufficient to prove that defendant "promoted" allegedly obscene material in violation of § 43.23(c).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment that convicted defendant of promoting obscene material and assessed punishment at one year in jail and a $ 2000.00 fine. The court held that the statutory definitions of "patently offensive" and "promoted" were not unconstitutionally overbroad and that the evidence was sufficient to prove that defendant promoted the material. Further, the trial court properly approved statement of facts despite spelling errors.

 

1551 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


MARTIN v. STATE


No. C14-82-740CR, A14-82-741CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


1983 Tex. App. LEXIS 4678



June 23, 1983 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] From the 182nd District Court of Harris County, Texas


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the 182nd District Court of Harris County (Texas) convicting him of delivering a controlled substance, revoking his probation for another offense, and sentencing him to six years confinement for the previous offense and 15 years for the subsequent offense, contending that the Texas Controlled Substances Act was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellant pled guilty to delivering a controlled substance. He also pled true to the state's motion to revoke probation for a prior offense of manufacturing a controlled substance. The court revoked his probation, and imposed a six-year sentence for the previous offense and a 15-year sentence for the subsequent offense. On review, appellant challenged the constitutionality of the Texas Controlled Substances Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15, § 4.03 (1982-1983). Further, he alleged that the motion to revoke probation failed to give him sufficient notice of the offense as charged because the pleadings alleged all three means of delivery enumerated in the statute. The court affirmed noting that the state's classification scheme must merely demonstrate a rational connection with its legislative goal to be constitutional. Because the state had a legitimate interest in regulating drug possession, which was effectuated by a statutory scheme, the court overruled appellant's first grounds of error. Finally, the court held that where the state alleged each type of delivery, appellant was on notice to prepare a defense for each.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court convicting appellant of delivery of a controlled substance, revoking appellant's probation for a prior offense, and sentencing him to six years confinement for the previous offense and 15 years for the subsequent offense was affirmed because the controlled substances law was constitutional and he had sufficient notice of the offense charged where the pleadings alleged three means of delivery.

 

1552 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Masters v. State


No. 3-82-153-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


653 S.W.2d 944; 1983 Tex. App. LEXIS 4608



June 22, 1983 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From the County Court at Law No. 3 of Travis County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate sought review of an order by the County Court at Law No. 3, Travis County, Texas, which entered a conviction based on appellant's plea of no contest for the offense of unlawfully carrying a weapon and ordered him to pay a fine of one dollar.


OVERVIEW: Appellant inmate was arrested for carrying a martial arts weapon on his person in violation of Texas Penal Code Ann §46.02 (1974). Appellant contended that he was constitutionally entitled to carry these weapons by U.S. Const. amend. II and Tex. Const. Art. I, §23 . The court held that U.S. Const. amend. II did not contemplate granting appellant the right to carry swords upon his person in a public place in order to be prepared in case he might need them. In fact, it merely protected the rights of the states to maintained armed militia under state control. The court further held that Tex. Const. Art. I, §23 gave the right to keep and bear arms directly to the individual. However, the legislature was entitled to reasonably regulate the wearing of arms. The court found that §46.02 and its predecessors had been universally held constitutional. Accordingly, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment because appellant suffered no deprivation of any right guaranteed by the Texas or United States Constitutions in his conviction.


OUTCOME: Trial court's judgment of conviction for the appellants of offense of unlawfully carrying a weapon was affirmed because appellant's state and federal constitutional rights were not violated in regards to his claimed right to keep and bear arms.

Peterson v. State


No. A14-82-789CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


659 S.W.2d 59; 1983 Tex. App. LEXIS 4670



June 16, 1983 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the 176th District Court of Harris County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment from the 176th District Court of Harris County (Texas) convicting him of murder because venue was not proven and the indictment was defective because it tracked the unconstitutional language of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 19.02(a)(2) as to his culpable mental state.


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged his conviction for murder on sufficiency of the evidence grounds claiming that the indictment was defective because it tracked the unconstitutional language of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 19.02(a)(2) (statute) for not requiring a culpable mental state for the act alleged to be dangerous to human life and because venue was not proven. The indictment alleged that appellant shot the victim at a named intersection in the county, causing the victim's death. The court affirmed the conviction, holding appellant failed to preserve the issue of improper venue, which was sufficiently proven, and holding the indictment was not defective for tracking the language of the statute, because the statute requiring only that appellant's culpable mental state be associated with the intent to cause serious bodily injury was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: Appellant's murder conviction was affirmed because appellant failed to preserve the issue of improper venue, and the indictment was not defective because the statute required only that appellant's culpable mental state be associated with intent to cause serious bodily injury.

Boutwell v. State

COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


653 S.W.2d 108; 1983 Tex. App. LEXIS 4616



June 8, 1983 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From the District Court of Bell County, 27th Judicial District, Honorable C.W. Duncan, Jr., Judge Presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction from the District Court of Bell County, 27th Judicial District (Texas), for the offense of sexual abuse of a child under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 21.10 (1974). Defendant alleged that the trial court erred in denying his pre-trial motions because defendant's conviction was barred by double jeopardy.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of the offense of sexual abuse of a child under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 21.10 (1974). Defendant appealed his conviction, contending that the trial court erred in denying his pre-trial motions to dispose of the charges on the ground that the conviction was barred by the doctrine of double jeopardy. Defendant was found guilty in an earlier jury trial of the offense of sexual abuse of a child, against a different person than the complainant in the appeal. Affirming the conviction, the court held that each crime was a product of a separate and distinct transaction and constituted a separate offense, so that defendant was not twice put in jeopardy.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for sexual abuse of a child, holding that each of defendant's crimes was the product of a separate and distinct transaction and constituted a separate offense and, therefore, his conviction was not barred by the doctrine of double jeopardy.

Wininger v. Department of Human Resources


No. 2-82-186-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Second District, Fort Worth


653 S.W.2d 376; 1983 Tex. App. LEXIS 4588



June 1, 1983 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied June 29, 1983.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the 30th District Court of Wichita County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed from the 30th District Court of Wichita County, Texas, which permanently enjoined plaintiff from operating a child care facility in her home pursuant to Texas Human Resources Code Chapter 42.


OVERVIEW: The court reversed and remanded the permanent injunction of plaintiff's operation of a childcare facility from her home. Tex. Hum. Res. Code Ann. §§ 42.076, 42.041 made it a Class B misdemeanor for anyone to operate a childcare facility without a license. At a hearing before the trial court prior to entry of the judgment, plaintiff stipulated to all facts necessary under the rules of the defendant Department of Human Resources to show that she operated the childcare facility in her home on a regular basis. Those facts, stipulated to by defendant, made it clear that plaintiff was operating a registered family home, which pursuant to Tex. Hum. Res. Code Ann. § 42.002(9) was an exception to the license requirement for childcare facilities. Therefore, defendant did not violate the licensing requirements as alleged in the complaint.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the permanent injunction on plaintiff's operation of a childcare facility from her home. Plaintiff did not violate the licensing requirements for operating a childcare facility because the facts indicated that plaintiff was operating a registered family home, which was an exception to the licensing requirement.

 

1556 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Boutwell v. State


No. 3-82-240-CR(T)


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


653 S.W.2d 100; 1983 Tex. App. LEXIS 4613



June 1, 1983 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From the District Court of Bell County, 146th Judicial District, William C. Black, Judge Presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the District Court of Bell County, 146th Judicial District (Texas), which convicted him of the offense of sexual abuse of a child under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 21.10 (1974). Defendant attacked the constitutionality of § 21.10 under the equal protection clause. Defendant challenged the lower court's failure to charge the jury that a witness was an accomplice as a matter of law.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of the offense of sexual abuse of a child pursuant to Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 21.10 (1974). Among other things, defendant attacked the constitutionality of § 21.10 under the equal protection clause. Defendant challenged the lower court's failure to charge the jury that a witness was an accomplice as a matter of law. The lower court judgment was affirmed. The court held that defendant was not entitled to challenge the constitutionality of the promiscuity defense because the evidence offered to the court did not show that the complaining witness was promiscuous. Age-based discrimination in § 21.10 furthered the state's interest in protecting children and the statutory scheme bore a fair and substantial relation to the objects that the legislation was designed to accomplish. The lower court was not bound to give an accomplice witness charge with respect to the witness because even thought the witness was an actor in a criminal transaction, he was not regarded as an accomplice because he was too young to be criminally responsible.


OUTCOME: The lower court judgment that convicted defendant of sexual abuse of a child was affirmed. The court held that defendant was not entitled to challenge the constitutionality of the promiscuity defense because the evidence offered to the court did not show that the complaining witness was promiscuous. The lower court was not bound to give an accomplice witness charge because the witness was too young to be criminally responsible.

Padgett v. State


No. 04-82-00026-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourth District, San Antonio


683 S.W.2d 453; 1983 Tex. App. LEXIS 5746



June 1, 1983 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied November 30, 1984.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the order from the trial court (Texas), which found him guilty of aggravated kidnapping and sentenced him to life imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of aggravated kidnapping and, finding both enhancement allegations to be true, the jury assessed punishment at life imprisonment. On appeal, defendant contended that a jury charge on the lesser included offense of kidnapping should have been given and that Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 20.04 was unconstitutional. The court held that § 20.04 was not vague as it clearly prohibited abduction with intent to terrorize the victim or a third person, nor was it overbroad as the aggravating element must be found to have been present to have raised the level of culpability to come within the prohibition of the aggravated kidnapping statute. The court held that where there was testimony raising the issue that defendant, if guilty at all, was guilty of only the lessor included offense, the charge on kidnapping as a lesser included offense of aggravated kidnapping should have been given to the jury when the defendant objected to its omission. The court reversed and remanded the judgment of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the order from the trial court that convicted defendant of aggravated kidnapping and, finding both enhancement allegations in the indictment to be true, sentenced him to life imprisonment. The court held that testimony raised the issue that defendant was guilty of only the lesser included offense of aggravated kidnapping, and as such the jury should have been given those instructions.
