PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the 139th District Court of Hidalgo County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant police officer sought review of an order from the 139th District Court of Hidalgo County (Texas) convicting him of official oppression by mistreatment.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, a police officer, was convicted of official oppression by mistreatment, under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 39.02(a)(1) (1974). Appellant was sentenced to probation and a fine. On appeal, appellant contended that he was denied his constitutional right to confront the witnesses against him when the trial court refused to allow him to cross-examine the victim as to certain matters designed to demonstrate the interest, motive, and bias of the victim against him. The court reversed and remanded for a new trial, finding that the trial court erred in denying appellant the opportunity to cross-examine the victim in the presence of the jury. The jury should have been given the opportunity to observe the victim's response to the questions. However, the court did find that upon viewing the evidence in the light most favorable to the jury's verdict, the evidence was sufficient to sustain the judgment of conviction.


OUTCOME: The order convicting appellant police officer of official oppression by mistreatment was reversed and remanded for a new trial because the trial court denied appellant the opportunity to question the victim in the presence of the jury.

Christian Jew Foundation v. State


No. 13,542


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin

CASE SUMMARY:

Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 5221b-5 (1982) and art. 5221b-7 (1971). Appellant claimed that it was statutorily exempt because it was a church within the meaning of the statute.


OVERVIEW: Appellant religious organization was ordered to pay monies to appellee state for its failure to properly pay into the Unemployment Compensation Fund (UCF) under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 5221b (1982) and 5221b-7 (1971). Appellant claimed that it was exempt from making the contributions to the UCF because it was a church. The court in reversing held that appellee had presented no evidence to the trial court showing that appellant was not a church as statutorily defined and that appellant was in fact a church within the meaning of the statute. It also said that the trial court erred in its conclusion of law that appellant was subject to the mandatory contributions required by UCF. The court held that appellee could take nothing by its suit.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's decision that appellant religious organization was liable to appellee state for appellant's failure to pay monies into the Unemployment Compensation Fund. Appellant met the statutory definition of church, so it was exempt from payment requirements.

Pope v. State


No. B14-82-589-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


667 S.W.2d 163; 1983 Tex. App. LEXIS 4453



May 12, 1983 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Second Opinion Rehearing Denied August 11, 1983, Reported at: 667 S.W.2d 163 at 166. Discretionary Review Refused February 8, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 177th District Court of Harris County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the 177th District Court of Harris County (Texas), which convicted him on a plea of nolo contendere for possession of cocaine. Appellant contested the sufficiency of evidence to support his plea, his denial of a speedy trial, and the constitutionality of the Texas Controlled Substance Act for not defining cocaine.


OVERVIEW: Appellant pleaded nolo contendere and was convicted of possession of cocaine. On appeal, the court rejected his claim that the evidence was insufficient to support his plea because the statement of facts did not show that the signed stipulation of evidence was offered. After reviewing the record, the court held that the stipulation was introduced and that the evidence was sufficient to support his plea. The court held that his nolo contendere plea waived all non-jurisdictional defects, including a claim that he was denied a speedy trial. Affirming the judgment convicting appellant, the court found his attack on the constitutionality of the Texas Controlled Substance Act unimpressive because its failure to define cocaine did not render the statute defective or too vague to prevent a determination of what conduct was prohibited.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for possession of cocaine holding that the record showed the introduction of a stipulation of evidence to sufficiently support his plea of nolo contendere. The court held that the plea waived his claim that he was denied a speedy trial and that the statute he violated was not unconstitutionally vague by its failure to define cocaine.

Hubert v. Harte-Hanks Tex. Newspapers


No. 13,580


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


652 S.W.2d 546; 1983 Tex. App. LEXIS 4412



May 11, 1983 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied June 8, 1983.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the District Court of Travis County, 147th Judicial District.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a state university, sought review from a judgment of the District Court of Travis County (Texas), which granted a writ of mandamus filed by appellee newspaper to compel appellants to make available the names and qualifications of candidates for the office of president of appellants' school pursuant to the Open Records Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6252-17a (1982).


OVERVIEW: Appellants, a state university, challenged the grant of a writ of mandamus filed by appellee newspaper to compel appellants to make available the names and qualifications of candidates for the office of president of appellants' school pursuant to the Open Records Act (Act), Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6252-17a (1982). The court held that appellee sought the names of candidates for president which were not facts of a highly embarrassing or intimate nature, or which, if publicized, would be highly objectionable to a reasonable person. The court found that the public was legitimately concerned with the names and qualifications of candidates for the presidencies of state universities. The court concluded that no invasion of privacy occurred and a liberal construction of the Act compelled disclosure of information, even when disclosure might cause inconvenience or embarrassment for some persons. Accordingly, the court affirmed the judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment against appellants, a state university, and in favor of appellee newspaper seeking to discover the names and qualifications of candidates for president of appellants' school pursuant to the Open Records Act. The court held that the names of candidates for president were not facts of a highly embarrassing or intimate nature which would offend a reasonable person and that no invasion of privacy occurred.

Lalande v. State


No. 08-82-00141-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Eighth District, El Paso


651 S.W.2d 402; 1983 Tex. App. LEXIS 4443



May 11, 1983 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from 205th District Court Of El Paso County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged judgment of the 205th District Court Of El Paso County, Texas, which convicted him of capital murder. Appellant alleged grounds that trial court erred in admitting the testimony of appellant's fellow county jail inmate subject to Tex. Crim. Proc. Code Ann. art. 38.22 and that certain evidence was produced by an allegedly invalid arrest of and invalid search while out of state.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of capital murder after being stopped and arrested in California for violation of San Francisco Municipal Code Section 1291(b), carrying a prohibited weapon, searched incident thereto, and returned to Texas pursuant to the outstanding murder warrant. Appellant challenged conviction on grounds that the trial court erred in admitting the testimony of appellant's fellow county jail inmate, and that various items of evidence produced by the allegedly invalid California arrest and search of his belongings. Affirming, the court held that where fellow inmate was not acting as an agent of law enforcement personnel at the time he received appellant's confession, the confession was not the product of custodial interrogation and was not subject to Tex. Crim. Proc. Code Ann. art. 38.22. Further, although the state failed to establish probable cause for the California arrest, emphasizing that appellant relied solely on federal constitutional grounds, no prophylactic purpose was served by applying an exclusionary rule where it would not serve to dissuade improper police conduct in California.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the capital murder conviction because appellant's fellow inmate was not acting as an agent of law enforcement when appellant allegedly confessed to him and the confession was therefore admissible. While the state failed to establish probable cause for the California arrest, the exclusionary rule was not applied where it would not serve any purpose other than to free a convicted felon.

Amarillo v. Langley


No. 9385


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Seventh District, Amarillo


651 S.W.2d 906; 1983 Tex. App. LEXIS 4440



April 29, 1983 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied May 18, 1983.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the District Court of Potter County; 108th Judicial District.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review of a judgment in the 108th District Court of Potter County (Texas), entered in favor of appellee citizens based on 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 and Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. § 6252-19 (1982), for injuries caused to appellees by appellant's police officer. Appellant claimed immunity, insufficient and improperly admitted evidence, erroneous jury instructions, and error in the award of attorney's fees and judgment interest.


OVERVIEW: Appellant city's police officer used a patrol vehicle to block appellee citizens, who were on motorcycles, from fleeing after a traffic violation, resulting in a collision. Appellees brought claims against appellant under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 and Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. § 6252-19 (1982), and were awarded a judgment against appellant for their injuries. Appellant sought reversal of the judgment, claiming insufficient and improperly admitted evidence, erroneous jury instructions and issues, error in the award of attorney's fees and judgment interest, and immunity under the Texas Tort Claims Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. § 6252-19 (1982). The court affirmed the judgment and held that the evidence showed that the officer acted pursuant to departmental policy and caused the collision with a patrol unit and a parked car. The court further found that the injuries, including one appellee losing a leg, were sufficient to justify the damage award, and under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1988, appellees were entitled to attorney's fees and interest, which were also supported by the evidence. The court further held appellant could not assert immunity under § 1983.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, because appellant city was liable for the use of excessive force by the officer hired by appellant city, which caused injuries to appellee citizens, and appellant could not assert immunity from appellees' federal civil rights action based on the officer complying with departmental procedures.

Nesloney v. State


No. A14-82-708-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


653 S.W.2d 582; 1983 Tex. App. LEXIS 4379



April 28, 1983 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from 258th District Court of Trinity County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a decision from the 258th District Court, Trinity County (Texas), convicting him under Tex. Parks & Wild. Code Ann. § 47.037 (1976) for refusing to allow an employee of the Department of Texas Parks and Wildlife to inspect aquatic products in his possession. Appellant asserted that § 47.037 violated the U.S. Const. amend. IV and Tex. Const. art. 1, § 9.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was approached outside of a building that he claimed was one of his residences, by a game warden who asked appellant to see his fishing license. Appellant complied with the request but refused to allow the warden to inspect his residence without a warrant. Appellant was convicted under Tex. Parks & Wild. Code Ann. § 47.037 (1976) for refusing to allow the game warden to inspect aquatic products in his possession. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded with instructions to dismiss the prosecution. The court found that § 47.037 contained no procedural safeguards. Section 47.037 gave unequivocal authorization to wardens to search and the requirement of a warrant was not even mentioned. The court held that § 47.037 on its face violated the U.S. Const. amend. IV and the Tex. Const. art. 1, § 9 because it allowed a criminal prosecution of one who asserted his right not to be searched unless the search was authorized by a neutral officer who believed that probable cause for it existed. Appellant would have been afforded protection even if the building were determined to have been a business instead of a residence.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded with instructions to dismiss the prosecution. The court found that a provision of the Texas Parks and Wildlife Code allowing a game warden to inspect a residence without a warrant violated the Fourth Amendment and the Texas Constitution because it gave unequivocal authorization to the game warden to search without a warrant, and contained no procedural safeguards.

Presley v. State


No. C14-82-614-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


655 S.W.2d 237; 1983 Tex. App. LEXIS 4335



April 20, 1983 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Discretionary Review Refused September 14, 1983.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 174th District Court of Harris County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a decision of the 174th District of Harris County (Texas), which convicted him of possession of a controlled substance and imposed a sentence of 10 years' confinement, after appellant waived a jury trial and entered a plea of guilty.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was charged with possession of less than 28 grams of cocaine and he waived a jury trial and entered a plea of guilty. The trial court found appellant guilty of possession of a controlled substance and imposed a sentence of 10 years' confinement. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15 was constitutional pursuant to Tex. Const. art. III, § 35 because the caption to the enabling legislation did meet constitutional requirements concerning the drafting of legislation. The caption was clearly sufficient to put a caption reader on notice that almost anything related to offenses and penalties under the Texas Controlled Substances Act was possible for violations of the act.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court, which found appellant guilty of possession of a controlled substance and imposed a sentence of ten years' confinement because the caption to the relevant statute was constitutional because it put the reader on notice that anything related to controlled substances offenses and penalties was possible therein.

 

1566 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Saunders v. Saunders


No. B14-82-080-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


650 S.W.2d 534; 1983 Tex. App. LEXIS 4245



April 14, 1983 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the 246th District Court of Harris County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father appealed an order of the 246th District Court, Harris County (Texas), which required him to pay child support under the Uniform Reciprocal Enforcement of Support Act, Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 21.01 et seq. (1975). The trial court ordered appellant to pay child support of $ 120.00 per month.


OVERVIEW: Appellant father sought review of an order requiring him to pay child support of $ 120 per month pursuant to the Uniform Reciprocal Enforcement of Support Act, Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 21.01 et seq. (1975). The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The trial court did not err in admitting the foreign certificate and petition for child support into evidence because the documents met the requirements of Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 21.36 (a), (b) and Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 3731a, § 2. Appellant failed to make a bill of exceptions, and the court could not speculate as to whether his testimony would have raised the defense of non-paternity. Appellant's rights under U.S. Const. amend. VI were not violated because the right to confront witnesses only applied in a criminal prosecution. Appellant made no bill of exceptions to the trial court's refusal to allow evidence of non-access to his spouse when he attempted to raise the issue of paternity. The trial court was not obligated to continue the case.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order requiring appellant father to pay child support. The foreign certificate and petition for child support met statutory requirements and were admissible. Appellant failed to make a bill of exceptions to disallowed testimony and the court therefore could not evaluate his claims. His Sixth Amendment rights were not violated because the right to confront witnesses applied only to criminal proceedings.

Atkins v. State


No. 05-83-00075-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


667 S.W.2d 540; 1983 Tex. App. LEXIS 4300



April 14, 1983 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From a District Court of Dallas County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the District Court of Dallas County (Texas), entered after a jury convicted him of theft of a trade secret in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 31.05. Defendant claimed error in the trial court's denial of his motion to quash the indictment, which he alleged was not sufficiently specific.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged and convicted of theft of trade secrets based upon an indictment which largely tracked the language of the statute, Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 31.05. The indictment identified the property in question as "architectural plans, designed and drawn by" a named architect. In reversing the indictment, the court found that the crime was a broad-based one and thus, in order to meet the statutory and constitutional guarantees with respect to indictments, the state was required to include language therein which specifically identified the property in question and any other particulars relevant to the crime. Notice to defendant that he was charged with theft of "architectural plans" did not meet the specificity required. The court, in so ruling, noted that the record in this case was replete with information, such the structure these plans were intended for, the name of the person who bought the plans, and their identifying number.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction and remanded the case because the indictment tracked the language of a broad-based offense but failed to state with specificity the particulars of the crime defendant allegedly committed. Thus, it did not give defendant adequate notice upon which he could have prepared a defense.

 

1568 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Mathis v. State


No. 05-81-01106-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


650 S.W.2d 532; 1983 Tex. App. LEXIS 4328



April 13, 1983 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From a District Court of Dallas County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction in the trial court, Dallas County (Texas), of delivery of the controlled substance of phenmetrazine.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted delivery of the controlled substance of phenmetrazine. On appeal, the court affirmed the conviction, holding that the statute under which defendant was charged, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15, § 4.02(d)(1)(D) (1982-83), was not unconstitutionally vague because it clearly stated that it was an offense to deliver the controlled substance phenmetrazine. In addition, failure to define "abuse" or "potential" was not grounds for striking down the statute. The court found that the phrase "having a potential for abuse associated with a stimulant effect on the central nervous system" in the indictment and statute was merely a factual matter which the state had to prove, and that the phrase had an understandable meaning. The court also held that the laboratory analysis was properly admitted under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 3636e (1982-82), as the supervisor of the laboratory testified that the analysis was performed under his supervision and the technician who performed it was qualified to do so.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the defendant's conviction, as the indictment and the statute under which defendant was convicted were not unconstitutionally vague.

 

1569 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Peters v. State


No. 05-81-01053-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


651 S.W.2d 31; 1983 Tex. App. LEXIS 4327



April 8, 1983 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Discretionary Review Granted July 6, 1983.


PRIOR HISTORY: From a County Court of Dallas County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of two judgments of a county court of Dallas County (Texas), which denied defendant's writ of habeas corpus and convicted him for driving while intoxicated.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with driving a motor vehicle on a public street while intoxicated. He filed an application to defer further proceedings and be placed on probation without an adjudication of guilt. The trial court granted his application and ordered commitment to jail until he paid a fine. Defendant filed a writ of habeas corpus, alleging that no fine could be imposed without adjudication of guilt. The state filed a motion in trial court to proceed, and defendant objected because of the pendency of the habeas corpus appeal. The trial court overruled and revoked his probation. The court dismissed defendant's application for habeas corpus because it became moot upon the adjudication of guilt, conviction, and sentence. Pendency of the habeas corpus appeal did not affect the court's authority to proceed because it was not an appeal from a final judgment of conviction. The court affirmed the conviction, concluding that it could not consider the constitutionality of Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 42.13, § 3d(a) because the trial court's decision to proceed with adjudication was not reviewable by the court pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 42.13, § 3d(b).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction for driving while intoxicated and dismissed defendant's application for habeas corpus, holding that the pendency of the habeas corpus appeal did not affect the court's authority to proceed because it was not an appeal from a final judgment of conviction, and that the trial court's decision to proceed with adjudication while the habeas corpus appeal was pending was not reviewable by the court.

 

1570 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Bowen v. State


No. 2-82-224-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Second District, Fort Worth


649 S.W.2d 384; 1983 Tex. App. LEXIS 4312



April 6, 1983 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From Criminal District Court #2 of Tarrant County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Criminal District Court #2 of Tarrant County (Texas), which revoked her probation for failure to pay costs, probation fees, and restitution.


OVERVIEW: The state filed a petition to revoke defendant's probation. The state subsequently waived its allegation of a new offense and proceeded to trial solely on defendant's failure to pay costs, probation fees, and restitution. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment revoking probation. The court held that defendant's inability to pay was an affirmative defense to revocation which she was required to prove by a preponderance of the evidence under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 42.12, § 8(c). As she failed to raise this affirmative defense, the state was not required to prove that she had the ability to pay and intentionally failed. The court also held that the affirmative defense created by art. 42.12, § 8(c) did not violate defendant's rights to due process and equal protection. The court found that the statutory scheme did not create a presumption that the probationer could pay and intentionally did not pay but merely required the probationer to come forward and explain the breach of the contract. The court held that art. 42.12, § 8(c) did not violate defendant's right against self-incrimination as she could have shown her inability to pay without taking the stand.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment revoking defendant's probation. The court held that because defendant did not raise the statutory affirmative defense of inability to pay fees, the state was not required to prove that she had the ability to pay and intentionally failed. The court also held that the statutory affirmative defense did not violate defendant's rights to due process and equal protection.

 

1571 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Lopez v. State


No. 04-81-00278-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourth District, San Antonio


651 S.W.2d 830; 1983 Tex. App. LEXIS 4183



March 30, 1983 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the 187th District Court of Bexar County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction from the 187th District Court of Bexar County (Texas), for the attempted murders of an assistant district attorney, and an acquaintance of appellant, and for an aggravated assault on a bailiff, contending that the trial court erred in failing to quash the indictments for failure to specify the manner in which appellant had the specific intent to commit murder under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 19.02 (1981).


OVERVIEW: The trial court convicted appellant for the attempted murders of an assistant district attorney, and an acquaintance of appellant, and for an aggravated assault on a bailiff. On appeal, appellant challenged the sufficiency of the evidence to show the weapon used to stab the bailiff was a deadly weapon. No knife was ever recovered. The court found the jury was justified, from the evidence and testimony adduced, to conclude that the same knife was used in all three stabbings, and thus that the weapon was deadly. Appellant further contended the trial court erred in failing to quash the indictments for failure to specify the manner in which appellant had the specific intent to commit murder under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 19.02 (1981). The thrust of appellant's argument was that the indictments did not put him on notice whether the state sought to prove that he intended to cause death under § 19.02(a)(1) or intended to cause serious bodily injury resulting in death under § 19.02(a)(2). The court held that appellant was clearly informed that the murder intended was a § 19.02(a)(1) type murder because he attempted (intended) to cause the death of the complainants. The court affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction on the grounds that appellant was clearly informed that the murder intended was in violation of a certain statute because he attempted (intended) to cause the death of the complainant. Nothing in the indictments indicated that appellant desired anything less than the deaths of the complainants when he used a knife to perform the act of stabbing.

 

1572 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Wolff v. State


No. 3-82-238-CR(T)


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


661 S.W.2d 130; 1983 Tex. App. LEXIS 4215



March 30, 1983 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From the County Court at Law No. 2 of Bell County.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, who was convicted by a jury in the County Court at Law No. 2, Bell County (Texas) of misdemeanor driving while intoxicated, challenged his conviction.


OVERVIEW: The court reversed appellant's conviction of driving while intoxicated, finding that the trial court had failed to instruct the jury properly as to the presumption of intoxication shown through a breathalyzer test result of .10 percent or above under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 67011-5, § 3(a) (1977). It held that the trial court erred in not telling the jury that the facts giving rise to the presumption had to be proved beyond a reasonable doubt, as required by Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 2.05 (Supp. 1982), thereby in effect telling the jury that the presumption was mandatory. Although appellant had not challenged the instruction, but based his appeal on other grounds, the court found that the erroneous instruction required reversal as a fundamental error because it deprived him of his due process rights. It remanded the case, writing that the evidence was sufficient for the jury to have found guilt beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: Finding that the trial court had erred in instructing the jury as to the presumption raised by a breathalyzer test result of .10 percent or above, the court reversed appellant's conviction of driving while intoxicated. It remanded the case, finding that the evidence was sufficient for the jury to have found guilt beyond a reasonable doubt.

 

1573 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Williams v. Northrup


No. 12-81-0063-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Twelfth District, Tyler


649 S.W.2d 740; 1983 Tex. App. LEXIS 4211



March 24, 1983 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied March 27, 1983.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 11th Judicial District Court of Harris County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant plan trustees challenged a decision from the 11th Judicial District Court of Harris County (Texas), rendering judgment in appellee ex-employee's favor for the money forfeited, prejudgment interest, and attorney fees, in his action for recovery of his alleged vested percentage in the employer's contribution under a thrift plan, which percentage was forfeited for appellee's knowing violation of a non-competition provision of the plan.


OVERVIEW: The trial court rendered judgment in favor of appellee ex-employee in his action against appellant plan trustees for recovery of his alleged vested percentage in the employer's contribution under a thrift plan, which percentage was forfeited by appellants because of appellee's knowing violation of a non-competition provision of the plan. On appeal, the threshold issue was whether or not appellants' failure to notify appellee to cease his competitive conduct within a prescribed period of time in violation of the terms of the plan was necessary to permit a forfeiture of the employer's contribution. The court held that strict adherence to the terms of the trust was required. It was improper to speculate whether appellee would have discontinued his competitive conduct to prevent a forfeiture. This disputed fact issue was not submitted to the jury, and since appellants had the burden of submitting this issue their failure to request such submission, or to object to its omission, waived such issue. The court found appellee was not entitled to prejudgment interest, reversed and modified the judgment to conform to the jury's verdict regarding attorney fees.


OUTCOME: The court reversed, and rendered in part, modified in part, and as modified, affirmed the judgment below in favor of appellee ex-employee and against appellant plan trustees for money forfeited, prejudgment interest and attorney fees. The court reversed and rendered by deleting the award of prejudgment interest, and modified that part of the judgment awarding attorney fees to conform to the jury's verdict.

OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of possession of marihuana under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15, § 4.015 (1981). Defendant argued that the title of the bill underlying the statute contained more than one subject, that it was inadequate to give notice to the effect of the bill, and that it was violative of Tex. Ex parte Progreso Independent School Dist.


No. 2503cv


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Thirteenth District, Corpus Christi


650 S.W.2d 158; 1983 Tex. App. LEXIS 4209



March 17, 1983 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied April 14, 1983.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the 93rd District Court of Hidalgo County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayers challenged the decision of the 93rd District Court, Hidalgo County (Texas), which declared that the bond election conducted by appellee Progreso Independent School District was proper and valid. Appellee brought a declaratory judgment action to determine the validity of the election that was consolidated with an action brought by appellants to enjoin issuance of the bonds.


OVERVIEW: Appellant taxpayers brought an action to enjoin issuance of bonds following a bond election. Appellee Progreso Independent School District filed a declaratory judgment action to have the bond election declared valid. The two actions were consolidated, and the trial court found that the election was proper in all respects and valid. Appellants sought review. The court first found that the Texas school bond election laws, in particular Tex. Educ. Code Ann. § 20.04, were unconstitutional in that they prohibited those who did not own property in the district from voting on a school bond issue. The court, however, determined that it could strike the offending provisions and that, as struck, the Texas laws authorizing school bond elections were valid. The court also determined that voters were not misled by language in the bond issue concerning interest rates and that sufficient notice was given that the actual rate could be higher than initially anticipated. Accordingly, the judgment of the trial court was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed because, after striking down as unconstitutional the requirement that voters own property within the district, the Texas law authorizing school bond elections was valid, and the proposition gave adequate notice that interest rate on bonds could be higher than initially anticipated.

Lunsford v. Board of Nurse Examiners for State


No. 13,548


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


648 S.W.2d 391; 1983 Tex. App. LEXIS 4087



March 3, 1983 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied March 30, 1983.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the District Court of Travis County, 200th Judicial District.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant nurse challenged the 200th District Court, Travis County, Texas, which affirmed the decision of appellee Board of Nurse Examiners suspending appellant's nursing license pursuant to Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4525(a)(9) because of unprofessional conduct.


OVERVIEW: Appellant nurse had her nursing license suspended pursuant to Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4525(a)(9), by appellee Board of Nurse Examiners for the State of Texas because of an incident that resulted in a patient's death. While on duty in an emergency room, appellant was told by a physician to send the patient to another hospital 24 miles away and while she suspected cardiac involvement, appellant told the patient's companion to speed to the other hospital and never checked the patient's vitals. Appellee found that appellant's conduct had been unprofessional and dishonorable conduct likely to injure the public. Appellant challenged the district court's order affirming the administrative order of appellee. The court found that reasonable minds could agree on the appellee's order revoking appellant's license, and therefore, such order was based upon substantial evidence. The court held that appellant had a duty to evaluate the medical status of the patient and institute appropriate nursing care. The court also held that the appellee's finding of fact was sufficient to meet the requirements of Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6252-13a, § 16(b). The judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's ruling which affirmed the decision of appellee Board of Nurse Examiners to suspend appellant nurse's license. The court held that the order was based on substantial evidence and that appellant had a duty to evaluate the patient and institute appropriate care.

Lamm v. State


No. 13-81-14-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Thirteenth District, Corpus Christi


653 S.W.2d 495; 1983 Tex. App. LEXIS 4059



February 24, 1983 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied April 7, 1983.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Court at Law No. 2 of Cameron County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction for speeding from the County Court at Law No. 2 at Cameron County, Texas.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was found guilty of speeding and fined $ 101.00. Appellant challenged. The court held that the trial court did not err in denying appellant's motion to quash the complaint for allegedly failing to reveal the place were the event occurred. The state's pleading came well within the acceptable limits of giving appellant notice of the location where the offense allegedly occurred. Thus, appellant received all the notice to which he was entitled, and the complaint was specific enough to bar another action for the same offense. Likewise, there was no error in denying the motion to quash for failing to allege a culpable mental state because the Court of Criminal Appeals had previously rejected this claim in another decision. The court further held that Tex. Code Crim. Proc. art. 6701d, §§ 167-169B were not unconstitutional delegations of the legislature's authority. Rather the limitations on the discretion of the State Highway and Public Transportation Commission were necessary to effect the legislature's purpose and were capable of reasonable application. Accordingly, the conviction was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction of speeding because the trial court did not err in denying appellant's motion to quash the complaint against him, and the statutory provisions complained of were not unconstitutional delegations of the legislature's authority.

 

1579 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Delgado v. Burns


No. B14-82-553-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


650 S.W.2d 505; 1983 Tex. App. LEXIS 4243



February 24, 1983 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied April 28, 1983.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 149th District Court of Brazoria County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a patient and her husband, challenged the order of the 149th District Court of Brazoria County (Texas), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee doctor and sustained his plea of limitation in the suit for medical malpractice. Appellants contended that the limitations statute, Tex. Ins. Code Ann. art. 5.82, § 4, was unconstitutional and that the "discovery rule" applied to the statute.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, a patient and her husband, brought a suit for medical malpractice against appellee doctor. Appellee filed a plea of limitation and motion for summary judgment under Tex. Ins. Code Ann. art. 5.82, § 4, and claimed that the action was time-barred. The trial court sustained the plea and granted summary judgment in favor of appellee. Appellant challenged the ruling and contended that the statute was unconstitutional, and that the "discovery rule" applied to the statute. The court affirmed the trial court's ruling and held that where appellant failed to raise the issue of the statute's constitutionality at the trial court, it was not reviewable. The court found that the limitations statute provided that an action had to be commenced within two years after it accrued, and that the courts had engrafted the "discovery rule" into the statute. In examining a subsequent legislative amendment to the statute, the court found that the language regarding when the cause of action "accrued" was deleted. The court held that the "discovery rule" no longer applied, and summary judgment was proper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment in favor of appellee doctor, sustaining appellee's plea of limitation in a medical malpractice suit by appellants, a patient and her husband. Appellants did not raise the issue of the limitation statute's constitutionality in the trial court, and in amending the statute the legislature deleted the reference as to when a cause of action accrued. Therefore, the "discovery rule" was not applicable.

Mills v. Habluetzel


No. 2683cv


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Thirteenth District, Corpus Christi


648 S.W.2d 18; 1983 Tex. App. LEXIS 4071



February 17, 1983 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Reversed and Remanded from the U.S. Supreme Court.



DISPOSITION:  Reversed and Remanded


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant child's appeal of the dismissal by the trial court (Texas), of appellant's original petition to establish a parent-child relationship between appellee father and appellant was remanded to the court by the United States Supreme Court, after reversal of the court's decision to affirm.


OVERVIEW: The Texas Department of Human Resources and appellant child filed an original petition to establish the parent-child relationship between appellee father and appellant. In his original answer, appellee asserted that appellant's cause of action was barred by limitation under Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 13.01, as it then existed. The trial court dismissed with prejudice the cause of action as barred by the one-year statute of limitations. Timely appeal of the dismissal was perfected to the court, and the court affirmed. Timely appeal was perfected to the United States Supreme Court, which then ruled that the one-year limitation under the 1975 enactment of Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 13.01 was unconstitutional as violative of the Equal Protection Clause of U.S. Const. amend. XIV. The U.S. Supreme Court reversed the court's decision and judgment, and remanded the case to the court for further proceedings not inconsistent with its opinion. The court then reversed and remanded for a new trial, in light of the U.S. Supreme Court's opinion.


OUTCOME: The cause was reversed and remanded, as the trial court's order of dismissal was based directly upon a one-year statute of limitations, and the statute was now held unconstitutional. A new trial was required, pursuant to applicable civil procedure rules. As the issue of any applicable statute of limitation in this type of action was not properly before the court in the appeal, the court declined to address it.

Ragan v. State


No. 10-82-100-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Tenth District, Waco


649 S.W.2d 662; 1983 Tex. App. LEXIS 3980



February 10, 1983 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From 13th Judicial District Court Navarro County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction in the13th Judicial District Court, Navarro County (Texas) of violating the Texas Controlled Substances Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15, §§ 4.05(a) and (b)(4), in that he knowingly or intentionally delivered a quantity of marihuana of five pounds or less but more than four ounces.


OVERVIEW: In challenging his conviction, appellant claimed that the amendment to the Texas Controlled Substances Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15, under which he was convicted, violated Tex. Const. art. III, § 35. The court held that the changes in § 4.05 and § 4.01 of art. 4476-15 by the amendment in question clearly related to offenses and criminal penalties under the Texas Controlled Substances Act, and thus were within the announced purpose of the amendatory act as set forth in its title, and they were not "remote" from the subject of the original act. The court affirmed, holding that notice of these changes was adequately expressed in the title of the amendatory act within the meaning and requirement of Tex. Const. art. III, § 35 because the only changes made by the amendment that related to appellant's case changed the offense committed by appellant from a third-degree felony to a second-degree felony due to the amount of marihuana delivered, and also changed the penalty for the offense.


OUTCOME: Appellant's conviction of violating the Texas Controlled Substances Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15 was affirmed because the amendment to the act put any reasonable caption reader on notice that he would find new matter in the body of the bill, and the amended act was not "remote" from the subject of the original act.

 

1582 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Huffines v. State


No. 05-81-00997-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


646 S.W.2d 612; 1983 Tex. App. LEXIS 3945



February 3, 1983 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied March 7, 1983.


PRIOR HISTORY: From a District Court of Dallas County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from his conviction in the District Court, Dallas County (Texas), for possession of a firearm silencer proscribed by Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 46.06(a)(4). Appellant alleged that his retrial and conviction subjected him to double jeopardy, his punishment was unlawful, he was entitled to dismissal of his indictment under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 51.14, and § 46.06(a)(4) was unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: After a prior trial in which the jury could not reach a verdict, defendant was convicted upon a confession of guilt more than 120 days after being surrendered to Texas from another jurisdiction pursuant to the Interstate Agreement on Detainers Act (Act). On appeal from this conviction, the court held that defendant's second and current trial did not subject him to double jeopardy because nothing in the record indicated that a new trial was granted on grounds of insufficient evidence. The court held that his punishment was authorized by law because punishment was no greater in the new trial than the punishment imposed in the first trial. Although defendant was not tried within the 120 days' time after his surrender to Texas from another jurisdiction as required by Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 51.14 of the Act, the court found that the parties agreed to a continuance, which was deemed necessary and reasonable. Lastly, the court held that Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 46.06 was not unconstitutionally vague because the definition of firearm silencer was ordinary and obvious and thus reasonably understood to a person of common intelligence.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and punishment for possession of a firearm silencer was affirmed because he was not subjected to double jeopardy for the new trial was not issued on the basis of insufficient evidence, his punishment was authorized by law, he was not entitled to dismissal because the delay was a result of a continuance, and the offense prescribed by statute was constitutional as enacted and as applied.

Exxon Co., U.S.A. v. State


No. 01-82-0125-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


646 S.W.2d 536; 1982 Tex. App. LEXIS 5532



December 16, 1982 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Discretionary Review Refused March 23, 1983.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Harris County Criminal Court at Law No. 9.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant oil company challenged a decision of the Harris County Criminal Court at Law No. 9 (Texas), which convicted it of air pollution in violation of Tex. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4477-5b.


OVERVIEW: Appellant oil company was convicted of air pollution in violation of Tex. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4477-5b. On appeal, the court affirmed the conviction and held that the trial court did not err in refusing to quash the information because art. 4477-5b was a strict liability statute and no culpable mental state had to be alleged.
