The information adequately stated an offense with elements from the statute that were not vague. The court held that the statute was enforceable by the county in the form presented and was properly supported by an affidavit of a credible person.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant oil company's conviction of air pollution because there was no requirement that the information allege a culpable mental state. The court further determined that the statute was not unconstitutionally vague and was prosecuted by the correct authority under a valid information.

 

1584 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Hoyle v. State


No. A14-81-664-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


650 S.W.2d 97; 1982 Tex. App. LEXIS 5543



December 16, 1982 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied January 13, 1983. Discretionary Review Granted April 6, 1983.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 8 of Harris County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the County Criminal Court at Law No. 8 of Harris County (Texas), which convicted appellant for promotion of obscenity, alleging the information was insufficient to put appellant on notice of the charges against him and Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 43.23(e) (Supp. 1982) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: A vice-officer entered a bookstore, and purchased a magazine, which was later determined to be obscene, from appellant. Appellant challenged his conviction for promotion of obscenity. On appeal, the court affirmed the conviction and held the trial court did not err in refusing to quash the information because the information fairly informed appellant of the charges against him and enabled him to plead an acquittal or conviction and bar future prosecutions for the same offense. The term sodomy in the information was sufficient to put appellant on notice of the acts alleged to be obscene and an acquittal or a conviction served as an adequate bar to future prosecutions. Additionally, the information charged appellant with promotion of obscenity through the sale of the magazine and whether the magazine depicted one or more obscene representations was irrelevant to the act of promoting the material. Further, Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 43.23(e) (Supp. 1982), was constitutional because the presumption that appellant knew the content and character of the material was valid and rational, as appellant worked in an adult bookstore and the covers of the magazine depicted acts of oral sodomy.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction for promotion of obscenity and held the refusal to quash the information was not erroneous because the term sodomy therein fairly put appellant on notice of the charges and the statute was constitutional because the permissive presumption was rational. A jury could have found appellant knew of the content and character of the material because he worked in an adult bookstore and the magazine depicted oral sodomy.

 

1585 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


August A. Busch & Co. v. Texas Alcoholic Beverage Com.


No. 9101


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Sixth District, Texarkana


649 S.W.2d 652; 1982 Tex. App. LEXIS 5552



December 14, 1982 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied January 11, 1983.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the 98th Judicial District Court of Travis County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant beer manufacturer challenged a judgment of the 98th Judicial District Court of Travis County, Texas, which affirmed the denial of its applications to renew six licenses by appellee Texas Alcoholic Beverage Commission.


OVERVIEW: Appellant beer manufacturer's applications to renew six licenses to distribute beer were denied by appellee Texas Alcoholic Beverage Commission because Tex. Alco. Bev. Code Ann. § 102.18 prohibited a licensed alcoholic beverage manufacturer from having a license to distribute alcohol. The trial court affirmed the denial. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that § 102.18 was constitutional because it had a reasonable basis and,even though it only applied to appellant, it was not so inflexibly fixed as to prevent its being applied to other entities or persons. The court found that a reasonable basis for § 102.18 is that the public interest was served by the prohibition of vertical integration within the alcoholic beverage industry and that the law reasonably prevented industry domination by a few.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of appellant beer manufacturer's applications for licenses to distribute beer, holding that the statute that prohibited granting beer manufacturers licenses to distribute alcohol was constitutional because it had a reasonable basis, and even though it only applied to appellant, it was not so inflexibly fixed as to prevent its being applied to other entities or persons.

 

1586 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Cross v. State


No. 05-81-00812-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


646 S.W.2d 514; 1982 Tex. App. LEXIS 5472



December 8, 1982 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied February 3, 1983. Discretionary Review Refused May 11, 1983.


PRIOR HISTORY: From a County Court, of Dallas County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the decision of a County Court, of Dallas County, Texas, which convicted him of cruelty to an animal under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 42.11(a)(2) (1982).


OVERVIEW: Appellant alleged that the information failed to give him proper notice of the offense, that the terms "unreasonably" and "necessary" were vague, and that without a more specific allegation he could not adequately prepare his defense even though the information tracked the language in the statute. The trial court denied his motion to quash the indictment and appellant was convicted of cruelty to an animal. The court affirmed the judgment and found the information was sufficient. It found that in order to prepare his defense, appellant was only required to meet the state's proof that the food provided was not sufficient in quantity and quality to sustain the horse, which information was a matter of common knowledge among persons familiar with the care of horses. It held that because the information alleged an unreasonable failure to provide necessary food, appellant could reasonably anticipate that the state's proof would concern both insufficient quantity and insufficient quality of the food provided, and prepare his defense accordingly.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that the information gave appellant fair notice and overruled his motion to quash because it put appellant on notice of the offense and he could anticipate the state's proof would concern both the quantity and quality of food provided to a horse.

 

1587 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Oliver v. State


Nos. 2-81-248-CR, 2-81-249-CR, 2-81-250-CR, 2-81-251-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Second District, Fort Worth


644 S.W.2d 135; 1982 Tex. App. LEXIS 5551



December 8, 1982 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied January 5, 1983. Discretionary Review Granted March 30, 1983. Discretionary Review Refused April 16, 1983.


PRIOR HISTORY: From County Criminal Court #2 of Tarrant County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants challenged their convictions from the County Criminal Court Number 2 of Tarrant County (Texas) for unlawfully practicing dentistry by making impressions for the purpose of constructing dentures and partial dentures.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, husband and wife, were convicted of unlawfully practicing dentistry by making impression of mouths for the purpose of constructing dentures and partial dentures. Appellant husband challenged his conviction on the grounds that his general occupation as a dental assistant, who worked on inert material only, was a defense to the charges that he took impressions inside the human mouth. The court overruled appellant husband's ground of error because the assertion raised no defense issue in evidence. Appellant wife challenged her conviction on the ground that the information on which she was charged was fatally defective. The court found that the information was fatally defective because it omitted an essential element of the offense. The court affirmed appellant husband convictions, and reversed and remanded one the informations against appellant wife and reversed and dismissed the defective information.


OUTCOME: Appellant husband's conviction was affirmed. One of the informations against appellant wife was reversed and dismissed because it was defective and the other information was reversed and remanded for a new information because the sentence assessed by the jury was predicated upon a finding of guilt on both informations.

 

1588 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Hays Consol. Independent School Dist. v. Valero Transmission Co.


No. 13,450


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


645 S.W.2d 542; 1982 Tex. App. LEXIS 5422



November 24, 1982 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied February 9, 1983.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the District Court of Hays County, 22nd Judicial District.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant school district sought review of a judgment of the 22nd District Court of Hays County (Texas), which declared invalid appellant's tax scheme and taxation of appellee taxpayer, a pipeline company, and ordered that appellant take nothing on its complaint for unpaid taxes. Appellant contended that the court erred in finding in appellee's favor because it entered only a general denial to the complaint, and thus did not establish its case.


OVERVIEW: Appellant school district sought to recover unpaid taxes on an interest in real estate owned by appellee taxpayer, a pipeline company. Appellee filed a general denial to the complaint. At trial, appellee presented evidence that the valuation on its properties for the tax year was grossly in excess of the fair market and assessed values, in that the valuation was at a considerably higher percentage of market value than farmland within the district. The trial court found the assessment discriminatory and invalid, and awarded appellant nothing on its complaint. Appellant challenged the judgment, asserting that the trial court erred because appellee had failed to comply with the requirements of pleading set forth in Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 7329, which provides the affirmative defenses available to a taxpayer. On appeal, the court agreed with appellant's assertions. The court concluded that because appellee had failed to affirmatively plead its defenses, the trial court could not enter judgment on the issues raised at trial. The court reversed the judgment and remanded the cause for entry of judgment in the amount of the delinquent taxes plus interest and penalties.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment, holding that the trial court erred in declaring the district's assessed valuation void and invalid on the basis that it was grossly in excess of that allowed by law or the basis that it resulted from a discriminatory scheme adopted by appellant school district. There being no pleading to support these affirmative defenses, and no trial by consent in that respect, the trial court could not enter judgment thereon.

 

1589 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Crisp v. State


Nos. 3-82-072-CR, 3-82-073-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


643 S.W.2d 487; 1982 Tex. App. LEXIS 5424



November 24, 1982 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Discretionary Review Granted January 12, 1983.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF FAYETTE COUNTY, 155TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sought review of an order from the District Court of Fayette County, 155th Judicial District (Texas), which denied their pre-conviction application for writ of habeas corpus. Appellants contended that a bill amending the Texas Controlled Substances Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15 (1982), violated Tex. Const. Ann. art. III, § 35 (1955).


OVERVIEW: Appellants, jointly indicted for possession of marijuana, filed a pre-conviction application for writ of habeas corpus. They contended that the caption to a bill amending the Controlled Substances Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15 (1982), violated Tex. Const. art. III, § 35 (1955). The lower court denied the writ. The court affirmed. The court agreed that the caption of the bill was unconstitutionally vague because it failed to give adequate notice of the substantive changes in state law contained in the body of the bill. The court determined that appellants were not entitled to be discharged from the indictment. The court found that the indictment stated an offense under the pre-amendment version of the act, which remained in full force and effect, as if the amendment had never existed. Appellants were ordered to remain in custody and to stand trial under the original law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order, which denied a pre-conviction application for writ of habeas corpus. The court held that the caption to a bill amending the act under which appellants were jointly indicted for possession of marijuana was unconstitutionally vague. Because the indictment stated an offense under the pre-amendment version of the law, which remained in full force and effect, appellants were ordered to stand trial.

 

1590 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Ex parte Muniz


No. B14-82-565-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


655 S.W.2d 224; 1982 Tex. App. LEXIS 5494



November 24, 1982 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Discretionary Review Granted March 3, 1983.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 228th District Court of Harris County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Applicant sought review of the decision of the 228th District Court of Harris County (Texas), which denied his application for a writ of habeas corpus following his indictment for the possession of cocaine, a named substance in penalty group one of the Controlled Substances Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15 (1982).


OVERVIEW: Applicant was in custody following his indictment for the possession of cocaine, a named substance in penalty group one of the Controlled Substances Act (Act), Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15 (1982). The trial court denied his application for a writ of habeas corpus. Applicant contended that the indictment was void because it was based upon an amendment to the Act, which was void because of an unconstitutionally vague title. Without determining whether the amendment was void, the court affirmed the trial court's decision because it found that the Act itself was valid, and the indictment was also based on the Act because cocaine was a controlled substance named in the Act prior to the amendment. Thus, the court concluded that it had no jurisdiction to grant relief because applicant was indicted under a valid statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of applicant's request for a writ of habeas corpus because it found that applicant was indicted under a valid statute, and the court, therefore, had no jurisdiction to grant relief.

 

1591 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Perry v. Merritte


No. C3026


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


643 S.W.2d 496; 1982 Tex. App. LEXIS 5642



November 24, 1982 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother sought review of a judgment of a Texas district court, which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee alleged father, finding that appellant's action to establish paternity and for child support was barred by the four-year limitation statute, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 5529 (1958).


OVERVIEW: After the trial court granted summary judgment in favor of appellee alleged father and found that appellant mother's paternity and child support action was barred by the four-year limitation statute, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 5529 (1958), appellant sought review. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded, holding that the four-year statute of limitations under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 5535 (1982-1983) applied and was tolled during the minority of the child, because the child was born before the effective date of the one-year statute of limitations, contained in Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 13.01, and it was not applied retroactively. Further, it was not illogical and a violation of the Equal Protection Clause of U.S. Const. amend. XIV to toll during minority the four-year limitations statute as to common law paternity actions, but not toll the operation of § 13.01 as to statutory actions of minors born after September 1, 1975, because the intention of the legislature in passing § 13.01 and amending it in 1981 could not affect the interpretation of an earlier tolling statute which was not amended.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the grant of summary judgment in favor of appellee alleged father in appellant's mother's action for paternity and child support, holding that the four-year limitations statute applied and was tolled during the minority of the child, because the child was born before the effective date of the one-year statute of limitations.

 

1592 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Ned v. State


No. 12-81-0096-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Twelfth District, Tyler


644 S.W.2d 859; 1982 Tex. App. LEXIS 5368



November 18, 1982 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Mandate Issued January 18, 1983.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 184th District Court of Harris County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction by the 184th District Court of Harris County, Texas, of aggravated robbery.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of aggravated robbery. Appellant alleged that the trial court erred by overruling his motion for mistrial or failing to quash the jury panel because of the discriminatory use of peremptory challenges by the state. The court affirmed appellant's conviction, finding no systematic exclusion. The court held that appellant's contention that the trial court erred in overruling his objection to continuous prejudicial remarks and arguments of state's counsel was multifarious and violated Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann, art. 40.09, § 9 (1982). Appellant claimed error in permitting the state's witness to bolster his identification testimony by testimony of a pre-trial line-up identification, but the court held that a witness who had identified appellant at the trial could also testify that he identified appellant at a line-up. The court held that appellant did not object to what he claimed was an unqualified witness, so his objection was waived. The court held that the state's opening statement was proper and that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in permitting the prosecuting attorney to inquire whether members of the jury panel had been victims of a crime.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for aggravated robbery because there was no systematic exclusion of jury members by the state, the state's witness was permitted to bolster his identification testimony by testimony of a pre-trial line-up identification, and the trial court did not abuse its discretion in permitting the prosecuting attorney to inquire whether members of the jury panel had been victims of a crime.

 

1593 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Bass v. State


No. 09-82-091 CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Ninth District, Beaumont


666 S.W.2d 113; 1982 Tex. App. LEXIS 5664



November 3, 1982 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Discretionary Review Granted January 12, 1983.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Jefferson County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the decision of the district court of Jefferson County (Texas), which convicted him of intentionally and knowingly possessing marihuana in a usable quantity of under two ounces. Appellant contended that possession of marihuana was no longer a crime because Tex H.B. 730 rendered the Texas Controlled Substances Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15 (1976), unconstitutional pursuant to Tex. Const. art. III, § 36.


OVERVIEW: Following appellant's conviction for intentionally and knowingly possessing marihuana in a usable quantity of under two ounces, appellant challenged the trial court's decision. The court affirmed holding that Tex. H.B. 730 complied with the requirements of Tex. Const. art. III, § 36. When the "reasonable caption reader" looked at H.B. 730, he was put upon notice that it was designed to accomplish two changes in the Texas Controlled Substances Act: the changes related to the offenses and to the criminal penalties. Further, the "reasonable caption reader" knew that there was but one "Texas Controlled Substances Act," the title to Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15, where marihuana was specifically mentioned as one of the controlled substances. Therefore, the court held that Tex. House Bill 730, when examined closely, did pass "constitutional muster."


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction holding that Tex. H.B. 730 provided sufficient notice under the constitution that it was amending the Texas Controlled Substances Act by referring to the Act by its title.

 

1594 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Hall v. State


No. 01-81-0211-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


646 S.W.2d 489; 1982 Tex. App. LEXIS 5328



October 28, 1982 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from County Criminal Court At Law No. 8 of Harris County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment of the County Criminal Court At Law No. 8 of Harris County (Texas) convicting him of possession with intent to promote an obscene device, namely, 29 dildos.


OVERVIEW: The court reversed appellant's conviction for possession with intent to promote an obscene device pursuant to Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 43.21, namely, 29 dildos. The court overruled all of appellant's grounds of error attacking the constitutionality of § 43.21. The court found that without the presumptions created by Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 43.23 (e) and (f) there was sufficient evidence to convict appellant under the valid sections of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 43.23. However, the trial court's charge on the effect of § 43.23(e) and (f) constituted reversible error. Sections 43.23(e) and (f) were facially unconstitutional as in violation of U.S. Const. amends. I, V, and XIV. Accordingly, the judgment of the trial court was reversed and the case was remanded.


OUTCOME: The court reversed a judgment finding appellant guilty of possession with intent to promote an obscene device because the trial court's jury charge was based on the effect of two facially unconstitutional subsections of the obscenity statute. The court remanded the case.

 

1595 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Sanders v. State


No. 01-81-0276-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


649 S.W.2d 59; 1982 Tex. App. LEXIS 5283



October 14, 1982 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the County Court of Criminal Law No. 7.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his commercially exhibiting obscene material conviction under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 43.23(c)(1) in favor of appellee state in County Court of Criminal Law No. 7 (Texas).


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought review of conviction for commercial exhibition of obscene material under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 43.23(c)(1), in favor of appellee state, based on several challenges to the constitutionality of the statute as applied to his sale of tickets for, and projection of, an adult film. The court reversed and remanded, explaining because the statute attempted to hold obscenity defendants to the community norm of proper behavior and taste as opposed to the permissible minimum standard of conduct the community was willing to tolerate, the portion of the statute allowing the accused's conduct to be judged on community standards of "decency" was unconstitutional and had to be struck. The court determined the remainder of the statute was complete within itself and capable of being executed in accordance with legislative intent independently of the rejected portion. The court determined reversal and remand was required because the lower court was assumed to have determined the issues of patently offensive and appeal to prurient interests by use of the perspective of the average person and applying contemporary standards of decency instead of the required "tolerance" standard.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded appellant's conviction for commercial exhibition of obscene materials because portion of statute permitting conviction upon standard of decency determined by community norms of proper behavior as opposed to minimum standards of conduct tolerable was unconstitutional and remand for application of the tolerance standard was mandated.

 

1596 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Trickey v. Trickey


No. 2-82-010-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Second District, Fort Worth


642 S.W.2d 47; 1982 Tex. App. LEXIS 5299



October 14, 1982 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied December 2, 1982.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the District Court of Tarrant County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant wife sought review from a judgment of the District Court of Tarrant County (Texas) granting appellee husband a no fault divorce under Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 3.01 (1970).


OVERVIEW: Appellee husband was granted a no fault divorce from appellant wife under Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 3.01 (1970). The trial court found that the marriage had become insupportable because of a conflict in personalities that destroyed the relationship of the parties and that there was no reasonable expectation of reconciliation. The trial court also concluded that § 3.01 was applicable to the case, regardless of the fact that the parties were married before that statute was passed, and that the statute did not violate either the federal of state constitutions. Appellant challenged the judgment on the ground that a Christian marriage performed in church could not be severed by the government or state. The court affirmed the judgment below, holding that the no fault divorce law was the law of the state and had to be followed and that the law was not unconstitutional as applied to a Christian marriage performed in church. Accordingly, the trial court did not err in granting appellee a no fault divorce.


OUTCOME: The judgment granting appellee husband a no fault divorce was affirmed. The no fault divorce law was the law of the state and was not unconstitutional as applied to a Christian marriage performed in a church.

 

1597 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Rogers v. State


No. 05-81-00748-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


641 S.W.2d 404; 1982 Tex. App. LEXIS 5274



September 29, 1982 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From a County Court of Dallas County, Texas.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment of conviction from a County Court, Dallas County (Texas), for the offense of driving with a suspended driver's license pursuant to Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6701h (1977), asserting constructional and constitutional infirmities in the presumption of notice and the erroneous admission of exhibits not qualified as business records.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of driving with a suspended driver's license pursuant to Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6701h (1977) and sought review, challenging the presumption of notice in Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6701h § 31 and related jury charge and urging error in the admission into evidence of certain records of the Department of Public Safety (department) and a private employer as not shown to be business or public records. The court affirmed, ruling that the notice of license suspension sent to appellant pursuant to § 31 conveyed the present fact of license suspension with a postponed effective date. Thus, the presumption of notice defined in § 31 applied and the court had not erred in so charging the jury. The statute satisfied fundamental fairness because the presumption arose from the common experience of mailing letters and mailing and receipt were reasonably related. The records, which had been made in the regular course of the department's business, were admissible as official records. An employment application was merely cumulative of appellant's withholding exemption certificate, which was an admission of the matters it contained.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for driving with a suspended license because the statutory presumption of notice was constitutional and safety department records were properly admitted as official records.

 

1598 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Tisdale v. State


No. 04-81-00181-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourth District, San Antonio


640 S.W.2d 409; 1982 Tex. App. LEXIS 5160



September 22, 1982 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Discretionary Review Refused.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Bexar County


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision of the District Court of Bexar County (Texas), which convicted her of prostitution.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of prostitution. On appeal, she argued that Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 43.02(a)(1) was unconstitutional because it deprived individuals of their right to privacy. However, the court found that the enactment of the statute was to protect the health, safety and welfare of the population at large, and was clearly within the province and discretion of the legislature. Defendant also argued the language of § 43.02(a)(1) was unconstitutionally overbroad, because adults engaged in consensual sex could be construed as engaging in prostitution. However, the court found no cases of convictions other than those in which the Texas courts had confined prosecution and conviction to situations involving commercial sex, that is an offer or agreement or actual act of sexual conduct for a fee. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.


OUTCOME: Trial court's decision that convicted defendant of prostitution was affirmed. Defendant's challenges to the constitutionality of the pertinent statute were without merit.

 

1599 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Aranda v. State


No. 04-81-00075-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourth District, San Antonio


640 S.W.2d 766; 1982 Tex. App. LEXIS 5162



September 22, 1982 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied October 19, 1982


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Webb County


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of a trial court in Webb County (Texas), which convicted him under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 19.03(a)(1) (1974) of capital murder after the jury answered negatively to special issue number two pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.071 (1981) and the trial court assessed punishment at life imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of capital murder, and on appeal he contended that his motion to quash the indictment should have been granted because an element of the offense was not correctly alleged. He further contended that the indictment was unconstitutionally vague since it did not specify facts denoting "official duty" of the deceased officer. The court rejected defendant's contentions, finding the indictment sufficiently charged defendant with shooting a peace officer in the lawful discharge of an official duty, knowing at the time that the officer was a police officer. The indictment was not void for vagueness and defendant had notice of the offense charged against him. The court held that a capital murder indictment need not allege the special issues of Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.071. The court also found the officer had specific and articulable facts which, with rational inferences, were sufficient to permit him to stop the vehicle and detain its occupants. Once the vehicle was stopped, gunshots erupted from within, causing the officer's death. The refusal to grant a motion for continuance was not error where defendant was not diligent in obtaining witnesses.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that entering defendant's conviction for capital murder. The court held that the indictment did not have to allege the special issues in order to sufficiently charge defendant.

 

1600 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Acosta v. State


No. 04-81-00327-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourth District, San Antonio


640 S.W.2d 381; 1982 Tex. App. LEXIS 5122



September 8, 1982 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Karnes County


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of a district court in Karnes County (Texas), which revoked his probation for the offense of possession of marijuana in an amount over four ounces, a felony.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of the offense of possession of marijuana in an amount over four ounces, a felony. Defendant was given probation, and one of the conditions was that he would not be convicted of any offense. The state alleged he had committed three offenses, all possession of marijuana of less than two ounces, during his probationary period, and the trial court ordered his probation revoked. On appeal, defendant asserted that he had a constitutional right to subpoena and question the members of the grand jury which indicted him for the primary offense, the subject of the revocation hearing. The court affirmed the order of revocation. The court held defendant's challenge of the grand jury evidence was time-barred, and should have been done before trial. The court held that there was no unlawful seizure by the police of contraband dumped from the automobile by defendant and probable cause existed at that point to search him, so the evidence was admissible. The court also found that the charging instrument sufficiently apprised defendant of the required elements of the offense to which he pled guilty, so he had notice.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order revoking defendant's probation because any challenge to the grand jury evidence was time-barred, there was no unlawful seizure of marihuana he dumped from his automobile, and probable cause existed to search him, so the evidence was admissible. The court also found defendant had proper notice because the charging instrument sufficiently apprised him of the required elements of the offense to which he pled guilty.
